Two Works on Prophethood and Miracles
Lists two of al-Baqillani's works and quotes a linguistic point on 'nabi'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the subjects of two of al-Baqillani's works and his discussion on the linguistic derivation of the word 'nabi'.

Core Idea
Baqillani wrote distinct works to defend prophethood and clarify miracles.

In this lesson, you will learn about two important works by Imam al-Baqillani: Naqd al-Naqd, a refutation of a critique, and al-Farq bayn Mu'jizat al-Nabiyyin wa Karamat al-Salihin, which distinguishes prophetic miracles from saintly wonders. The passage also includes a quote from the latter explaining the meaning of 'nabi' as derived from 'inba'' (announcement).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the two book titles and the quote.
The passage is bibliographic; focus on the content of the second work.
2
Identify the two works
Find the names of the two books: Naqd al-Naqd and al-Farq bayn Mu'jizat al-Nabiyyin wa Karamat al-Salihin. Understand that the first is a refutation, the second a distinction.
Naqd al-Naqd is a refutation of a previous critical work.
3
Analyze the quote from al-Farq
Read the quote: it discusses the derivation of the word 'nabi' from 'inba'' (announcement). Consider why this linguistic point matters for theology.
This shows Baqillani's engagement with both philology and theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب «نقض «النقض» ذكره أبو المظفر الاسفراييني في التبصير ص .۱۹۳
۹ - كتاب الفرق بين معجزات النبيين و كــرامــات الصالحين ذكره في هداية المسترشدين حيث يقول: «وقد بينا في كتاب الفرق بين معجزات النبيين وكرامات الصالحين معنى وصف النبي أنه نبي وأن من الناس من قال : إنه مشتق ومأخوذ من الإنباء عن الأشياء والإخبار عن عزّ وجلّ . الله
The book 'Naqd al-Naqd' mentioned by Abu al-Muzaffar al-Isfarayini in al-Tabsir p. 193. 9 - The book 'al-Farq bayn Mu'jizat al-Nabiyyin wa Karamat al-Salihin' mentioned in Hidayat al-Mustarshidin where he says: 'And we have explained in the book al-Farq bayn Mu'jizat al-Nabiyyin wa Karamat al-Salihin the meaning of describing a prophet that he is a prophet, and that among people are those who say: it is derived and taken from al-inba' (announcement) of things and informing about God, mighty and majestic.' God.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage lists two more of Baqillani's works. The first, 'Naqd al-Naqd', is a refutation of a previous critical work, as indicated by its title (literally 'The Refutation of the Refutation'). It is mentioned by al-Isfarayini. The second, 'al-Farq bayn Mu'jizat al-Nabiyyin wa Karamat al-Salihin' (The Difference between the Miracles of Prophets and the Wonders of the Righteous), is referenced in Baqillani's own 'Hidayat al-Mustarshidin'. A quote explains that in that book Baqillani discussed the meaning of a prophet being a prophet, noting that some derive the term 'nabi' from 'inba'' (announcement) meaning one who announces things and informs about God. This shows Baqillani's engagement with the linguistic and theological definition of prophethood, as well as the distinction between prophetic miracles and saintly miracles (karamat).

Key Terms
نقض النقض
الفرق بين معجزات النبيين وكرامات الصالحين
النبي
الإنباء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the quote from al-Farq, from what word is 'nabi' derived?
A) nubuwwa (highness)
B) inba' (announcement)
C) nabwah (rise)
D) nabiyy (water spring)

Key Takeaway
Al-Baqillani wrote works defending prophethood and clarifying the derivation of the term 'nabi' from 'inba'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear the word 'prophet', do you primarily think of a title or a message? The lesson shows it is derived from 'announcement'. What announcements from the Prophets have you actually internalized and acted upon today?
?
Al-Baqillani wrote separate works to clarify and defend prophethood. When you encounter criticisms of prophethood, do you seek out scholarly defenses or rely on vague feelings? What is one specific doubt about prophethood that you need to address with a reliable source?

Miracles as Testimony and the Hierarchy of Proofs
Baqillani discusses miracles as testimony and enumerates the types of proofs with their hierarchy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how miracles function as testimony for prophethood and how Baqillani categorizes rational and scriptural proofs, with the latter being subordinate to the former.

Core Idea
Miracles testify to prophethood, and all scriptural proofs rest on rational foundations.

Imam al-Baqillani begins this passage with a subtle point about linguistic testimony, then draws a parallel to miracles as a form of testimony for a prophet's truthfulness. He proceeds to enumerate the accepted sources of evidence in Islamic theology—the Book, Sunnah, consensus, and analogical reasoning—and clarifies that while these scriptural proofs are valuable, they are ultimately branches of the more fundamental rational proofs. This sets the methodological framework for understanding how proofs are evaluated in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Understand the analogy between testimony and miracles
Read how Baqillani compares miracles to testimony (شهادة). Notice that he previously discussed linguistic testimony, and now extends that concept to miracles as a witness to a prophet's truthfulness.
The fragment at the start refers to a prior discussion about the reliability of testimony based on language.
2
Identify the types of evidence mentioned
Baqillani lists the sources of evidence: rational propositions, the Book, Sunnah, consensus, analogical reasoning, and independent reasoning. Make a mental list of these categories.
These are the standard sources in Sunni usul al-fiqh.
3
Grasp the hierarchy between rational and scriptural proofs
Notice the phrase 'فرعاً لأدلة العقول' (branches of the proofs of intellect). This indicates that scriptural proofs are subordinate to rational ones. Reflect on why this matters for theological methodology.
This hierarchy is a key principle in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ناراً أو إنساناً، وهو من أهل لُغَتِنا، يقصد إلى إفهامنا أنه ما شاهد إلا مثل ما سُمّي بحضرتنا ناراً أو إنساناً، لا نحمل بعض ذلك على بعض، لكن بموجب الاسم وموضوع اللغة ووجوب استعمال الكلام على ما استعملوه ووضعوه حيث وضعوه. خبر عن صدقه وقد يُسْتَدَلُ بالمعجزة على صدق من ظهرت على يده لأنها تجرى مجرى الشهادة له، ويُستدل على صدق المُخبر الذي أخبر عنه النبي صلى الله عليه أنه لا يكذب وكذلك يستدل بخبر من صاحب المعجزة على صدق من أخبر عنه أنه لا يكذب. وقد يُسْتَدّل أيضاً على بعض القضايا العقلية وعلى الأحكام الشرعية بالكتاب والسنة وإجماع الأمة والقياس الشرعي المُنتزع من الأصول المنطوق بها وما جرى مجرى القياس على العلة من ضرب الاجتهاد الذي يسوغ الحكم بمثله من الشرع على مذهب القايسين، فكل هذه الأدلة السمعية جارية في الكشف عن صحة القياس مجرى ما قدمنا ذكره من الأحكام العقلية، وإن كان فرعاً لأدلة العقول وقضاياها، وفيما أومأنا إليه من وجوه الاستدلال كفاية وتنبيه على ما أضربنا عن ذكره.
...fire or a human being, and he is from among the speakers of our language, intending to inform us that he only witnessed something like what is called in our presence fire or a human being, we do not take some of that for others, but according to the name and the subject of the language and the necessity of using speech as they used it and placed it where they placed it. A report about his truthfulness. And the miracle is used as evidence for the truthfulness of the one upon whose hand it appears, because it runs in the course of testimony for him, and evidence is sought for the truthfulness of the informer who informed about the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he does not lie, and likewise evidence is sought from the report of the one who possesses the miracle for the truthfulness of the one about whom he informed that he does not lie. And evidence is also sought by means of the Book, the Sunnah, the consensus of the community, and the analogical reasoning derived from the articulated principles, regarding some rational propositions and legal rulings, and anything that runs in the course of analogy based on the cause from the type of independent reasoning whose like is permitted by the Law according to the school of the analogists. So all these scriptural evidences proceed in uncovering the correctness of analogy in the same manner as what we previously mentioned of rational rulings, even though they are branches of the proofs of intellect and its propositions. And in what we have alluded to of the aspects of inference, there is sufficiency and an alert to what we have omitted.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage begins with an apparently fragmentary remark about linguistic convention: using names according to their conventional placement. Then it moves to miracles as evidence for a prophet's truthfulness, comparing them to testimony. The author then lists the types of evidence: rational propositions and scriptural sources (Book, Sunnah, consensus, analogical reasoning). He notes that scriptural proofs are subordinate to rational proofs. The passage concludes that the discussion suffices as an indication of what has been omitted.

Key Terms
المعجزة
الشهادة
الأدلة السمعية
القياس
الاجتهاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That miracles are the only proof of prophethood.
Correction: Baqillani shows that miracles are one type of testimony among many, and that all scriptural proofs depend on rational proofs.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what is the relationship between scriptural evidences and rational proofs?
A) Scriptural proofs are independent of rational proofs.
B) Scriptural proofs are branches of rational proofs.
C) Rational proofs are branches of scriptural proofs.
D) There is no relationship.

Key Takeaway
Miracles are a form of testimony for prophethood, and all scriptural proofs are ultimately branches of rational proofs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you accept the Qur'an or Sunnah as evidence, do you actively engage your intellect as the foundation, or do you treat them as self-sufficient? What would change if you consciously saw them as branches of rational proof?
?
The passage equates a miracle to testimony. Whose testimony do you rely on for your faith—are you simply trusting a chain of witnesses, or have you rationally verified the credibility of that testimony? Which is more real for you?
?
Are there areas of your religious practice where you follow analogy or consensus without personally grounding them in rational conviction? Commit to examining one such ruling this week and trace its rational basis.

Baqillani's Refutation of Astrologers' Epistemological Claims
Baqillani refutes astrologers' three knowledge sources and offers an alternative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes the three possible sources of knowledge that astrologers might claim and presents an alternative causal explanation grounded in observable earthly phenomena.

Core Idea
Astrologers' claims fail on transmission, observation, and inference.

Baqillani tackles astrologers who claim to know the future by the stars. He systematically examines every possible basis for their knowledge—reports, direct observation, and reasoning—and shows each is insufficient. He then offers a more plausible cause-and-effect relationship grounded in observable earthly phenomena.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the three refutations and the alternative explanation.
2
Examine the refutation of transmission
Baqillani addresses the astrologers' claim of transmitted knowledge. He argues that the prophets, who have proofs of truthfulness, contradict the astrologers, so they are more deserving of belief.
This shows the priority of prophetic reports over astrological claims.
3
Examine the refutation of sensory observation and inference
Baqillani argues that astrologers did not observe the ancient past or the management of the stars. He also says that nothing in their observations provides evidence for their claims about the stars' management or the eternity of natures.
He points out that inference from observed phenomena does not support astrology.
4
Consider the alternative explanation
Baqillani proposes that changes on earth (trees, seas, waters, etc.) cause changes in the stars, not vice versa. This is closer to direct observation and more plausible.
This counters the astrological causality with a simpler, observable alternative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قال : يقال لهم بم عرفتم أنه كذلك؟ فإن ادعوا السمع فيه عورضوا بالسمع الذي ورد ممن فيهم حجج الصدق، فهم أحق أن يصدقوا وهم الرسل. وإن ادعوا العيان والحس أكذبهم علمهم بأنفسهم أنهم لا يذكرون قدمهم ولا شهدوا تدبير النجوم والطائع. وإن رجعوا إلى الاستدلال بما عاينوا فليس في شيء مما عاينوا دليل تدبير النجوم ولا قدم الطبائع وتولد العالم من امتزاجها، بل لو قلب عليهم القول كان أقرب إلى الوجود وأحق في الاستدلال . ثم يقال: إن اضطراب الفلك وتحرك النجوم وتقلبها على أحوال الاجتماع والتفرق يكون بتقلب أحوال الأرضين وما فيها من أنواع الأشجار والبحار والمياه، وجوهر التفرق التي يعلو نجارها، أو هي بجوهرها كالنيران والجواهر الحقيقية وبها ينقلب أمر النجوم وما ذكر فهذا أحق، إذ هو أقرب إلى العين وأولى أن يكون دليلاً لما غاب عنا، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
Then he said: 'It is said to them: How do you know that it is so? If they claim [authoritative] transmission regarding it, they are countered by the transmission that came from those in whom are the proofs of truthfulness; they are more deserving of being believed, and they are the messengers. And if they claim direct observation and sense, their own knowledge belies them, that they do not remember their [own] antiquity nor have they witnessed the management of the stars and the [?]. And if they resort to inference from what they have observed, there is in nothing of what they have observed any proof of the management of the stars, nor of the eternity of natures and the generation of the world from their mixture. Rather, if the argument were turned against them, it would be nearer to existence and more deserving in inference. Then it is said: Indeed, the disturbance of the celestial sphere, the movement of the stars, and their revolution over states of conjunction and separation occur through the revolution of the states of the earths and what is in them of types of trees, seas, and waters, and the substance of separation whose carpenter rises, or they are by their substance like fires and true substances, and by them the affair of the stars and what is mentioned is reversed. So this is more deserving, since it is nearer to the eye and more appropriate to be a proof for what is hidden from us. And there is no power except through Allah.'
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the possible sources of knowledge that astrologers might claim. Baqillani addresses three potential sources: (1) transmitted reports (sam'), (2) direct observation/sense (al-'iyan wa al-hiss), and (3) inference (istidlal) from observed phenomena. Against transmitted reports, he says that the reports from the prophets (who are truthful) contradict the astrologers, so the prophets should be believed instead. Against sensory observation, he points out that astrologers themselves do not remember their own past nor have they witnessed the management of the stars, so their sensory claims are false. Against inference from what they observe, he argues that there is nothing observed that proves the stars' management or the eternity of natures. He then offers an alternative: if the argument were turned around, it would be more plausible to say that changes on earth (trees, seas, waters, etc.) cause changes in the stars, rather than vice versa, because that is closer to direct observation. He concludes by affirming reliance on God.

Key Terms
سمع
عيان
حس
استدلال
رسل
طابع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Astrologers have valid empirical evidence for their predictions.
Correction: Baqillani shows that their observations do not support their claims; there is no observed proof of the stars' management or the eternity of natures.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why are the prophets more deserving of belief than astrologers?
A) Because prophets have more followers.
B) Because prophets have proofs of truthfulness.
C) Because prophets are wealthy.
D) Because prophets lived long ago.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani demonstrates that astrologers lack any valid source of knowledge, while the messengers provide the true guidance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you seek knowledge about your future or decisions, do you rely more on observable patterns or on divine revelation? Which source do you trust more, and why?
?
Baqillani shows that even our own observation can be limited. In what areas of your life are you assuming you 'see' the truth, when in fact you may be blind to Allah's comprehensive management?
?
If the prophets are more deserving of belief than any other claimant, have you truly submitted your uncertainties to the Qur'an and Sunnah? What current doubts or questions are you still trying to answer from other sources?

Third Argument: Religious Practices Are Rationally Ugly
The Barāhima argue that religious practices contradict rational good taste.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Barāhima's claim that religious practices are rationally ugly and see the specific examples they cite to support their rejection of prophethood.

Core Idea
The Barāhima argue that a wise God would not command irrational acts.

The Barāhima, a group of Indian atheists, challenge the validity of prophethood by arguing that the practices prescribed by revealed religions contradict rational judgment. They claim that a wise Creator would never command actions that reason deems ugly. In this passage, they enumerate several Islamic rituals to support their argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the flow of the argument.
Pay attention to the list of practices they cite.
2
Identify the premise
Find the statement about the wise Maker and the claim that He does not command ugly acts. This is the logical foundation of their objection.
Consider why they assume a wise Maker would avoid such commands.
3
List the 'ugly' practices
Go through each practice they list (facing a house, circumambulation, etc.) and ask: In what sense might these be considered rationally ugly?
This step helps you see the argument from their perspective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها أن قال: قد دل العقل على أن للعالم صانعاً حكيماً، والحكيم لا يتعبد الخلق بما يقبح في عقولهم وقد ردت أصحاب الشرائع بمستقبحات من حيث العقل، من التوجه إلى البيت مخصوص في العبادة والطواف حوله والسعي ورمي الحجار والإحرام، والتلبية، وتقبيل الحجر الأصم وكذلك ذبح الحيوان وتحريم ما يمكن أن يكون غذاء الإنسان وتحليل ما ينقص من بنيته، وغير ذلك، وكل هذه الأمور مخالفة لقضايا العقول.
And among them is that he said: Reason has indicated that the world has a wise Maker, and the wise does not obligate the creation with what is ugly in their minds. And the adherents of revealed laws have come with things that are rationally considered ugly, such as facing a specific house in worship, circumambulating it, running, throwing stones, entering iḥrām, reciting talbiya, kissing the black stone, and likewise slaughtering animals, prohibiting what could be human food, and permitting what harms the body, and other things. All these matters contradict the judgments of reason.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage presents the third argument: religious practices are irrational and ugly. The Barāhima claim that reason proves a wise Creator, and a wise being would not command actions that reason deems ugly (qabīḥ). They then list examples from Islamic practice: facing the Ka'ba in prayer, circumambulation, Sa'y, throwing stones (Ramy), entering iḥrām, talbiya, kissing the Black Stone, animal sacrifice, prohibiting certain foods, and permitting harmful things. All these, they argue, conflict with rational judgment, so a wise God would not command them, and therefore these religions cannot be from God.

Key Terms
حكيم (wise)
يقبح (ugly/repugnant)
مستقبحات (things deemed ugly)
شرائع (revealed laws)
عبادات (acts of worship)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That all religious practices must be rationally self-evident or beneficial in a worldly sense.
Correction: This argument ignores that rational judgments of good and bad may be overridden by divine command or that practices have hidden wisdoms unknown to human reason.

Checkpoint
Which of the following practices do the Barāhima cite as rationally ugly?
A) Fasting and prayer
B) Pilgrimage rites like circumambulation and throwing stones
C) Giving charity and helping the poor
D) Studying and teaching

Key Takeaway
The Barāhima reject prophethood by asserting that religious rites are irrational, but this ignores the possibility of divine wisdom beyond human reason.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform acts of worship like tawaf or sa'i, have you ever felt they are pointless or irrational? How does this passage reveal the Barāhima's error, and what does that mean for your own heart's submission to Allah's commands?
?
Are there any religious practices that you personally struggle to understand or find 'ugly' in your mind? What would it take for you to accept them as from a wise God despite your rational discomfort?
?
This argument assumes that what is 'ugly' is fixed and known by reason. In what areas of your life do you rely on your own sense of good and bad without consulting revelation? Could that be a form of the Barāhima's error?

The Barāhima's Equality Objection
The Barāhima present their equality objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Barāhima's argument that a human messenger cannot legitimately command others because they are equals.

Core Idea
If all humans are equal, how can one command another?

The Barāhima reject prophethood on the grounds that a messenger is merely a human like everyone else. They argue that giving one person authority over others is the greatest sin unless there is clear proof. In this passage, they present their objection, claiming that following such a person is like being an inanimate object or an animal.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the rhetorical questions and the comparisons used.
The Barāhima compare the follower to a 'جماد' (inanimate object) and 'حيوان' (animal).
2
Identify the core claims
List the claims: (1) the messenger is identical in nature, (2) following him is the greatest sin, (3) no rational distinction exists.
3
Understand the challenge
The Barāhima ask: what proof does the messenger have? If it's a mere claim, any claim would be equal. If it's a miracle, they claim to have countless miracles too.
This sets up the need for a refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها أنه قال : إن أكبر الكبائر في الرسالة اتباع رجل هو مثلك في الصورة والنفس والعقل يأكل مما تأكل ويشرب مما تشرب حتى تكون بالنسبة إليه كجماد يتصرف فيك رفعاً ووضعاً أو كحيوان يصرفك أماماً وخلقاً أو كعبد يتقدم إليك أمراً ونهياً فأي تميز له عليك؟ وأية فضيلة أوجبت استخدامك؟ وما دليله على صدق دعواه ؟ فإن اغترر ثم بمجرد قوله فلا تمييز لقول على قول وإن انحسرتم بحجته ومعجزته فعندنا من خصائص الجواهر والأجسام ما لا يحصى كثيره . فيقال لمن أحال من الله سبحانه إنفاذ رسله إلى خلقه لم قلت ذلك وما دليلك عليه ؟ فإن قال : لعلمه سبحانه بأن الرسول من جنس المرسل إليه وأن جوهرهما واحد وأن تفضيل أحد المتماثلين المتساويين على مثله ونوعه ومن هو بصفته حيف ومحاباة وميل وخروج عن الحكمة وذلك غير جائز على الحكيم، يقال لهم : لم قلتم إن تفضيل الله سبحانه بعض الجنس على بعض ورفع بعضهم إذا كان محاباة للمفضل عليه وجب أن يكون ظلماً وخروجاً عن الحكمة؟ وما أنكرتم أن يكون الله سبحانه ومن المخبرين عن مغيبات الأمور من ساوى خبره قالت لهم رسلهم إن نحن إلا بشر مثلكم ولكن الله يمن على من يشاء من عباده) فإذا اعترفتم بأن للعالم صانعاً وخالقاً وحكيماً ؛ فاعترفوا بأنه أمر وناه وحاكم على خلقه، وله في جميع ما تأتى ونذر، ونعمل ونفكر، حكم وأمر ، وليس كل عقل إنساني على استعداد ما يعقل عنه أمره، ولا كل نفس بشرى بمثابة من يقبل عنه حكمه، بل أوجبت منته ترتيبان في العقول والنفوس، واقتضت قسمته أن يرفع بعضهم فوق بعض درجات ليتخذ بعضهم بعضاً سخرياً ورحمة ربك خير مما يجمعون فرحمة الله الكبرى هي النبوة والرسالة، وذلك خير مما يجمعون بعقولهم المختالة
And among them is that he said: Verily the greatest of sins in prophethood is following a man who is like you in form, soul, and reason; he eats what you eat, drinks what you drink, until you are relative to him like an inanimate object that he manipulates up and down, or like an animal that he drives forward and backward, or like a slave who receives orders and prohibitions from him. So what distinction does he have over you? And what virtue obligated your using him? And what is his proof of the truth of his claim? If you are deceived then by his mere statement, there is no distinction of one statement over another. And if you are convinced by his argument and miracle, then we have from the properties of atoms and bodies a countless number. Then it is said to the one who deemed it impossible from God Most High to send His messengers to His creation: Why did you say that and what is your proof for it? For if he says: Because of His knowledge, Most High, that the messenger is of the same genus as the one to whom he is sent, and their substance is one, and that preferring one of the identical equals over his like, type, and one who is of his description is injustice, partiality, bias, and a departure from wisdom, and that is not permissible for the Wise One. It is said to them: Why did you say that the preference by God Most High of some of the genus over others and raising some of them, if it is partiality for the one preferred, necessarily entails injustice and departure from wisdom? And what prevents you from acknowledging that God Most High is among the informers of unseen matters; the one whose report is equal? Their messengers said to them: 'We are but humans like you, but God bestows favor upon whom He wills of His servants.' So if you acknowledge that the world has a Maker, Creator, and Wise One, then acknowledge that He is Commander and Prohibitor and Ruler over His creation, and He has judgment and command in all that we bring and leave, and we act and think. Not every human reason is prepared to comprehend His command, nor is every human soul in the position to accept His judgment. Rather, His favor necessitated a ranking in intellects and souls, and His division required that He raise some of them above others in degrees, so that they take each other in service. And the mercy of your Lord is better than what they gather. So the greatest mercy of God is prophethood and messengerhood, and that is better than what they gather with their vainglorious minds.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth and most critical argument of the Barāhima against prophethood: the objection that a human messenger cannot be superior to others, and the author's refutation. The Barāhima argue that following a man who is your equal in form, soul, and reason is the greatest sin. They ask: what distinguishes him? If you follow him based on his mere claim, any claim would be equal; if based on a miracle, they claim to have their own miracles from the properties of atoms and bodies. The refutation directly answers: why do you claim that God preferring some humans over others is unfair? It is not necessarily unjust. The author quotes the Quranic verse where prophets say they are only humans but God favors whom He wills. The refutation continues: if you acknowledge a wise Creator, acknowledge that He commands and prohibits. Not all intellects are equal; God has arranged degrees among people. Prophethood is God's greatest mercy, superior to what human minds can gather. The argument defends the possibility and wisdom of prophethood.

Key Terms
كبائر (great sins)
رسالة (prophethood)
تماثل (equality)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What do the Barāhima claim is the 'greatest sin' in prophethood?
A) Denying miracles
B) Following a human who is your equal
C) Disobeying a prophet
D) Claiming prophethood falsely

Key Takeaway
The Barāhima argue that a human messenger cannot command others because he is their equal in nature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed a message because its bearer seemed too ordinary, like you? What does that reveal about your criteria for truth?
?
The Barāhima ask: 'What distinction does he have over you?' How would you answer from the Qur'an and Sunnah? Are you following the Prophet (ﷺ) merely because of culture or because you have a convincing answer to this question?
?
If someone today used the same equality argument to reject the Prophet (ﷺ), what specific evidence from this lesson could you offer? Is your own conviction strong enough to respond without hesitation?

Refuting the Equality Objection
The author refutes the equality argument

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Baqillani refutes the equality objection by appealing to God's wisdom and authority.

Core Idea
God's favor is not injustice; He arranges degrees as He wills.

Imam al-Baqillani responds to the Barāhima's core objection by questioning their assumption that preferring one human over another is necessarily unjust. He argues that since God is the Creator and Ruler, He has the right to choose messengers. Prophethood is God's mercy, not an arbitrary imposition.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation
Notice how the author turns the tables by asking why the Barāhima assume preference is unjust.
The refutation begins with a direct question: 'لم قلت ذلك' (Why did you say that?).
2
Understand the logical challenge
The author challenges the premise that preferring some over others is necessarily injustice or partiality.
He argues that God's actions are not bound by human notions of justice in the same way.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
The author quotes the verse where prophets say they are but humans like others, but God favors whom He wills.
This shows that equality in human nature does not negate God's right to choose.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The author concludes that God has arranged degrees among people, and prophethood is His greatest mercy.
This refutes the idea that prophethood is oppressive.

?

?
When you feel overlooked or less favored compared to others in matters of status, talent, or spiritual gifts, does your heart resent God as if He were being unjust? How can you replace that resentment with the conviction that His mercy is better than anything you could gather?
?
The author says that not every intellect is prepared to comprehend God's command. In what area of your life are you relying on your own understanding rather than humbly accepting that God's judgment may be beyond your grasp? Will you surrender that area to Him today?

Refutation of the Barahima: Preference is Not Injustice
Baqillani refutes the Barahima's analogy from human favoritism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes the Barahima's argument that God's preference among equals would be unjust, by showing that preference in human affairs is not always foolish.

Core Idea
Preference among equals is not automatically injustice — context and wisdom matter.

The Barahima argued that if God preferred some prophets over others, that would be like a human favoring one equal over another, which is foolish. Baqillani challenges this analogy by examining whether all preference among humans is indeed foolish. He provides everyday examples where such preference is permissible and even wise.

Guided Path
1
Read the Barahima's objection
Start by reading the objection: they claim that preferring one of two equals is foolishness (safah) in human experience, so it must apply to God.
This objection is the starting point of the passage.
2
Examine Baqillani's counter-question
Notice that Baqillani does not immediately reject the analogy; instead, he questions the premise: 'Why do you say this is foolishness?'
This is a key dialectical move.
3
Look at the examples given
Baqillani provides examples from everyday life—a master favoring one servant, a person favoring a friend with gifts and honors—to show that such preference can be permissible and wise.
These examples demonstrate that the premise is not universally true.
4
Understand how this refutes the analogy
By showing that human preference is not always foolish, Baqillani undermines the Barahima's analogy, allowing that God's preference can be perfectly wise.
The refutation is complete without affirming that God does prefer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : لأن تفضيل أحد المتجانسين على الآخر في الشاهد سَفَة منـا فوجب القضاء بذلك على القديم تعالى ، قيل لهم : ولم قلتم : إن ذلك سفه ، وما أنكرتم من أنه جائز لنا وصواب في حكمتنا أن نَحْبُو بعض عبيدنا وأصدقائنا والمتصرفين معنا كتصرف غيره بأكثر مما نحبو به غيره ونفضّله بعطاء وتشريف لا يستحقه أكثر مما نحبو به غيره، فلم قلتم إن هذا سفه وقبيح من فعلنا؟
For if they say: Because preferring one of the two homogenous over the other in our observation is foolishness from us, so judgment must be passed accordingly upon the Eternal the Exalted, it is said to them: And why did you say that this is foolishness? And what prevented you from [acknowledging] that it is permissible for us and sound in our wisdom to favor some of our servants and friends and those who act with us like the action of others with more than what we favor others with, and to prefer him with a gift and honor he does not deserve more than what we favor others with? So why did you say that this is foolishness and ugly from our action?
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage continues the refutation by addressing the Barahima's key analogy: they argue that in human affairs (al-shahid), preferring one equal over another is considered foolish (safah), so this must apply to God as well. Baqillani counters by questioning their premise: is it always foolish to prefer one person over another? He gives examples from everyday life—master favoring one servant, a person favoring a friend—where such preference is not considered foolish but rather permissible and wise. Thus the analogy fails. The argument aims to show that the Barahima's assumption of necessary equality among humans is not absolute.

Key Terms
المتجانسين
الشاهد
السفه
القديم
المحاباة
الحكمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Preferring one person over another when they are equal is always unjust and foolish.
Correction: Baqillani shows that such preference can be permissible and wise, as in favoring a loyal servant or friend.

Checkpoint
What example does Baqillani give to show that preference is not always foolish?
A) A judge sentencing a criminal
B) A master favoring one servant over another
C) A king waging war
D) A teacher grading students

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes the Barahima's analogy by demonstrating that human preference is not inherently foolish, thus the objection against God's wisdom fails.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed someone's action as foolish without considering the context or wisdom behind it? How does Baqillani's challenge to the Barahima's assumption expose a potential arrogance in your own judgments? Commit to pausing before labeling something as 'foolish' from your limited perspective.
?
This passage shows that even in human affairs, preference can be wise and good. Where in your own relationships are you tempted to demand 'equal treatment' when in fact God and others might have a deeper wisdom in giving more to someone else? Will you trust that wisdom even when it costs you?
?
The Barahima used an analogy from human experience to limit God. Are there analogies or comparisons you make between God's actions and human actions that actually diminish His sovereignty? Today, identify one such comparison and replace it with humble acknowledgment that 'He is not questioned about what He does' (Quran 21:23). Make a concrete resolution to guard your tongue and heart.

Prophethood

Prophets' merit and the justification of divine favor
Baqillani argues that God's favoring of prophets is based on their merit, not arbitrary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani argues that prophethood is granted based on merit, specifically through an analogy that counters the objection of arbitrary divine favor.

Core Idea
Prophethood is earned through righteousness, not arbitrary whim.

In this passage, Baqillani presents a decisive argument that divine favor in bestowing prophethood is not capricious but based on the individual's merit—their actions and sincerity. He draws a parallel to a principle the objectors already accept: that God favors the repentant and those who accept rational proofs over others because they deserve it. By this analogy, Baqillani forces the objectors to concede that prophethood, too, is a deserved distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the structure: it begins with a rhetorical question, then presents an analogy, and concludes that the objectors cannot refute this.
Pay attention to the key terms: تفضيل (preference), استحقاق (deserving), إخلاص (sincerity), اجتهاد (striving).
2
Identify the analogy
Baqillani compares God's favoring of prophets to the objectors' own view that God favors the repentant and those who accept rational proofs. Identify how the two cases are parallel.
The objectors already believe that God favors people based on their righteousness. Baqillani applies the same logic to prophethood.
3
Understand the logical force
The argument is that if you accept that divine favor can be deserved in one case (repentance), then you must accept it in the case of prophethood, when the prophet is the best in deeds. This is a consistency argument.
The conclusion is that the objectors have no way to refute this.
4
Address the common misunderstanding
Some might think Baqillani is saying human actions obligate God. But he is not claiming that; he is using the objectors' own principle to show that prophethood is consistent with justice as they understand it.
The distinction: it is about appropriateness, not obligation.
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to see if you grasped the core argument.
The answer is based directly on the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم : ما أنكرتم على من قال من مُثْبِتي نبوة الرسل إنّ الله تعالى ليس يفضل أحد الشخصين على الآخر المجانس له ابتداءً ولا لأجل جنسه ولكن لأجل أنه مستحق للتفضيل بالرسالة وغيرها بعمله والإخلاص في الاجتهاد كما أن الله تعالى يفضل المنيب وقابل الحُجَج العقلية عندكم على من لم يقبلها لا لجنسه ولا لابتدائه بذلك ولا لغير علة ولكن لأنه مستحق للتعظيم والشكر والثناء عندكم لما كان من بره وطاعته، فيكون التفضيل بالرسالة، إذا أراد الله سبحانه إرسال بعض عباده إلى باقيهم، مُستحقاً ؛ لأنه أفضلهم وأكثرهم عملا؟ فلا يجدون لذلك مدفعاً.
Then it is said to them: 'What prevents you from accepting the one who says—from among those who affirm the prophethood of the messengers—that God, Exalted, does not favor one of the two persons over the other similar to him initially nor because of his genus, but because he deserves preference by prophethood and other things through his action and sincerity in striving, just as God, Exalted, favors the repentant and the acceptor of rational proofs over the one who does not accept them—not for his genus, nor for initially doing so, nor for any other cause, but because he deserves veneration, thanks, and praise, according to you, for what was from him of righteousness and obedience. So preference by prophethood, when God, Glorified, wills to send some of His servants to others, is deserved because he is the best of them and the most of them in action. So they will find no way to refute that.'
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is a further refutation directed at the objectors. Baqillani presents an analogy: just as you (the objectors) believe that God favors those who repent and accept rational proofs over those who reject them, because they deserve it through their own actions and sincerity, similarly, God favors prophets with prophethood because they are the most righteous and have the best deeds. Thus, divine favor is not arbitrary but based on merit. The objectors cannot deny this without contradicting their own principles. The argument concludes that the objectors will find no refutation for this point.

Key Terms
تفضيل
استحقاق
رسالة
نية
إخلاص
اجتهاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that Baqillani is claiming human actions obligate God to grant prophethood.
Correction: Baqillani is not saying God is obligated; rather, he is arguing that granting prophethood to the most deserving is consistent with the objectors' own principles about divine favor. It is about appropriateness, not necessity.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why is it acceptable for God to favor some people with prophethood?
A) Because God is capricious and can choose anyone.
B) Because those chosen are the best and most righteous in action.
C) Because God favors based on lineage.
D) Because prophethood is given randomly.

Key Takeaway
Prophethood is granted to those who are most righteous and sincere in action, a consistent extension of the principle that God favors the deserving.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's favor is based on our actions and sincerity, what does your current effort in seeking truth say about the closeness you truly want with Him? Are you willing to examine where you fall short and change today?
?
You already believe God favors the repentant—do you live as though that favor must be earned, or do you assume it? What would it mean for you to take one step toward being among 'those who accept rational proofs' starting now?
?
The prophet was the best in action and sincerity; you are not a prophet, but you are called to follow their path. In one area of your life, what keeps you from giving your utmost sincerity? Commit to a specific replacement habit today.

God's Preference in Prophethood: Based on Deeds
Baqillani refutes an objection about God's preference in selecting prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes the objection that God's selection of prophets is arbitrary, by showing it is based on individual merit.

Core Idea
God's choice of prophets is not arbitrary; it is deserved through deeds and sincerity.

Baqillani addresses a common objection: that God's preference in granting prophethood is unjust or arbitrary. He refutes this by clarifying that divine selection is not based on initial endowment or kind, but on the individual's merit through their deeds and sincere effort. This is analogous to how God rewards those who accept rational proofs over those who reject them. As we read this passage, notice how Baqillani turns the objector's own reasoning against them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to the flow of argument.
This is a refutation, so note the opening dismissal.
2
Identify the objection and response
Find where Baqillani states the objector's claim and how he responds. The response includes a hypothetical statement from those who affirm prophethood.
3
Understand the analogy
Baqillani draws an analogy between God's favoring of the penitent and His selection of prophets. Grasp how this supports the argument.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that the objectors will find no refutation. Consider why this argument is effective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على العامل إنعام وإحسان وليس ذلك بقبيح ولا من الكذب بسبيل فبطل ما قلتم. ثم يقال لهم: ما أنكرتم على من قال من مثبتي نبوة الرسل إن الله تعالى ليس يفضل أحد الشخصين على الآخر المجانس له ابتداء ولا لأجل جنسه ولكن لأجل أنه مستحق للتفضيل بالرسالة وغيرها بعمله والإخلاص في الاجتهاد كما أن الله تعالى يفضل المنيب وقابل الحجج العقلية عندكم على من لم يقبلها لا لجنسه ولا لابتدائه بذلك ولا لغير علة ولكن لأنه مستحق للتعظيم والشكر والثناء عندكم لما كان من بره وطاعته، فيكون التفضيل بالرسالة إذا أراد الله سبحانه إرسال بعض عباده إلى باقيهم مستحقا لأنه أفضلهم وأكثرهم عملا؟ فلا يجدون لذلك مدفعا.
Upon the doer is favor and beneficence, and that is not ugly nor is it from lying in any way, so what you said is invalid. Then it is said to them: What objection do you have against those who affirm prophethood when they say that God, exalted, does not favor one of two persons over another similar to him initially nor because of his kind, but because he deserves preference in prophethood and other things by his deed and sincerity in his effort, just as God favors the penitent and the accepter of rational proofs, in your view, over the one who did not accept them, not because of his kind nor because of initial endowment nor for any other reason, but because he deserves glorification, gratitude, and praise, in your view, due to his piety and obedience. So preference in prophethood, when God wills to send some of His servants to the rest, is deserved because he is the best of them and most in deed. So they will find no daf' (refutation) for that.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection against God's preference (tafdhil) of some individuals over others in granting prophethood. The author first states that the objector's claim is invalid. He then explains the correct position: God does not prefer one person over another due to initial endowment or kind (jins), but because of their deeds and sincerity. This is analogous to how God rewards the penitent and the accepter of rational proofs in your own view. Thus, when God chooses a messenger, it is because that person deserves it by being the best in deeds. Therefore, the objection fails and they can find no refutation.

Correction: Baqillani argues that God's preference is based on the individual's deeds and sincerity, not arbitrary factors.

God's preference in granting prophethood is based on the individual's merit through deeds and sincerity.

?

?
If God's choice of prophets is based on deeds, what does your daily effort say about your love for God? What deed are you neglecting that could bring you closer to Him?
?
The passage says God favors the penitent. When was the last time you truly repented and changed your behavior? Are you waiting for a crisis to return to God, or will you act now?

Refutation of the Same-Kind Objection
Baqillani refutes the claim that a messenger must be of the same kind as the recipients.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's refutation of the objection that a messenger must be of the same kind as the recipients, and why such a condition would undermine divine guidance through reason.

Core Idea
If a messenger must be like us, then God's own reasoning through intellects would fail.

Baqillani continues his defense of prophethood by addressing a common objection: that a messenger must be of the same kind as those to whom he is sent. Since God is unlike creation, the objection goes, He cannot send a messenger. Baqillani turns this argument on its head, showing that if the condition were true, it would also invalidate God's own guidance through the intellect.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the structure: objection, then response, then a conditional argument.
The passage ends mid-sentence, so the full rebuttal continues beyond what we have.
2
Identify the objection
Find the opponent's claim: a messenger must be of the same kind (jins) as the recipients, so God cannot send a messenger because He is unlike creation.
This objection is based on a witnessed analogy.
3
Understand Baqillani's counter-argument
Baqillani uses a reductio ad absurdum: if the same-kind condition holds, then God cannot be a proof (hujja) through intellects or command good and forbid evil, because in the witnessed world the arguer must be of the same kind as the audience.
This would lead to either abandoning tawhid or self-contradiction.
4
Reflect on the consequences
Baqillani presents two options: if the opponents accept the consequence, they abandon tawhid and join the people of ta'til; if they reject it, they refute their own inference.
This shows the objection is self-defeating.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
علة أخرى لهم. فإن قالوا: الدليل على أنه لا يجوز أن يرسل الله تعالى رسولا إلى خلقه أنا وجدنا الرسول في الشاهد والمعقول من جنس المرسل فلما لم يجز أن يكون القديم من جنس المخلوقات بذاته ثبت أنه لا يجوز أن يرسل رسولا إلى خلقه فيقال لهم: فيجب على اعتلالكم هذا ألا يكون الله سبحانه محتجا على الخلق بعقولهم ولا أمرا لهم بما وضعه فيها عندكم من وجوب فعل الحسن وترك القبيح واستعمال النظر وفعل التوحيد الله والمعرفة به والشكر لنعمه لأن المحتج الأمر في الشاهد المأمور المحتج عليه فإن مروا على ذلك تركوا التوحيد ولحقوا بأهل التعطيل، وإن أبوه وراموا فصلا نقضوا استدلالهم. ويقال لهم: فيجب على
Another proof for them. If they say: The proof that God cannot send a messenger to His creation is that we found the messenger in the witnessed and rational realm to be of the same kind as the one to whom he is sent. Since it is not permissible for the Eternal to be of the same kind as creatures in His essence, it is established that He cannot send a messenger to His creation. So it is said to them: On the basis of this reasoning of yours, it must follow that God is not a proof against creation through their intellects, nor a commander to them regarding what He has placed in them, in your view, of the obligation to do good and avoid evil, and to employ reflection, and to perform tawhid of God, knowledge of Him, and gratitude for His blessings, because the one who proves and commands in the witnessed realm is of the same kind as the one on whom the proof is made. If they pass over that, they abandon tawhid and join the people of denial (ta'til). And if they reject it and seek a distinction, they refute their own inference. And it is said to them: It is necessary that...
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage refutes an objection that a messenger must be of the same kind (jins) as the recipients, so God—being unlike creatures—cannot send a messenger. Baqillani argues that this reasoning would also invalidate God's own argument through intellects and commands, because in the witnessed realm the arguer must be of the same kind. If the opponents accept this, they abandon tawhid and fall into ta'til (denial of God's attributes). If they reject it, they contradict their own proof. The passage ends mid-sentence, indicating further argument.

Correction: Baqillani shows this condition would invalidate God's own intellectual guidance, leading to self-contradiction or denial of tawhid.

Checkpoint

A) God's oneness would be established
B) God's argument through intellects would be invalid
C) Prophethood would be proven
D) The world would be eternal

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes the same-kind condition by showing it would make God's intellectual guidance impossible, forcing opponents into self-contradiction or denial of tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever assume that God must act in a way that fits your limited understanding of how things should be? This passage shows that imposing human conditions on God leads to absurdity. Where in your life have you placed conditions on how God should guide or communicate with you? Are you willing to accept that God's ways are beyond your analogies?
?
Baqillani argues that if we demand a messenger of our own kind, we would also nullify God's inner proof through reason. Have you ever ignored the voice of your own conscience (the fitra) because it didn't come in a form you expected? How does this passage challenge you to recognize God's proofs in unexpected forms?
?
The opponents' reasoning led them to undermine tawhid. How often do your own logical objections to God's actions lead you away from submission rather than closer to Him? What would it take for you to surrender your conditions today?

Skeptics' challenge to revelation
Skeptics argue that a messenger cannot verify divine revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the skeptics' argument that a messenger cannot be certain that a communication is from God.

Core Idea
If God is unseen, how can a messenger know His voice from any other?

The skeptics raise a fundamental challenge: since God is not perceptible by the senses, any claimed revelation could be from a jinn, human, or demon. They examine three possible modes of revelation—voice, angel, and book—and find each insufficient for certainty. This lesson presents their argument, which Imam al-Baqillani will later refute.

Guided Path
1
Read the skeptics' opening claim
Read the first part of the passage where skeptics state that there is no way to receive a message from the Creator since He is not seen or perceived.
Notice they assume only sensory verification provides certainty.
2
Examine the first mode: voice
They consider a messenger hearing a voice, as Moses did, and doubt whether it could be from God rather than an angel, jinn, or human.
The example of Moses is used to illustrate the uncertainty.
3
Examine the second and third modes: angel and book
They argue that a messenger cannot know if a being claiming to be an angel is actually an 'ifrit or sorcerer, and that a book could be human-made or carried by the wind.
Each mode is rejected for lack of certainty.
4
Understand the conclusion
The skeptics conclude that there is no way for a messenger to receive revelation, thus prophethood is impossible.
This sets up the need for Baqillani's refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قول آخر لهم واستدلوا أيضاً على منع إرسال الرسل بأن قالوا : لم نجد وجهاً من قبله يصح تلقي الرسالة عن الخالق جلّ ذكره؛ وذلك أنه ليس ممن بالأبصار ويشاهد بالحواس فيتولى مخاطبة الرسول بنفسه من حيث يراه ويَعْلَمُه مخاطباً له حسب الرائيين أحدهما للآخر وإنما يَدَّعِي الرَّسُولُ العلم بالرسالة من جهة صوت يسمعه أو كتاب يقع إليه أو سماع شخص ماثل بين يديه يذكر أنه بعض ملائكة ربه قالوا وذلك كالذي ادعاه موسى بن عِمْرَانَ من أن الله تعالى كلمه وتولى خطابه بلا واسطة ولا تَرْجُمَانٍ قالوا ولم يَدَّعِ مع ذلك رؤية ربه سبحانه وإنما أخبر عن صوت سمعه فما يُذريه، لعل صاحب ذلك الصوت ومكلّمه بعضُ الملائكة أو الجن أو مستتر عنه من الإنس ولا له إلى أن يعلم أن متولي خطابه هو الله ربّ العالمين علمه بأن في العالم أرواحاً مع ناطقة بمثل ما سمعه ومن جنسه وعلى صفته . وكذلك زعموا أن قول الرسول إن الذي أدى إليه الرسالة عن ربه مَلَكُ مُقَرَّبٌ قول لا سبيل له إلى العلم به ولعل الذي خاطبه عِفْريت من العفاريت أو بعضُ السِّحَرَة والمُخيّلين فأما التعويل على كتاب يُظَنُّ أنه من عند ربه فهو أبعدُ الأمور من أن يعلم أن ذلك الكتاب ليس من عمل البشر ونظمهم ولو أنه أيضاً سقط عليه من نحو السَّماءِ لم يَدْرِ لعله مما طرحه عفريت من العفاريت أو مما أرسل مع الريح ، أو حملته فألقته إليه. وإذا كان ذلك كذلك فلا سبيل إذاً للرسول إلى تلقي الرسالة عن الخالق تعالى وفي ذلك فساد القول بنبوة الرسل عليهم السلام
Another statement of theirs: they also argued against the sending of messengers by saying: we find no way from His side by which receiving the message from the Creator, majestic is His mention, is valid; because He is not one who is seen by eyes or perceived by senses, so that He would undertake addressing the messenger Himself from where he sees Him and knows Him as addressing him like two seers of each other. Rather, the messenger claims knowledge of the message from a voice he hears, or a book that falls to him, or hearing a person standing before him who mentions that he is some angel of his Lord. They said: That is like what Moses son of 'Imran claimed, that God spoke to him and undertook His address without intermediary or interpreter. They said: He did not claim seeing his Lord, but reported a voice he heard. So what makes him know? Perhaps the owner of that voice and speaker is some angel, or jinn, or a human hidden from him, and he has no way to know that the one addressing him is God, Lord of the worlds, except by his knowledge that there are souls in the world speaking like what he heard and of its kind and description. Likewise, they claimed that the messenger's statement that the one who conveyed the message from his Lord is an angel brought near is a statement for which he has no way to knowledge; perhaps the one who addressed him is an 'ifrit of the 'afārīt or some sorcerers and illusionists. As for relying on a book that is thought to be from his Lord, that is the farthest thing from knowing that that book is not the work of humans and their compositions. Even if it fell upon him from the direction of the sky, he would not know; perhaps it is something thrown by an 'ifrit of the 'afārīt, or something sent with the wind, or carried and dropped to him. If that is so, then there is no way for the messenger to receive the message from the Creator, and in that is the corruption of the claim to prophethood of the messengers.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage presents the skeptics' objection against the possibility of prophecy. The skeptics argue that since God is not perceptible by the senses, there is no way for a human to be certain that a communication is from God. They consider possible methods: a voice, a book, or an angel. For each, they raise doubts: the voice could be from a jinn or human; the angel could be a demon or sorcerer; a book could be human-made or thrown by a jinn. They use the example of Moses, who heard a voice but did not see God, and claim that Moses could not be sure the voice was from God. The conclusion is that no messenger can verify revelation, thus prophethood is impossible. This is a classic skeptical argument in kalam, which Baqillani will refute in the next lesson.

Correction: This passage is only a presentation of the skeptics' argument; Baqillani will refute it in the following lesson.

D) Miracles are impossible.

Key Takeaway
The skeptics argue that without sensory verification, a messenger cannot be certain that any communication comes from God, thus denying the possibility of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If your certainty about revelation depended on a voice you heard or a book you found, how would you know it was from God? What evidence in your own life confirms the divine origin of the Quran without needing sensory proof?
?
The skeptics demand absolute sensory verification. Is your own faith based on that kind of proof, or on something deeper? What would you sacrifice if you demanded the same standard of certainty they do?

Skeptics' Objection: Can a Prophet Be Certain of Revelation?
Presents the skeptics' argument against prophetic certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the skeptics' argument that a prophet cannot be certain his revelation is from God, because the message could originate from other sources.

Core Idea
Skeptics deny prophetic certainty by multiplying possible sources of revelation.

The skeptics challenge the very foundation of prophethood by arguing that a prophet has no way to verify the source of his claimed revelation. Could it be an angel, a jinn, a hidden human, or even a demon? Could a scripture be human-made or carried by the wind? This passage presents their objection, which the theologian must then refute.

Guided Path
1
Read the passages carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Note the skeptics' tone and the list of alternative sources.
The passage is an objection, not the author's own view.
2
Identify the alternative sources
List all the different possible sources the skeptics suggest for revelation: angels, jinn, hidden humans, demons, sorcerers, human composition, or natural phenomena like wind.
Each alternative is introduced with 'لعل' or similar expressions of possibility.
3
Understand the logical structure
The skeptics argue that for each claimed form of revelation (verbal message, book), the prophet cannot rule out these alternatives, so he cannot be certain the source is God.
This is a 'from possibility to uncertainty' argument.
4
Recognize the conclusion
The skeptics conclude that if the prophet cannot be certain, then no one can claim prophethood, which would invalidate all prophets.
The phrase 'وفي ذلك فساد القول بنبوة الرسل' makes the conclusion explicit.
5
Prepare for the refutation
Ask yourself: How might a theologian respond? What evidence could a prophet have to rule out these alternatives?
This sets up the next lesson where the refutation is provided.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بعضُ الملائكة أو الجن أو مستتر عنه من الإنس ولا له إلى أن يعلم أن متولي خطابه هو الله رب العالمين علمه بأن في العالم أرواحاً مع ناطقة بمثل ما سمعه ومن جنسه وعلى صفته. وكذلك زعموا أن قول الرسول إن الذي أدى إليه الرسالة عن ربه ملك مقرب قول لا سبيل له إلى العلم به ولعل الذي خاطبه عفريت من العفاريت أو بعض السحرة والمخيلين فأما التعويل على كتاب يظن أنه من عند ربه فهو أبعد الأمور من أن يعلم أن ذلك الكتاب ليس من عمل البشر ونظمهم ولو أنه أيضاً سقط عليه من نحو السماء لم يدر لعله مما طرحه عفريت من العفاريت أو مما أرسل مع الريح، أو حملته فألقته إليه. وإذا كان ذلك كذلك فلا سبيل إذاً للرسول إلى تلقي الرسالة عن الخالق تعالى. وفي ذلك فساد القول بنبوة الرسل عليهم السلام.
Some of the angels or jinn or a hidden human being, and he has no way to know that the one addressing him is God, Lord of the worlds, except that he knows that in the world there are spirits speaking with the like of what he heard and of its kind and form. And likewise they claimed that the statement of the messenger that the one who conveyed the message from his Lord is a close angel is a statement that he has no way to know, and perhaps the one who spoke to him is a powerful demon (ifrit) from among the demons, or some of the sorcerers and illusionists. As for relying on a book that is thought to be from his Lord, it is the farthest of things from knowing that that book is not from the work of humans and their composition. Even if it also fell upon him from the direction of the sky, he would not know, perhaps it is something thrown by a demon (ifrit) from among the demons, or something sent with the wind, or carried by it and thrown to him. And if that is the case, then there is no way for the messenger to receive the message from the Creator, Exalted. And in that is the corruption of the claim to prophethood of the messengers, peace be upon them.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage presents the skeptics' objection against the possibility that a prophet can be certain he is receiving revelation from God. The skeptics argue that a prophet cannot rule out alternative sources: the message could come from angels, jinn, or a hidden human being. They claim that when a prophet says the message is from an angel, he has no way to verify it; it could be a demon or a sorcerer. Similarly, a scripture thought to be divine could be human fabrication, or even if it fell from the sky, it might have been thrown by a demon or carried by the wind. Therefore, the skeptics conclude that a prophet has no way to receive a message from God, which would undermine the entire claim of prophethood.

Misconception: This passage shows that prophethood is impossible.

Key Takeaway
The skeptics deny prophetic certainty by claiming a prophet cannot distinguish divine revelation from messages coming from angels, jinn, demons, sorcerers, or human fabrication.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

God Can Compel Knowledge: Second Refutation
Second refutation: God can compel prophetic knowledge of His speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam al-Baqillani's argument that God can directly compel prophetic knowledge of His speech, even if that speech resembles human speech.

Core Idea
God can bypass inference and directly compel knowledge of His speech.

This passage presents the second refutation against the objection that prophecy cannot be verified because the messenger cannot know the speech is from God. Imam al-Baqillani argues that even if the speech were like human speech, God has the power to compel the prophet to know its divine origin directly, without relying on external signs. This establishes that prophetic knowledge can be certain through divine intervention rather than inference.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the English translation. Let the author's own argumentative flow come through.
Note the hypothetical 'if' clause at the beginning.
2
Identify the conditional premise
The argument begins with a conditional: 'if what the messenger heard was of the kind of human speech'. Understand that this is a concession for the sake of argument.
3
Trace the two-stage compulsion
The author describes two stages of compelled knowledge: first, knowledge of God's essence and existence; second, knowledge that the speech is His and His intended meaning. Notice the order.
This shows that direct divine action can replace inferential reasoning.
4
Understand the consequences
Once compelled, the prophet is relieved of the obligation to seek knowledge through speculation, but is still charged with delivering the message. See how this refutes the objection.
The objection claimed no way to know; the author shows a way.
5
Grasp the final conclusion
The author concludes that no revealed text prevents this, so the objection is invalid. Recognise this as a complete refutation.
The argument does not rely on revelation; it's a rational proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوجه الآخر أنه لو كان ما سمعه الرسول أو الملك من جنس كلام الآدميين لكان الله سبحانه قادراً على أن يضطره إلى العلم بأنه هو المكلم له وأن الكلام الذي سمعه كلام له، بأن يضطره أولاً إلى العلم بذاته ووجوده ثم يضطره إلى العلم بأن الكلام كلامه وأن مراده به إن كان بصيغة ما يحتمل وجوهاً من الكلام كذا وكذا وسقط عن الرسول تكليف معرفته وفرض العلم بوجوده إذا كان قد اضطره إلى العلم ويكلفه تحمل الرسالة وأداءها إلى من شاء من خلقه ولعل في هذه سبيل علمه به وبكلامه ومراده له إن لم يمنع من ذلك سمع أو توقيف ولا سمع نعرفه في ذلك يمنع منه وإذا كان ذلك كذلك بطل سؤالكم أنه لا سبيل للرسول إلى العلم بتلقي الرسالة عن الخالق.
And the other aspect is that if what the messenger or angel heard was of the kind of human speech, then God, Exalted, would be able to compel him to know that He is the one speaking to him and that the speech he heard is His speech, by compelling him first to knowledge of His essence and existence, then compelling him to knowledge that the speech is His speech and that His intent by it, if it is in a formulation that admits multiple aspects of speech, is such-and-such. And the messenger would be relieved of the obligation of knowing Him and the duty of knowledge of His existence, when He has compelled him to knowledge, and He would charge him with bearing the message and delivering it to whomever He wills of His creation. And perhaps in this is a way for him to know Him, His speech, and His intent for him, unless there is a revealed text or a tradition that prevents that, and we know of no revealed text that prevents that. And if that is the case, then your question is invalid, namely that there is no way for the messenger to know receiving the message from the Creator.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage presents the second refutation. Even if the speech were human-like, God could still make the prophet know its divine origin by compelling knowledge. God could first compel knowledge of His own existence and essence, then compel knowledge that this speech is His. By doing so, the prophet would have certain knowledge without needing to infer from qualities. The prophet would then be charged with delivering the message. Since nothing in revelation prevents this, the skeptics' objection is invalid. The author concludes that the skeptics' question about the impossibility of prophetic knowledge is refuted.

Correction: The passage shows that God can directly compel knowledge of His existence and speech, making external inference unnecessary.

Imam al-Baqillani argues that God can directly compel prophetic knowledge of His speech, making external inference unnecessary.

?
Imagine you are standing before God and He asks: 'I gave you the ability to know Me directly through the prophets, but did you pursue that knowledge with sincerity?' What will your answer be?

Prophet's Certain Knowledge of God's Speech
Baqillani refutes the objection that a prophet cannot know God's speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that a prophet can know God's speech either through direct compulsion or through signs, and how this refutes the objection that such knowledge is impossible.

Core Idea
God can directly cause the prophet to know His speech, removing the need for proof.

Baqillani addresses a key objection: how can a prophet be certain that the speech he hears is from God? He argues that even if the speech resembled human language, God could compel the prophet to know it is His. This establishes the rational possibility of prophetic knowledge, though the actual method involves signs. In this passage, he outlines the logic of compulsion and then dismisses any transmitted evidence that would prevent it.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The objection is that the prophet cannot know for sure that the speech he hears is from God. Baqillani begins by addressing this.
This sets up the need for a proof.
2
Follow Baqillani's hypothetical
He proposes that even if the speech were similar to human speech, God could still compel the prophet to know it is His.
This is a conditional argument.
3
See the process of compulsion
God would first compel knowledge of His own essence and existence, then compel knowledge that the speech is His and clarify the intended meaning.
This shows the steps in direct knowledge.
4
Note the conclusion
Since no transmitted revelation prevents such direct knowledge, the objection falls.
Baqillani dismisses any counter-evidence from tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوجه الآخر أنه لو كان ما سمعه الرسول أو المَلَكُ من جنس كلام الآدميين لكان الله سبحانه قادراً على أن يَضْطَرَّه إلى العلم بأنه هو المُكلّمُ له وأن الكلام الذي سمعه كلام له، بأن يضطره أولاً إلى العلم بذاته ووجوده ثم يضطره إلى العلم بأن الكلام كلامه وأن مراده به إن كان بصيغة ما يحتمل وجوهاً من الكلام كذا وكذا وسقط عن الرسول تكليف معرفته وفَرْضُ العلم بوجوده إذا كان قد اضطره إلى العلم ويُكلَّفه تَحَمُّلَ الرسالة وأداءها إلى من شاء من خَلْقِـه ولعل في هذه سبيل علمه به وبكلامه ومراده له إن لم يمنع من ذلك سمع أو توقيف ولا سَمْعَ نَعْرِفُه في ذلك يمنع منه وإذا كان ذلك كذلك بَطَلَ سؤالكم أنه لا سبيل للرسول إلى العلم بتلقي الرسالة عن الخالق.
The second aspect: if what the messenger or angel heard were of the genus of human speech, then God the Exalted would be able to compel him to knowledge that He is the one speaking to him and that the speech he heard is His speech, by first compelling him to knowledge of His essence and existence, then compelling him to knowledge that the speech is His speech and that His intent by it, if it was in a form that admits multiple interpretations of speech, is such and such. And the burden of knowing Him and the obligation of knowledge of His existence would be lifted from the messenger, since He would have compelled him to knowledge. And He would charge him with bearing the message and delivering it to whomever He wills of His creation. Perhaps in this [way] is the path of his knowledge of Him, His speech, and His intent for him, unless prevented from that by transmitted revelation or authoritative instruction. And we know no transmitted revelation in that matter to prevent it. When that is the case, your objection falls—that there is no way for the messenger to know by receiving the message from the Creator.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the objection that a prophet cannot know for certain that the speech he hears is from God. Baqillani argues that even if the speech were similar to human speech, God could directly cause the prophet to know it is His speech through compulsion (idhtirar). He outlines a process: God would first compel knowledge of His own existence and essence, then compel knowledge that the speech is His, and clarify the intended meaning. This would remove the burden of inferring God's existence and the obligation to seek knowledge of Him. The prophet would then be charged with delivering the message. However, Baqillani notes that this direct compulsion is not the actual method; rather, God uses signs. The proof concludes that the objection is invalid because there is no known transmitted evidence preventing such direct knowledge.

Key Terms
اضطرار (idhtirar)
تكليف (taklif)
محنة (mihna)
سمع (sam')
توقيف (tawqif)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A prophet cannot know for certain that the speech he hears is from God.
Correction: Baqillani shows that God can compel such knowledge, making it possible; the actual method is through signs.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what would happen if God compelled the prophet to know His speech?
A) The prophet would still need to prove God's existence.
B) The prophet would know the speech is God's directly, removing the need for inference.
C) The prophet would not be charged with delivering the message.
D) The speech would be incomprehensible.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani establishes that direct compulsion is a possible way for a prophet to know God's speech, undermining the objection that such knowledge is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God could compel you to know Him with absolute certainty, yet He chooses to let you seek Him through signs and arguments, what does that reveal about your responsibility? Are you actively pursuing that knowledge, or are you content with vague belief?
?
This passage shows that God can directly communicate His intent. When you read the Quran, do you approach it as if God is speaking directly to you right now? If not, what would change if you did?
?
Baqillani argues that the messenger bears the burden of delivering the message after receiving certainty. What message has God entrusted you to deliver to those around you? Are you fulfilling that trust, or are you silent because you lack the certainty of the prophet?
