First Method: Reports of Hidden Things
Baqillani explains the first way: reports of hidden things.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how accurate reports about hidden matters serve as a proof that a prophet's speech is from God.

Core Idea
Accurate reports of secrets prove the Speaker knows the unseen.

Baqillani presents the first of two ways a prophet can be certain that the speech he receives is from God. By including in the address reports about matters only the prophet himself knows, God demonstrates that the speaker is the Knower of the Unseen. This method relies on the impossibility of any creature producing such accurate reports in large numbers. Let's examine Baqillani's reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the flow.
2
Identify the core claim about guessers (hadis)
Notice the analogy: a guesser can hit the truth once or twice but not repeatedly without error. This sets up the proof.
3
Understand the logic of probability
The prophet receives many reports that are all true. This cannot be by chance or guesswork. It must be from the Knower of the Unseen.
This is a rational proof based on custom (ʿāda).
4
Connect to the conclusion
The prophet knows that only God can know all hidden things. Thus the speaker must be God.
The passage ends by calling this a clear path with no ambiguity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما أنكرتم أيضاً من أن يصح عِلْمُ الرسول بأن الله سبحانه هو المتولي لكلامه مع بقاء المِحْنَةِ عليه وإلزام الله سبحانه إياه معرفته من وجهين: أحدهما أن يَجْعَلَ الخطاب له خبراً عن غيب اسْتَسَرَّهُ عليه السلام واعتقده في نفسه ولم يُطْلِع عليه أحداً من الخلق ويُخبره ملائكته من ذلك عما أحبه قلبه وانطوى عليه ضميره أخباراً متصلة تخرج بكثرتها عن حد ما يمكن إصابةُ الظَّان والمُخَمِّن فيه؛ لأن المعلوم بمُسْتَقر العادة أن الحادس يصيب في الخبر والاثنين والثلاثة ولا يصيب في المائة والمائتين والألف والألفين حتى لا يَغْلَط في واحد منها؛ وإذا كان ذلك كذلك، كان الله تعالی أراد إعْلَامَ من يتولى خطابه أنه المُتَوَلِّي لكلامه ضَمِّنَ خطابه الإِخْبَارَ عن الغيوب وما أسَرَّتَهُ النفوس، فَيَعْلَمُ المُخَاطَبُ عند ذلك أن المُتَولي لكلامه هو عَلامُ الغيوب لتقدم علمه بأن الإخبار عن الغيوب والإصابة فيها مُتَعَذِّرٌ على المخلوقين وأن المنفرد بهذا هو رب العالمين وهذا طريق للعلم بصحة الرسالة عن الله واضح لا إشكال فيه. وقد يمكن أن يُعْلِم الله سبحانه الرسول أنه المتولي لخطابه بأن يقول: أنا الله الذي لا إله إلا أنا؛ وآية ذلك أني أقلب الجماد حيواناً وأخْرِجُ يدك بيضاء وأفلق البحر وأخرج الحيوان من الصخر فَيَعْلَمُ الرسول أن المتولي لخطابه هو مُحْدِثُ الآيات ومبدع المعجزات لتقدم علمه بأن الخلق لا قدرة لهم على ذلك. وليس يجوز أن يُحمِّل الله الرسالة لبعض أنبيائه وهو مع ذلك ممن لم يتقدم علمه بأن أحداً من المخلوقين لا يستطيع الإخبار عن الغيوب والإصابة فيها ولا يقدر على إبداع الأجسام وإحياء الموات وخرق العادات بل لا يرسل إلا أكمل الخلق علماً به ومعرفة له وإذا كان ذلك كذلك سقط ما توهمتم.
Also, what do you deny regarding the possibility of the messenger's knowledge that God the Exalted is the one undertaking His speech while the trial remains upon him? And God the Exalted obligated him to know it in two ways: One of them is that He makes the address to him a report about a hidden matter that he (peace be upon him) had concealed and believed in his soul, and had not disclosed to any of the creation, and His angels inform him of that—continuous reports about what his heart loved and his conscience harbored, reports whose multiplicity exceeds the limit of what a conjecturer or guesser could hit upon. For it is known by settled custom that a guesser may hit upon one, two, or three reports, but does not hit upon a hundred, two hundred, a thousand, or two thousand without erring in a single one of them. When that is the case, God the Exalted intended to inform the one undertaking His address that He is the one undertaking His speech, so He included in His address reports about unseen things and what souls conceal. Then the addressee knows at that point that the one undertaking His speech is the Knower of the Unseen, because of his prior knowledge that reporting about unseen things and hitting upon them is impossible for creatures, and that the one unique in this is the Lord of the worlds. This is a clear path to knowledge of the truth of the message from God, with no ambiguity in it. And it is possible that God the Exalted inform the messenger that He is the one undertaking His address by saying: 'I am God, there is no god but Me; and the sign of that is that I turn inanimate objects into living beings, bring forth your hand white, split the sea, and bring forth animals from rock.' Then the messenger knows that the one undertaking His address is the Creator of signs and the originator of miracles, because of his prior knowledge that creatures have no power over that. And it is not permissible for God to charge some of His prophets with the message while, at the same time, he is one whose prior knowledge does not include that no creature can report about unseen things and hit upon them, nor can they originate bodies, bring the dead to life, or break customs. Rather, He only sends the most perfect of creatures in knowledge of Him and cognizance of Him. When that is the case, what you have supposed falls away.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is a second refutation, presenting two concrete ways a prophet can know that a speech is from God. First, God can include in His address reports about hidden things (ghayb) that only the prophet himself knows, such as secrets he never disclosed. The prophet receives numerous accurate reports from angels, which customarily could not be guessed correctly in such volume. This proves the source is the Knower of the Unseen. Second, God can accompany the address with miracles (mu'jizat), like turning inanimate objects into living beings, making a hand white, splitting the sea, etc. The prophet already knows that creatures cannot do these things, so the miracle confirms the speaker is the Creator. Baqillani concludes that it is impossible for God to send a prophet who does not already possess this prior knowledge that creatures cannot perform these feats; thus the objection that a prophet cannot know the source of speech is baseless.

Key Terms
غيب (ghayb)
إصابة (isaba)
حادس (hadis)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophets know God's speech through subjective feelings or personal inspiration alone.
Correction: This passage shows an objective, rational proof: the accuracy of many reports about hidden matters, which cannot be guessed.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why can't a guesser (hadis) be the source of many accurate reports?
A) Because guessers are always wrong.
B) Because custom shows guessers err after a few correct guesses.
C) Because the reports are about the unseen.
D) Because angels are not guessers.

Key Takeaway
God proves His speech through numerous accurate reports of hidden matters, which only the Knower of the Unseen can produce.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The prophet received reports that matched the secrets he alone knew. Think of a time when you received a sign that could only come from someone who knows your deepest secrets. Did it increase your certainty in God? Why or why not?
?
This proof shows that certainty comes from evidence. Where does your own certainty about the truth of the Prophet come from? Is it built on rational evidence like this, or on social habit? What will you do if it is only habit?
?
The One who knows all your hidden thoughts has revealed them to His prophet. Does that knowledge make you want to draw closer to Him, or does it scare you? Commit to one specific action today that acknowledges that He sees you.

Second Method: Miracles and Prior Knowledge
Baqillani explains the second way: miracles, and adds a necessary condition about prior knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how miracles accompanying a prophetic address confirm its divine origin and why the prophet must already know that creatures cannot perform miracles.

Core Idea
Miracles confirm the speaker is the Creator.

Baqillani now presents the second way: God can accompany the address with miracles such as turning inanimate objects into living beings, making a hand white, splitting the sea, or bringing forth animals from rock. The prophet, already knowing that creatures cannot do such things, recognizes the speaker as the Creator. Baqillani also adds a necessary condition: God only sends prophets who already possess this prior knowledge, thereby refuting the objection. Let's explore this proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the second method and the concluding condition.
2
Identify the types of miracles mentioned
Notice the specific examples: turning inanimate to living, white hand, splitting sea, animals from rock. These are signs of creative power.
3
Understand the logic of miracles as proof
The prophet sees these miracles happening in connection with the speech. He knows from prior knowledge that no creature can do these things. Therefore the speaker must be the Creator of those miracles.
4
Grasp the final condition
Baqillani states that God does not charge a prophet with the message unless he already knows that creatures cannot perform such acts. This answers the objection that a prophet might doubt the source.

آية (aya)
إبداع (ibda')

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think miracles are just unexplained events that could be done by anyone.
Correction: Miracles are signs of divine power because they involve creating life and breaking natural laws, which only God can do.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what prior knowledge does a prophet have that allows him to recognize the speaker as God through miracles?
A) Knowledge that creatures can perform miracles.
B) Knowledge that no creature can perform such acts.
C) Knowledge that angels are powerful.
D) Knowledge that the speech is eloquent.

Key Takeaway
Miracles accompanying a prophetic address prove it is from God, and a prophet must already know that no creature can perform such acts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you have the same certainty as the prophets that no creature can perform miracles? When you witness something extraordinary, do you instinctively attribute it to God, or do you rationalize it away? What would it take for you to be as convinced as the prophets were?
?
Baqillani says that God only sends the most perfect creatures in knowledge of Him. In what specific areas of your life are you striving to increase your knowledge of God? If you are not actively seeking that knowledge, what does that say about the authenticity of the messages you claim to follow?
?
The passage ends with 'what you have supposed falls away.' What assumptions have you held about prophethood, miracles, or divine communication that might be shattered by this argument? Are you willing to let them go, even if it means rethinking deeply held beliefs?

Prophethood
beginner
5 min
Proof of Prophethood Through Knowledge of the Unseen
Baqillani presents the tawātur-based argument for prophethood through knowledge of the unseen.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Baqillani uses the concept of tawātur (mass transmission) of reports about hidden matters to prove that the speaker is God, the Knower of the Unseen, and thus establish the truth of prophecy.

Core Idea
Accurate reports about hidden things, beyond all guesswork, can only come from God.

How can we know that a prophet's message truly comes from God? Al-Baqillani presents a rational argument: when a person makes numerous accurate claims about what is hidden in people's hearts, and those claims are so many that no human guesser could consistently get them right, this proves the speaker knows the unseen—something only God can do. In this lesson, we explore this proof from mass transmission (tawātur) of hidden knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on the logic of tawātur.
Notice how Baqillani contrasts guessers with the multitude of reports.
2
Understand the tawātur argument
Identify why reports of hidden matters beyond a certain number (hundreds, thousands) cannot be attributed to coincidence or guesswork.
3
Connect to the proof of prophethood
See how this demonstrates that the speaker must be God, the Knower of the Unseen.
4
Reflect on the epistemological basis
Consider why this argument is considered a 'clear, unambiguous path' according to Baqillani.
This is a foundational argument in kalam for divine origin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متى ذلك عما أحبه قلبه وانطوى عليه ضميره أخباراً متصلة تخرج بكثرتها عن حد ما يمكن إصابة الظان والمخمن فيه؛ لأن المعلوم بمستقر العادة أن الحادس يصيب في الخبر والاثنين والثلاثة ولا يصيب في المائة والمائتين والألف والألفين حتى لا يغلط في واحد منها؛ وإذا كان ذلك كذلك، كان الله تعالى أراد إعلام من يتولى خطابه أنه المتولي لكلامه ضمن خطابه الإخبار عن الغيوب وما أسرته النفوس، فيعلم المخاطب عند ذلك أن المتولي لكلامه هو علام الغيوب لتقدم علمه بأن الإخبار عن الغيوب والإصابة فيها متعذر على المخلوقين وأن المنفرد بهذا هو رب العالمين وهذا طريق للعلم بصحة الرسالة عن الله واضح لا إشكال فيه. وقد يمكن أن يعلم الله سبحانه الرسول أنه المتولي لخطابه بأن يقول: أنا الله الذي لا إله إلا أنا؛ وآية ذلك أني أقلب الجماد حيواناً وأخرج يدك بيضاء وأفلق البحر وأخرج الحيوان من الصخر فيعلم الرسول أن المتولي لخطابه هو محدث الآيات ومبدع المعجزات لتقدم علمه بأن الخلق لا قدرة لهم على ذلك. وليس يجوز أن يحمل الله الرسالة لبعض أنبيائه وهو مع ذلك ممن لم يتقدم علمه بأن أحداً من المخلوقين لا يستطيع الإخبار عن الغيوب والإصابة فيها ولا يقدر على إبداع الأجسام وإحياء الموات وخرق العادات بل لا يرسل إلا أكمل الخلق علماً به ومعرفة له وإذا كان ذلك كذلك سقط ما توهمتم. وكذلك أيضاً إنما يتبين الرسول من البشر أن المنزل عليه بالرسالة ملك من عند ربه بأن يكون الخطاب الذي أداه إليه متضمناً لإخباره أو بأن يظهر معه من الآيات مثل الذي ظهر على أيدي الرسول عند الأداء إلى أمثالهم من ولد آدم فيعلم عند ذلك أن من ظهرت هذه الأمور على يده فليس بساحر ولا شيطان ولا متمثل من الأرواح وكل هذا يبطل ما توهموه فأما الكتاب الساقط على يد الرسول فلا بد من أن يكون معه آية تظهر على يد ملك سواه يؤديه أو بأن ينطق الله الكتاب ويحييه حتى يؤدي عن نفسه ويخبر بمتضمنه ويخرق العادة بما يظهر منه فلا تعلق لهم في ذلك.
When reports about what the heart loves and what the inner self conceals are continuous (mutawātira), reaching by their multiplicity beyond the limit of what a guesser or conjecturer could possibly get right—because it is established by stable custom that a guesser may be correct about one, two, or three reports, but not about a hundred, two hundred, a thousand, or two thousand without erring in any of them—and if that is so, then God Most High, when He intends to inform the one He is addressing that He is the one who has undertaken His speech, includes in His speech the report of unseen things and what the souls have hidden; so the addressee knows at that point that the one who has undertaken His speech is the Knower of the Unseen, because he already knows that reporting on unseen things and being accurate in all of them is impossible for creatures and that the one uniquely capable of this is the Lord of the Worlds. This is a clear, unambiguous path to knowledge of the truth of the message from God. And it is possible for God—glorified is He—to inform the messenger that He is the one who has undertaken His speech by saying: 'I am God, there is no god but I; and the sign of that is that I turn inanimate matter into a living being, make your hand white, split the sea, and bring forth a living creature from rock,' so that the messenger knows that the one who has undertaken His speech is the originator of the signs and the creator of miracles, because he already knows that creatures have no power over that. And it is not permissible for God to entrust the message to some of His prophets while that prophet is one who has not previously been certain that no creature can report on unseen things and be accurate in them, nor create bodies, revive the dead, or break customs. Rather, He only sends the most perfect of creatures in knowledge of Him and recognition of Him. If that is so, then what you have imagined collapses. And likewise, it is only known that the one who has been sent down the message is an angel from his Lord by the fact that the speech he delivers to the prophet contains information (about the unseen) or that miracles like those that appeared at the hands of the messenger (when delivering to their like among the children of Adam) appear with him; so he knows at that point that the one in whose hand these things appear is not a sorcerer, a devil, or a manifestation of spirits. All of this invalidates what they have imagined. As for the book that descends upon the hand of the messenger, it must either have a miracle appearing at the hand of an angel other than him who delivers it, or God makes the book speak and brings it to life so that it speaks for itself and reports what it contains, breaking custom by what appears from it. Thus they have no argument in that.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage presents a multi-step proof of prophethood. First, Baqillani argues that a prophet's accurate reports about hidden things, when they are numerous and beyond the reach of guesswork (tawātur), demonstrate that the speaker is God, who alone knows the unseen. Second, God may directly address the prophet with a miracle (e.g., changing inanimate matter to life) as a sign that the speaker is God. Third, God only sends a prophet who already knows that no creature can perform such acts. Fourth, the identity of the angel delivering revelation is confirmed either by the content of the message (knowledge of unseen) or by accompanying miracles similar to those the prophet himself performs. Finally, the scripture itself may be a miracle if God makes it speak. The cumulative effect is that prophethood is proven by clear signs that cannot be faked.

Key Terms
أخبار متصلة (mutawātir reports)
إخبار عن الغيوب (knowledge of the unseen)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Baqillani, what makes the knowledge of the unseen reported by a prophet different from human guesswork?
A) The reports are moral teachings
B) The reports are numerous and consistently accurate beyond what any guesser could achieve
C) The reports are written in beautiful language
D) The reports come from angels

Key Takeaway
A prophet's numerous accurate reports about hidden matters, beyond the capacity of human guesswork, prove that the speaker is God, the Knower of the Unseen.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you had to choose one hidden truth about your own heart that you know only God fully sees, what is it—and does that realization make you feel exposed or comforted? How does this lesson's argument about God's knowledge affect your accountability before Him today?
?
When you encounter a claim about prophethood from someone who reports unseen things, do you instinctively test it against your own experience of human limitation? How does this lesson's criterion change the way you evaluate whether a message is from God?
?
What if you were asked to produce just ten accurate reports about what is in another person's mind—would you be certain of failing? How does that human limitation make the prophetic proof not just academic but personally urgent for your faith?

Proof of Prophethood Through Direct Miracles
Baqillani explains how miracles accompanying divine speech confirm the message.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how God’s direct performance of miracles on behalf of a prophet serves as a sign confirming that the prophet’s message is from God.

Core Idea
Miracles beyond human power show that God is speaking.

Al-Baqillani presents another proof: God can directly show the prophet a miracle, such as turning a stone into a living thing, as a sign that the one speaking is the Creator. This lesson examines that argument and its logical basis.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage with focus on the divine speech
Notice how God introduces Himself and then gives a visible sign.
2
Identify what the miracle demonstrates
The miracle proves that the speaker is the originator of all such signs, which no creature can do.
3
Relate to the prophet’s prior knowledge
The prophet already knows that creatures cannot perform such acts, so he recognizes the speaker as God.

Prophethood
beginner
4 min
God Only Chooses the Most Knowledgeable Prophets
Baqillani states that God only sends prophets who already know the limits of creatures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God only sends prophets who already know that no creature can perform miracles or know the unseen, thus preventing confusion.

Core Idea
The prophet must already know creaturely limits to recognize divine signs.

Al-Baqillani adds a crucial condition: before receiving revelation, a prophet must already be certain that no creature can report the unseen or work miracles. This ensures that when he experiences such things, he knows it is from God. This lesson explores the wisdom behind this requirement.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Notice the emphatic denial: 'It is not permissible for God to entrust the message to some of His prophets while he is one who has not previously been certain...'
2
Identify what the prophet must know beforehand
The prophet must know that no creature can report the unseen with accuracy, create bodies, revive the dead, or break customs.
3
Understand why this is necessary
Without this prior knowledge, the prophet might mistakenly attribute the miraculous phenomena to a creature, thus not recognizing God as the source.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That a prophet could be ignorant of the fact that creatures cannot perform miracles, and thus be unsure about the source of the message.
Correction: Baqillani asserts that God only sends prophets who already know creaturely limitations, so when they witness miracles, they are certain it is from God.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what must a prophet know before receiving his message?
A) The entire scripture beforehand
B) That no creature can report the unseen or perform miracles
C) The details of the afterlife
D) The names of all angels

Key Takeaway
God selects prophets who already understand that creatures cannot do the miraculous, so they can reliably identify divine signs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe in your heart that no creature—no human, no jinn, no angel—can independently cause events like healing, provision, or accidents? Or do you, in moments of desperation, attribute such things to creatures? This lesson demands that you examine your tawheed. Will you repent and renew your certainty that all power belongs to God alone?
?
If you were entrusted with a great responsibility tomorrow, would you first ensure you know the limits of your own ability and the inability of all creatures to do what only God can do? How would that knowledge change the way you rely on God versus relying on people?

How the Angel and Scripture Are Recognized as Divine
Baqillani explains how the angel and the scripture are verified as from God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the angel delivering revelation is identified as truly from God, and how the scripture itself can be a miracle.

Core Idea
The angel’s message contains knowledge of the unseen or brings miracles, and the scripture may be made to speak.

Al-Baqillani addresses two more scenarios: how we know the angel who delivers the book is truly from God, and how the book itself can be a miracle. In both cases, the presence of knowledge of the unseen or the breaking of custom proves the divine origin.

Guided Path
1
Read the final part of the passage
Focus on the two methods: the angel's speech containing unseen knowledge, or miracles appearing with the angel.
2
Distinguish between the angel and the prophet
The angel's miracles are like those of the prophet but appear with the angel to confirm his identity.
3
Understand the miracle of the speaking book
God can make the book speak and report its contents, which is a breaking of custom that proves its divine origin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متى ذلك عما أحبه قلبه وانطوى عليه ضميره أخباراً متصلة تخرج بكثرتها عن حد ما يمكن إصابة الظان والمخمن فيه؛ لأن المعلوم بمستقر العادة أن الحادس يصيب في الخبر والاثنين والثلاثة ولا يصيب في المائة والمائتين والألف والألفين حتى لا يغلط في واحد منها؛ وإذا كان ذلك كذلك، كان الله تعالى أراد إعلام من يتولى خطابه أنه المتولي لكلامه ضمن خطابه الإخبار عن الغيوب وما أسرته النفوس، فيعلم المخاطب عند ذلك أن المتولي لكلامه هو علام الغيوب لتقدم علمه بأن الإخبار عن الغيوب والإصابة فيها متعذر على المخلوقين وأن المنفرد بهذا هو رب العالمين وهذا طريق للعلم بصحة الرسالة عن الله واضح لا إشكال فيه. وقد يمكن أن يعلم الله سبحانه الرسول أنه المتولي لخطابه بأن يقول: أنا الله الذي لا إله إلا أنا؛ وآية ذلك أني أقلب الجماد حيواناً وأخرج يدك بيضاء وأفلق البحر وأخرج الحيوان من الصخر فيعلم الرسول أن المتولي لخطابه هو محدث الآيات ومبدع المعجزات لتقدم علمه بأن الخلق لا قدرة لهم على ذلك. وليس يجوز أن يحمل الله الرسالة لبعض أنبيائه وهو مع ذلك ممن لم يتقدم علمه بأن أحداً من المخلوقين لا يستطيع الإخبار عن الغيوب والإصابة فيها ولا يقدر على إبداع الأجسام وإحياء الموات وخرق العادات بل لا يرسل إلا أكمل الخلق علماً به ومعرفة له وإذا كان ذلك كذلك سقط ما توهمتم. وكذلك أيضاً إنما يتبين الرسول من البشر أن المنزل عليه بالرسالة ملك من عند ربه بأن يكون الخطاب الذي أداه إليه متضمناً لإخباره أو بأن يظهر معه من الآيات مثل الذي ظهر على أيدي الرسول عند الأداء إلى أمثالهم من ولد آدم فيعلم عند ذلك أن من ظهرت هذه الأمور على يده فليس بساحر ولا شيطان ولا متمثل من الأرواح وكل هذا يبطل ما توهموه فأما الكتاب الساقط على يد الرسول فلا بد من أن يكون معه آية تظهر على يد ملك سواه يؤديه أو بأن ينطق الله الكتاب ويحييه حتى يؤدي عن نفسه ويخبر بمتضمنه ويخرق العادة بما يظهر منه فلا تعلق لهم في ذلك.
When reports about what the heart loves and what the inner self conceals are continuous (mutawātira), reaching by their multiplicity beyond the limit of what a guesser or conjecturer could possibly get right—because it is established by stable custom that a guesser may be correct about one, two, or three reports, but not about a hundred, two hundred, a thousand, or two thousand without erring in any of them—and if that is so, then God Most High, when He intends to inform the one He is addressing that He is the one who has undertaken His speech, includes in His speech the report of unseen things and what the souls have hidden; so the addressee knows at that point that the one who has undertaken His speech is the Knower of the Unseen, because he already knows that reporting on unseen things and being accurate in all of them is impossible for creatures and that the one uniquely capable of this is the Lord of the Worlds. This is a clear, unambiguous path to knowledge of the truth of the message from God. And it is possible for God—glorified is He—to inform the messenger that He is the one who has undertaken His speech by saying: 'I am God, there is no god but I; and the sign of that is that I turn inanimate matter into a living being, make your hand white, split the sea, and bring forth a living creature from rock,' so that the messenger knows that the one who has undertaken His speech is the originator of the signs and the creator of miracles, because he already knows that creatures have no power over that. And it is not permissible for God to entrust the message to some of His prophets while that prophet is one who has not previously been certain that no creature can report on unseen things and be accurate in them, nor create bodies, revive the dead, or break customs. Rather, He only sends the most perfect of creatures in knowledge of Him and recognition of Him. If that is so, then what you have imagined collapses. And likewise, it is only known that the one who has been sent down the message is an angel from his Lord by the fact that the speech he delivers to the prophet contains information (about the unseen) or that miracles like those that appeared at the hands of the messenger (when delivering to their like among the children of Adam) appear with him; so he knows at that point that the one in whose hand these things appear is not a sorcerer, a devil, or a manifestation of spirits. All of this invalidates what they have imagined. As for the book that descends upon the hand of the messenger, it must either have a miracle appearing at the hand of an angel other than him who delivers it, or God makes the book speak and brings it to life so that it speaks for itself and reports what it contains, breaking custom by what appears from it. Thus they have no argument in that.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage presents a multi-step proof of prophethood. First, Baqillani argues that a prophet's accurate reports about hidden things, when they are numerous and beyond the reach of guesswork (tawātur), demonstrate that the speaker is God, who alone knows the unseen. Second, God may directly address the prophet with a miracle (e.g., changing inanimate matter to life) as a sign that the speaker is God. Third, God only sends a prophet who already knows that no creature can perform such acts. Fourth, the identity of the angel delivering revelation is confirmed either by the content of the message (knowledge of unseen) or by accompanying miracles similar to those the prophet himself performs. Finally, the scripture itself may be a miracle if God makes it speak. The cumulative effect is that prophethood is proven by clear signs that cannot be faked.

Key Terms
آية (sign/miracle)
خرق العادات (breaking of customs)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the angel could be a sorcerer or a devil disguised as an angel.
Correction: Baqillani argues that the presence of knowledge of the unseen or miracles that only God can empower rules out such impostors.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, how can the angel delivering revelation be identified as truly from God?
A) By the angel's shining light
B) By the angel's speech containing knowledge of the unseen or by miracles appearing with him
C) By the angel's name
D) By the angel's ability to fly

Key Takeaway
The angel and the scripture are verified as divine through signs that surpass all creaturely ability.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quran, do you treat it as a living book that can speak to you directly, or as a historical document? If God could make the book speak, what is stopping you from hearing His voice in it today?
?
The angel’s message contained knowledge of the unseen. In your daily life, do you seek guidance from that unseen knowledge (the revelation) or do you rely more on your own opinions and worldly sources? Which one truly shapes your decisions?
?
Have you ever doubted that what you received as revelation is truly from God? Baqillani gives two proofs for the angel. Do these proofs strengthen your certainty, or have you taken the Quran for granted without reflecting on its divine origin?

Deniers' Objection and the Initial Response
Baqillani presents the deniers' argument that miracles are rationally impossible and begins his refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the deniers' argument that miracles are rationally impossible and Baqillani's crucial distinction between impossibility by custom and impossibility in God's power.

Core Idea
Miracles are impossible by custom, not by God's power.

This lesson introduces a key objection to prophethood from those who deny miracles. They argue that claimed miracles contradict natural laws and are therefore rationally impossible. Baqillani begins his refutation by asking a simple but profound question: what do you mean by 'impossible'? This distinction becomes the foundation for the defense of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Understand the deniers' argument
Read the passage to see the list of miracles they consider impossible and their reasoning that quantity cannot change.
2
Notice Baqillani's response
He does not immediately refute; instead he asks for clarification on what 'impossible' means.
3
Reflect on the distinction
Consider the difference between something being impossible by custom (unusual but possible for God) and impossible in God's power (denying omnipotence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قول آخر لمنكري الرسالة واستدلوا على إبطال الرسالة بأن قالوا: وجدنا المدعين للرسالة يزعمون أنه لا طريق إلى العلم بصدقهم إلا وجود محالات ممتنع في العقل وجودها من نحو فلق البحر وخلق ناقة من صخرة وقلب العصا حية وإحياء الموتى وإبراء الأكمه والأبرص والمشي على الماء وإنطاق الذئب والحصا وما جرى مجرى ذلك من ادعائهم جعل القليل كثيراً والقليل لا يتكثر كما أن الكثير لا يتقلل ويتوحد وإذا كان كذلك بطل ما يدعونه، فيقال لهم: ما الذي أردتم بقولكم إن هذه الأمور مستحيلة ممتنعة؟ أعنيتم بذلك أنها مستحيلة في العادة أو في قدرة الصانع تعالى؟ فإن قالوا: في قدرة
Another statement from the deniers of prophethood: They argued for nullifying prophethood by saying: 'We find those who claim prophethood alleging that there is no way to know their truthfulness except through the existence of impossibilities whose existence is rationally prevented, such as splitting the sea, creating a camel from rock, turning a staff into a serpent, reviving the dead, healing the blind and leprous, walking on water, speaking of wolves and pebbles, and what is like that from their claims—making the little much, while the little cannot become much just as the much cannot become little or be unified. If that is so, what they claim is false.' So it is said to them: 'What did you mean by your statement that these things are impossible and prevented? Did you mean by that that they are impossible according to custom or impossible in the power of the Creator, Exalted is He?' If they say: 'In His power...'
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage presents an objection from those who deny prophethood (probably naturalists or philosophers). They argue that the claimed miracles—like splitting the sea, turning a staff into a snake, reviving the dead, etc.—are rationally impossible because they violate natural laws. They claim that quantity cannot be changed (little cannot become much, much cannot become little). Therefore, they assert, all claims to prophethood are false. Baqillani begins his refutation by asking them to clarify what they mean by 'impossible': do they mean impossible according to custom (i.e., unusual but not impossible in itself) or impossible according to God's power (i.e., truly impossible for God)? This distinction is crucial because if they mean impossible by custom, that does not preclude divine intervention; if they mean impossible in God's power, that would be a denial of God's omnipotence. The response is incomplete here, but the seed of the refutation is planted.

Key Terms
محالات (impossibilities)
ممتنع في العقل (rationally prevented)
عادة (custom)
قدرة الصانع (power of the Creator)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles are absolutely impossible because they break natural laws.
Correction: Baqillani points out that what is impossible by custom is not impossible for God; miracles are supernatural acts of God, not violations of omnipotence.

Checkpoint
In Baqillani's response to the deniers, what key distinction does he ask them to clarify?
A) Whether miracles are small or large
B) Whether they mean impossible by custom or by God's power
C) Whether the prophets were truthful or lying
D) Whether miracles benefit the public or only individuals

Key Takeaway
The deniers mistake customary impossibility for absolute impossibility; Baqillani's distinction opens the door for affirming miracles as possible through divine power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What is one situation in your life right now that you have dismissed as hopeless because it seems impossible by normal standards? How does Baqillani's distinction challenge your assumption and call you to trust in God's power?
?
Have you ever mistaken your limited experience for an absolute limit on what God can do? Be honest: when have you acted as if God is bound by your expectations? How does this passage demand that you repent of that limited thinking?
?
The deniers used their intellect to reject prophethood. In what areas of your faith have you used 'rational' objections to avoid submitting to God's commands? What one step will you take this week to obey where your intellect says 'impossible'?

Two Signs that Distinguish a Prophet
Baqillani explains the two signs distinguishing a prophet: the message and the miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two rational signs by which a true prophet is distinguished from impostors according to Baqillani.

Core Idea
A prophet is known by his message or by miracles — both break the ordinary.

How can we tell if someone is truly a prophet of Allah? Baqillani answers this by pointing to two clear signs: either the message itself contains knowledge of the unseen, or miraculous events accompany his preaching. These signs rule out sorcery or deception, ensuring that the claimant is not a sorcerer, devil, or spirit.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the logical flow: first the general distinction, then the special case of the book.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the two signs
The passage presents two ways a prophet is known: (1) the message contains information about the unseen, and (2) miracles appear at his hands. Find these in the text.
3
Understand the exclusion of false claimants
Baqillani says these signs prove the prophet is not a sorcerer, devil, or spirit. Ask yourself why these three are specifically mentioned.
This addresses common objections to prophethood.
4
Analyze the special case of the book
The last part discusses a revealed book (like the Qur'an). It must be accompanied by a miracle, either through an angel or by God making the book itself speak. See how this fits the two signs.
This is a more detailed application of the second sign.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عن الغيوب وكذلك أيضاً إنما يتبين الرسول من البشر أن المُنْزَلَ عليه بالرسالة مَلَكَ من عند ربه بأن يكون الخطاب الذي أداه إليه مُتَضَمِّناً لإخباره أو بأن يَظْهَرَ معه من الآيات مثلُ الذي ظهر على أيدي الرسول عند الأداء إلى أمثالهم من ولد آدم فيعلم عند ذلك أن من ظهرت هذه الأمور على يده فليس بساحر ولا شيطان ولا مُتَمَثَّل من الأرواح وكل هذا يبطل ما توهموه فأما الكتاب الساقط على يد الرسول فلا بد من أن يكون معه آية تظهر على يد ملك سواه يؤديه أو بأن يُنطِق اللهُ الكتاب ويُحْيِيهِ حتى يؤدي عن نفسه ويخبر بمُتَضَمَّنِه ويخرق العادة بما يظهر منه فلا تعلق لهم في ذلك
Concerning the unseen. And similarly, the messenger is distinguished from humans [only] by that which is sent down upon him with the message being an angel from his Lord, either by the speech delivered to him containing information [about the unseen], or by the appearance with him of miracles like those that appeared at the hands of the messenger when delivering to their likes among the children of Adam. Then it is known by that that the one at whose hand these things appear is not a sorcerer, nor a devil, nor a manifestation from spirits. And all of this invalidates what they had imagined. As for the book that falls at the hand of the messenger, it must be accompanied by a miracle appearing at the hand of an angel other than him who delivers it, or by God making the book speak and giving it life so that it delivers itself and informs of its contents, and breaking the custom by what appears from it. So they have no point of attachment in that.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is a definition/explanation of how a prophet is distinguished from ordinary humans. Baqillani states that the prophet is known either by the message itself containing information about the unseen, or by miracles that accompany his delivery. These signs show he is not a sorcerer or devil. Then he specifically addresses the book sent down: it must have a miracle, either through an angel or by God making the book itself speak, breaking custom.

Key Terms
رسول
آية
معجزة
خرق العادة
مَلَك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think any extraordinary event indicates prophethood, failing to distinguish miracles from sorcery.
Correction: Baqillani shows that true prophetic miracles are accompanied by a message from God and cannot be replicated by sorcerers or devils.

Checkpoint
What are the two ways a prophet is distinguished from others according to Baqillani?
A) By his lineage and wealth
B) By the message containing unseen knowledge or by miracles
C) By his eloquence and wisdom

Key Takeaway
A true prophet is known either through the message containing unseen knowledge or through accompanying miracles that break natural laws, invalidating claims of sorcery or deception.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
Baqillani explains that the messenger is known by the message containing unseen knowledge. In your daily life, do you actively seek knowledge of the unseen from revelation, or do you prefer to rely on your own speculation? Where does your certainty about the future and the afterlife come from?
?
The passage says that all this invalidates the skeptics' claims. Is there any part of your faith that you treat as if it were a mere human invention or coincidence? Have you ever dismissed a divine sign in your own life as 'natural' to avoid the responsibility of submission?

The Deniers' Objection: Miracles as Impossibilities
Baqillani presents the objection of the deniers of prophethood regarding miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that miracles are rationally impossible and how it challenges prophethood.

Core Idea
Miracles are deemed impossible only if one confuses custom with absolute power.

Before we examine Baqillani's response, we must first understand the objection he is answering. The deniers argue that the miracles attributed to prophets are rationally impossible, therefore prophethood is false. This objection relies on a specific understanding of impossibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the list of miracles mentioned.
2
Identify the core claim
The deniers claim that miracles are impossible in reason (ممتنع في العقل). Why do they think that?
They argue because such things have never been seen.
3
Understand the reasoning
The deniers say that the little cannot become much, etc. This is their logical basis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قول آخر لمنكري الرسالة واستدلوا على إبطال الرسالة بأن قالوا : وجدنا المدعين للرسالة يزعمون أنه لا طريق إلى العلم بصدقهم إلا وجود محالات ممتنع في العقل وجودها من نحو فَلْقِ البحر وخَلْقِ ناقة من صخرة وقلب العصا حية وإحياء الموتى وإبراء الأكمه والأبرص والمشي على الماء وإنطاق الذئب والحصا وما جرى مجرى ذلك من ادعائهم جعل القليل كثيراً والقليل لا يتكثر كما أن الكثير لا يتقلل ويتوحد وإذا كان كذلك بَطَلَ ما يدعونه، فيقال لهم : ما الذي أردتم بقولكم إن هذه الأمور مستحيلة ممتنعة؟ أعنيتم بذلك أنها مستحيلة في العادة أو في قدرة الصانع تعالى؟ فإن قالوا: في قدرة الصانع ألحدوا وتركوا دينهم، وقيل لهم : ما الدليل على إحالة ذلك؟ وإن قالوا لأننا لم نجد أحداً فعله ولا يقدر عليه ولا رأينا ذلك قط ولا جرى مثل ما تدعون، قيل لهم : فيجب أن تحيلوا أيضاً أن يخلق الله تعالى الأجسام وألا يوجد آدم إلا من ذكر وأنثى وألا يخلق دجاجة إلا من بيضة أو بيضة إلا من دجاجة أو نطفة إلا من إنسان أو إنساناً إلا من نطفة لأن ذلك أجمع لم يوجد قط ولم يشاهد فإن مروا على ذلك لحقوا بأهل الدهر وإن أبوه نقضوا اعتلالهم
Another statement for the deniers of prophethood. They argued for the invalidation of prophethood by saying: We find the claimants to prophethood claiming that there is no way to know their truthfulness except by the existence of impossibilities that are impossible in reason to exist, such as splitting the sea, creating a she-camel from a rock, turning a staff into a snake, reviving the dead, healing the blind and the leper, walking on water, the speaking of the wolf and pebbles, and similar things, including their claim of making the little much, while the little cannot become much just as the much cannot become little, and it is confirmed [that it is impossible]. And if that is the case, what they claim is invalid. So it is said to them: What did you intend by your statement that these matters are impossible? Did you mean that they are impossible in custom or in the power of the Maker? If they say: in the power of the Maker, they have apostatized and abandoned their religion, and it is said to them: What is the proof of the impossibility of that? And if they say: because we have never found anyone who did it, nor is it possible for anyone, nor have we ever seen it, nor has anything like what you claim ever occurred, it is said to them: Then you must also consider impossible that God creates bodies, and that Adam came into existence except from a male and female, and that a chicken comes into existence except from an egg, or an egg except from a chicken, or a drop except from a human, or a human except from a drop, because all of that has never occurred nor been witnessed. If they accept that, they join the materialists; if they reject it, they have nullified their own argument.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer dialectic. The deniers argue that the miracles claimed by prophets are rationally impossible, so prophethood is false. Baqillani's response first clarifies the sense of impossibility: if they mean impossible in God's power, that is apostasy; if they mean impossible in custom, then the reply uses a reductio ad absurdum: by their own reasoning, they would have to deny the common origin of creatures from their sources (e.g., humans from humans, chickens from eggs) because they haven't witnessed the original creation. This forces them into the absurd position of either accepting atheism (ahl al-dahr) or abandoning their objection.

Key Terms
محالات
ممتنع
العقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles are impossible because they have never been observed.
Correction: Baqillani will show that impossibility in custom is not the same as impossibility in God's power.

Checkpoint
According to the deniers, what is the basis for claiming miracles are impossible?
A) They are against reason
B) They have never been seen
C) They are not in the Quran
D) Prophets are liars

Key Takeaway
The deniers' objection relies on the assumption that whatever is unusual is rationally impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read about miracles like the splitting of the sea, do you ever feel a silent doubt, thinking they are just stories? What would it mean for your faith if they were not literally true?
?
The deniers measured Allah's power by their own limited experience. In what area of your life do you limit what Allah can do because you have never seen it happen?
?
If you had been present at one of these miracles, would you have believed it was from Allah, or would you have looked for a natural explanation? What does your answer reveal about your reliance on reason versus submission?

Baqillani's Reply: Impossibility in Power or Custom?
Baqillani responds to the objection by distinguishing impossibility in power vs. custom and using a reductio.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's strategy of distinguishing between impossibility in God's power and in custom, and his reductio argument.

Core Idea
If miracles are impossible only in custom, then the same reasoning would deny creation itself.

In this lesson, we examine how Baqillani responds to the objection. He first forces the deniers to clarify what they mean by impossible: impossible in God's power or in custom? He then shows the absurd consequences of their position if they say in custom.

Guided Path
1
Read Baqillani's response
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the two possibilities he presents.
2
Analyze the first option
If they say impossible in God's power, that is apostasy. Why?
Because it limits God's power.
3
Analyze the second option
If they say impossible in custom, Baqillani uses a reductio: they would have to deny creation itself.
He gives examples like Adam, chicken, egg.
4
Understand the conclusion
If they accept, they become materialists; if they reject, they abandon their argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قول آخر لمنكري الرسالة واستدلوا على إبطال الرسالة بأن قالوا : وجدنا المدعين للرسالة يزعمون أنه لا طريق إلى العلم بصدقهم إلا وجود محالات ممتنع في العقل وجودها من نحو فَلْقِ البحر وخَلْقِ ناقة من صخرة وقلب العصا حية وإحياء الموتى وإبراء الأكمه والأبرص والمشي على الماء وإنطاق الذئب والحصا وما جرى مجرى ذلك من ادعائهم جعل القليل كثيراً والقليل لا يتكثر كما أن الكثير لا يتقلل ويتوحد وإذا كان كذلك بَطَلَ ما يدعونه، فيقال لهم : ما الذي أردتم بقولكم إن هذه الأمور مستحيلة ممتنعة؟ أعنيتم بذلك أنها مستحيلة في العادة أو في قدرة الصانع تعالى؟ فإن قالوا: في قدرة الصانع ألحدوا وتركوا دينهم، وقيل لهم : ما الدليل على إحالة ذلك؟ وإن قالوا لأننا لم نجد أحداً فعله ولا يقدر عليه ولا رأينا ذلك قط ولا جرى مثل ما تدعون، قيل لهم : فيجب أن تحيلوا أيضاً أن يخلق الله تعالى الأجسام وألا يوجد آدم إلا من ذكر وأنثى وألا يخلق دجاجة إلا من بيضة أو بيضة إلا من دجاجة أو نطفة إلا من إنسان أو إنساناً إلا من نطفة لأن ذلك أجمع لم يوجد قط ولم يشاهد فإن مروا على ذلك لحقوا بأهل الدهر وإن أبوه نقضوا اعتلالهم
Another statement for the deniers of prophethood. They argued for the invalidation of prophethood by saying: We find the claimants to prophethood claiming that there is no way to know their truthfulness except by the existence of impossibilities that are impossible in reason to exist, such as splitting the sea, creating a she-camel from a rock, turning a staff into a snake, reviving the dead, healing the blind and the leper, walking on water, the speaking of the wolf and pebbles, and similar things, including their claim of making the little much, while the little cannot become much just as the much cannot become little, and it is confirmed [that it is impossible]. And if that is the case, what they claim is invalid. So it is said to them: What did you intend by your statement that these matters are impossible? Did you mean that they are impossible in custom or in the power of the Maker? If they say: in the power of the Maker, they have apostatized and abandoned their religion, and it is said to them: What is the proof of the impossibility of that? And if they say: because we have never found anyone who did it, nor is it possible for anyone, nor have we ever seen it, nor has anything like what you claim ever occurred, it is said to them: Then you must also consider impossible that God creates bodies, and that Adam came into existence except from a male and female, and that a chicken comes into existence except from an egg, or an egg except from a chicken, or a drop except from a human, or a human except from a drop, because all of that has never occurred nor been witnessed. If they accept that, they join the materialists; if they reject it, they have nullified their own argument.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer dialectic. The deniers argue that the miracles claimed by prophets are rationally impossible, so prophethood is false. Baqillani's response first clarifies the sense of impossibility: if they mean impossible in God's power, that is apostasy; if they mean impossible in custom, then the reply uses a reductio ad absurdum: by their own reasoning, they would have to deny the common origin of creatures from their sources (e.g., humans from humans, chickens from eggs) because they haven't witnessed the original creation. This forces them into the absurd position of either accepting atheism (ahl al-dahr) or abandoning their objection.

Key Terms
العادة
قدرة الصانع
أهل الدهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles are impossible because they break the laws of nature.
Correction: Baqillani shows that such impossibility is only in custom, not in God's power, and the argument leads to absurdity.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what happens if someone says miracles are impossible in God's power?
A) They are mistaken
B) They apostatize
C) They are ignorant
D) They are still Muslims

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's response shows that the denial of miracles based on custom leads to absurd conclusions, thereby defending the possibility of miracles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you read Baqillani's challenge to the opponents, do you feel the weight of logic? Which of your own deeply held assumptions might crumble if you subjected them to the same reductio? Write down one belief you hold based on 'how things always are' and ask yourself if it could be otherwise by God's will.
?
Baqillani warns that restricting God's power leads to apostasy. Is there any area of your life where you unconsciously act as if God cannot intervene — in your habits, your sins, your relationships? Acknowledge that limitation before Him and ask for a miracle of change.

Refuting the Objection on Prophets and Rational Forbiddances
Baqillani refutes the objection that a prophet cannot permit what reason forbids.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani begins to refute the claim that a true prophet cannot permit what reason forbids, by exposing a logical limitation in the objection.

Core Idea
A prophet's permission of irrational acts does not disprove all prophethood.

In this passage, Baqillani presents an objection from critics who argue that a prophet who permits acts reason deems evil cannot be from God. He then begins his response by pointing out a logical flaw: the objection only targets a particular claimant, not the entire concept of prophethood. This lesson examines the objection and the opening of Baqillani's refutation, noting that the full argument is cut off.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation to understand the claim: that a true prophet cannot permit what reason forbids, using examples like animal slaughter.
Notice the tone: the objectors present this as a decisive proof against all prophets.
2
Identify key terms
Focus on terms like 'محظور' (forbidden), 'عقل' (reason), 'إباحة' (permission). Understand how they frame the argument.
These terms are central to the debate about rational judgments.
3
Analyze Baqillani's initial response
Baqillani says the objection only proves the claimant might be false, not that no prophet can be sent with such permissions. This is a logical narrowing of the argument.
He uses the phrase 'ليس فيه ما يدل على أنه لا يجوز أن يرسل غير من ذكرتم'.
4
Reflect on the incomplete argument
The source text cuts off, so Baqillani's full refutation is not provided. Consider what might follow based on the opening response.
This lesson covers only the beginning of his rebuttal.

So what we have described indicates that they are not from Allah Almighty. Then it is said to them: The first thing in this is that what you have mentioned only entails that the permitter of these matters and the claimant of permission from Allah Almighty is a liar in his claim of prophethood, and that Allah Almighty cannot send him. The objectors claim that a true prophet cannot be sent with commands that reason deems evil, such as killing and using animals, because a wise God would not permit what reason forbids. Baqillani starts his answer by pointing out that the objection only proves that a particular claimant who brings such permissions might be lying, but it does not prove that God cannot send any prophet with such permissions. The argument is incomplete in the text, but the initial response is that the objection is too narrow. The full refutation is cut off.

The Opponent's Objection and the First Response
Baqillani presents an objection against prophets permitting what reason prohibits and gives the first part of his refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical flaw in the opponents' argument that a prophet cannot permit what reason prohibits, and how Baqillani limits the scope of their objection.

Core Idea
Objections against a specific prophet do not disprove prophethood in general.

Imam Baqillani presents a powerful objection from those who deny prophethood. They argue that since reason prohibits certain actions, a wise God would never permit them through a prophet. However, Baqillani's response shows that this argument only targets a particular claimant, not the institution of prophethood itself. Let us examine this exchange and learn how to distinguish between refuting a specific claim and rejecting an entire concept.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to how the opponents frame their evidence: they claim that intellect prohibits certain actions, and therefore a wise God cannot permit them through a prophet.
Notice the key terms: حظر (prohibition), إباحة (permission), عقل (reason).
2
Identify Baqillani's first response
Baqillani points out that the opponents' evidence only proves that the specific claimant who permits these acts is false. It does not prove that no prophet can be sent at all. This is a crucial logical distinction.
The argument only applies to a particular case, not to all prophets.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why Baqillani says that discussing specific prophets is pointless if you reject prophethood entirely. The real issue is whether prophethood is possible, not which individual is a prophet.
Debating details only makes sense after agreeing on the broader framework.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قول آخر لهم
وإن قالوا: الدليل على كذب مدعي الرسالة أنا وجدنا كل مدع تحضره العقول من إيلام الحيوان وذبحه وسلخه وتسخيره وغير ذلك مما يجرى مجراه والحكيم لا يجوز أن يبيح ما تحظره العقول ولا أن يبعث من يتكذب عليه في إطلاق ذلك وإباحته فدل ما وصفناه على أنهم ليسوا من عند الله سبحانه
فيقال لهم: أول ما في هذا أن الذي ذكرتموه إنما فيه أن يكون مبيح هذه الأمور ومدعي الإباحة على الله سبحانه كاذباً في ادعاء الرسالة وأن الله تعالى لا يجوز أن يرسله وليس فيه ما يدل على أنه لا يجوز أن يرسل غير من ذكرتم ولا من يبيح محظوراً في العقل ولا يحضر مباحاً فيه
فليس الكلام معكم في نبوة قوم بأعيانهم فإن الكلام في ذلك بين أهل الملل والمجوزين لإرسال الله تعالى الرسل، وأنتم تحيلون أن يرسل الله رسولاً أصلاً فلا معنى للكلام في تعيين رسالة فلان دون فلان فإنه خروج عن الكلام وعجز وانتقال من باب إلى باب
Another statement of theirs: And if they say: The evidence for the falsity of a claimant to the message is that we found every claimant whom intellects forbid—from inflicting pain on animals, slaughtering them, skinning them, subjugating them, and other things of that sort—and the Wise (God) cannot permit what intellects forbid, nor send one who lies about Him in permitting and allowing that; so what we have described indicates that they are not from God, exalted is He. Then it is said to them: The first thing in this is that what you have mentioned only entails that the permitter of these things and the claimant of permission from God, exalted is He, is lying in his claim to the message, and that God, exalted is He, cannot send him; but it does not contain evidence that He cannot send other than the one you mentioned, nor one who permits what is prohibited by reason, nor one who does not bring what is permitted in it. So the discussion with you is not about the prophethood of specific individuals, for the discussion about that is among the people of religions and those who allow the possibility of God, exalted is He, sending messengers; but you deem it impossible for God to send any messenger at all, so there is no point in specifying the message of so-and-so rather than so-and-so, for that is a departure from the discussion, an inability, and a shift from one chapter to another.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-response unit. It begins with an objection from opponents who argue that reason prohibits certain actions like inflicting pain on animals, slaughtering, skinning, etc. They claim that since these actions are prohibited by reason, a wise God cannot permit them through a prophet, and therefore anyone claiming prophethood who permits such things must be lying. Baqillani then gives the first part of his refutation. He points out that the opponent's argument only proves that such a specific claimant is false; it does not prove that no prophet can be sent at all. He further notes that the discussion about specific prophets only makes sense among those who accept the possibility of prophethood in general. Since the opponents reject prophethood entirely, engaging in debate about particular individuals is pointless—it is a departure from the real issue and a sign of weakness.

إباحة
عقل
رسالة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The opponent's argument proves that no prophet can permit what reason prohibits, thus all prophethood is false.
Correction: Baqillani clarifies that the argument only disproves a specific claimant who permits prohibited acts, not the possibility of prophethood in general.

C) The argument is based on a false premise about animals.
D) The argument contradicts the consensus of all religions.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's first response shows that an objection against a specific prophetic claim does not invalidate the entire concept of prophethood.

God's Right to Inflict Pain Without Compensation
Baqillani responds to an objection with a consensus argument and the grace-obligation distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's consensus-based argument that God's infliction of pain on animals is an act of grace, not an injustice requiring compensation.

Core Idea
God's actions toward animals are grace, not obligation; withholding grace is not injustice.

In this passage, Baqillani addresses a key objection from opponents who ask: what proof is there that God can cause pain to animals without any prior sin or compensation? He responds by appealing to a consensus among monotheists that God's blessings are acts of grace, and then draws a crucial distinction between grace and obligatory rights. This distinction establishes that God may withhold pleasure (i.e., inflict pain) without committing injustice.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation, noting the question from opponents and Baqillani's response. This is a standard objection-answer format.
The text ends mid-sentence in our copy, but the argument is clear up to that point.
2
Identify the consensus argument
Baqillani cites the agreement of Muslims and all monotheists that God is gracious and deserves praise. Understand why this consensus is used as a premise.
The term 'تفضل' (grace) is key here.
3
Understand the grace-obligation distinction
Baqillani distinguishes between grace (تفضل), which can be given or withheld without injustice, and obligatory right (مستحق واجب), which must be given. Grasp why this distinction is critical.
This distinction is central to the proof.
4
Consider the intended conclusion
Even though the Arabic ends abruptly, the logic suggests that since God's pleasures are grace, withholding them (causing pain) is permissible and not unjust. Reflect on how this argument answers the objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: فما الدليل على أن الله سبحانه ابتدأ الحيوان بالآلام من غير عوض ولا جرم تقدم؟ قيل لهم: الدليل على ذلك اتفاقنا وسائر أهل التوحيد وأهل الملل على أن الله تعالى متفضل على الحيوان بالنعم واللذات التي يبتدئهم بها وأنه مستوجب للحمد والشكر على ذلك وإذا كان هذا هكذا وكان للمتفضل فعل التفضل وله تركه على وجه ما كان له فعله، وأن هذا هو الفرق بين التفضل وبين المستحق الواجب الذي يجب الظلم بتركه ثبت أن الله سبحانه أن يترك فعل اللذة في الحيوان على وجه
Then if they say: What is the evidence that God, exalted is He, originally inflicted pains upon animals without compensation or prior offense? It is said to them: The evidence for that is our agreement and that of all the people of tawhid and the people of religions that God, exalted is He, is gracious to animals with the blessings and pleasures that He originally bestows upon them, and that He deserves praise and thanks for that. And when this is so, and the gracious one has the act of grace and its abandonment in the manner that He has the act, and that this is the difference between grace and the obligatory right whose abandonment would be injustice, it is established that God, exalted is He, may abandon the act of pleasure in the animal in a manner...
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage presents a fourth argument, framed as a question and answer. The opponents ask: What proof is there that God originally inflicts pain on animals without any prior sin or compensation? Baqillani answers using a consensus argument: Muslims and all monotheists agree that God is gracious (متفضل) to animals by giving them pleasures, and He deserves praise for that. Then he draws a distinction between grace (تفضل) and obligatory right (مستحق واجب). Grace is something one may either grant or withhold without injustice, whereas withholding an obligatory right would be unjust. Since God's bestowal of pleasures is an act of grace, He may also withhold it (i.e., inflict pain) without committing injustice. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the intended conclusion is that God's action is therefore permissible.

Key Terms
تفضل
مستحق واجب
عوض
جرم
اتفاق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God must always compensate for any pain He causes.
Correction: Baqillani argues that God's acts are graces, not obligations; therefore, He may withhold pleasures without compensation.

Checkpoint
What is the key distinction Baqillani uses to prove that God can inflict pain without compensation?
A) The distinction between obligatory and forbidden.
B) The distinction between grace and obligatory right.
C) The distinction between animals and humans.
D) The distinction between this world and the afterlife.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani uses the consensus that God's blessings are graces to show that withholding them (causing pain) is not unjust.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you have experienced pain or loss, have you ever secretly felt that God owes you something? How does this lesson's distinction between grace and obligation challenge that feeling? What will you actively do the next time such a thought arises?
?
In your relationships, do you treat your kindness to others as grace freely given, or do you expect gratitude and feel wronged when it's not reciprocated? How would your heart change if you saw every good act as pure grace, not an obligation?
?
If God's actions towards animals are entirely gracious, what does that imply for the pains you suffer? Will you commit today to trusting His wisdom and justice, even when you cannot see the reason? Write down one area of suffering where you will consciously practice this trust.

The Objection of Foolishness and the First Response
Baqillani presents an objection and its first refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that sending prophets to those known to reject is foolish, and Baqillani's first refutation that God can send prophets to those He knows will accept.

Core Idea
The charge of foolishness fails because God sends prophets to those who accept.

Baqillani addresses a common objection: if God knows someone will reject, sending a prophet seems foolish. He first points out that God can certainly send prophets to those He knows will accept and benefit, so the objection does not apply to them.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
The objectors argue that sending a prophet to someone known to reject is foolish, and since God is not foolish, He cannot send such prophets.
Focus on the term 'سفه' (foolishness).
2
Identify the first refutation
Baqillani responds that God can send prophets to those He knows will accept, because the charge of foolishness does not apply to them.
Notice he uses 'يجب جواز' to emphasize necessity of permissibility.
3
Understand the logical structure
The objection uses a general statement, but Baqillani shows it does not cover all cases, thus the conclusion is not universal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : الدليل على أنه لا يجوز في حكمة الله سبحانه إرسال الرسل أن إرساله الرسل إلى من يعلم أنه يكفر به ويشتمه ويرد قوله ويستوجب بذلك العقاب الأليم سَفَهُ وخلاف الصواب؟ فلما لم يجُزْ السِّفَهُ على الله سبحانه لم يجز أن يرسل الرسل إلى من حاله ما وصفنا فيقال لهم : أول ما في هذا أنه يجب جواز إرسال الله تعالى الرسل إلى من يعلم قبوله منهم وانتفاعه بهم لأن هذه العلة عنهم زائلة ثم يقال لهم : فيجب على اعتلالكم ألا يخلق الله سبحانه من يعلم أنه يكفر به ويجحد نعمه ويلحد في صفاته ولا ينتفع بوجود نفسه وألا يحتج بالعقول وما وضعه من الأدلة فيها على أحد علم أنه يجحدها ولا يستعملها ولا يُنيب إلى ما وضح في عقله حسنه، ولا يحذر مما حدر منه فإن مروا على ذلك تركوا دينهم وإن أبوه نقضوا اعتلالهم .
If they say: The proof that it is not permissible in the wisdom of God, exalted is He, to send messengers is that sending messengers to one whom He knows will disbelieve in Him, abuse Him, reject His word, and thereby deserve painful punishment is foolishness and contrary to correctness. Since foolishness is not permissible for God, exalted is He, it is not permissible that He send messengers to one whose state is as we described. Then it is said to them: The first thing in this is that it is necessary to permit the sending of God, exalted is He, of messengers to one whom He knows will accept from them and benefit from them because this cause is absent concerning them. Then it is said to them: According to your reasoning, it would be necessary that God, exalted is He, not create one whom He knows will disbelieve in Him, deny His blessings, and blaspheme His attributes, and not benefit from his own existence, and not argue through intellects and what He placed of proofs in them against anyone whom He knows will deny them and not use them and not incline to what is clearly good in his intellect, and not beware of what He warned against. If they continue on that, they abandon their religion, and if they refuse, they invalidate their reasoning.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes an objection against the possibility of God sending prophets to those He knows will reject them. The objectors argue that such action would be foolishness (سفه), which is impermissible for God. The author refutes in two steps. First, he points out that God can certainly send prophets to those He knows will accept and benefit, since the alleged cause (foolishness) does not apply to them. Second, he argues according to the objectors' own reasoning, it would follow that God should not create anyone He knows will disbelieve, nor give them intellects and proofs, since they will reject them. This would lead to absurd consequences. The author concludes that if the objectors accept this, they abandon their religion; if they reject it, they invalidate their own argument.

Key Terms
إرسال الرسل
سفه
حكمة الله
القبول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God cannot send prophets to those He knows will reject.
Correction: God can send prophets to those He knows will accept, so the objection does not prove a general impossibility.

Checkpoint
What is the first point Baqillani makes in refuting the objection about sending prophets?
A) God never sends prophets.
B) God can send prophets to those He knows will accept.
C) Prophets are unnecessary.
D) God does not know the future.

Key Takeaway
God can send prophets to those He knows will accept, so the objection does not disprove sending prophets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a person who rejects God's message, do you ever think their rejection makes God's sending of prophets pointless? How does this lesson challenge that thought and what responsibility does it place on you to be among the 'acceptors'?
?
Have you ever dismissed a teaching of Islam as 'foolish' because it seemed impractical or opposed to your desires? What is the root of that judgment, and how can you train yourself to submit to God's wisdom even when you don't fully understand?
?
The objector argues from 'wisdom' to limit God's actions. In your own life, do you use your limited understanding to judge what God should or should not do? How can you repent of that and instead trust His perfect wisdom?

The Absurd Consequence of the Objection
Baqillani presents a reductio ad absurdum argument against the objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's reductio ad absurdum argument that the objectors' reasoning would force God to refrain from creating disbelievers and giving them intellects, which is absurd.

Core Idea
The objectors' logic would force God to not create anyone who might disbelieve.

Baqillani then turns the tables: if God cannot send prophets to those He knows will reject, then by the same logic, He should not create such people at all, nor give them intellects and proofs. This absurdity invalidates their objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Baqillani draws out the consequences of the objectors' principle: if it is foolish to send prophets to rejecters, then it must also be foolish to create them or give them intellects.
Note the phrase 'فيجب على اعتلالكم' – 'according to your reasoning.'
2
Understand the reductio
The objectors would have to deny creation of disbelievers and the use of intellects, which is untenable.
This is a logical consequence, not a theological claim.
3
See the conclusion
The objectors are left with two choices: either accept the consequence (which abandons their religion) or reject their own premise.
The phrase 'فإن مروا على ذلك تركوا دينهم وإن أبوه نقضوا اعتلالهم' is the final verdict.
