Refuting Partial Acceptance of Prophets
Baqillani refutes the Brahamah who partially accept prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the Brahamah's own acceptance of some prophets to argue for the prophethood of all prophets via the same transmission evidence.

Core Idea
Accepting some prophets on transmitted miracles forces acceptance of all prophets on the same basis.

This passage shows a clever argument against a sect that picks and chooses prophets. Baqillani turns their own reasoning against them. By accepting Adam and Abraham based on transmitted miracles, they commit to a principle that also proves Moses, Jesus, and Muhammad. The lesson follows this dialectic.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the argument's flow.
Notice the footnote markers in parentheses; they indicate textual variants.
2
Identify the Brahamah's position
The Brahamah accept Adam and Abraham as prophets but reject later ones. Note that this is not a complete denial of prophethood.
This is important because they already accept the principle of prophethood.
3
Trace Baqillani's dialectical question
He asks for the evidence (dalil) for the prophethood of Adam and Abraham. The opponents respond with miracles (a'lam) transmitted by reliable people.
This is the same method they would use for later prophets.
4
See the refutation
Baqillani counters that the same transmission (naql) used for Adam and Abraham also exists for Moses, Jesus, and Muhammad. Thus, rejecting them is inconsistent.
The argument is analogous to that against the Jews.
5
Reflect on the lesson's core idea
The argument shows that partial acceptance based on transmitted miracles cannot be sustained without accepting all prophets with similar transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما المثبتون من البراهمة لنبوة آدم الجاحدون (١١) لمن بعده من الرسل (١١) والمثبتون لنبوة إبراهيم الجاحدون (١٢) لمن بعده بن (١٣) الرسل (١٤) فقد (١٥) أقروا بجواز إرسال الرسل وأنه (١٦) قد وُجِدَ (۱۷) ونُقل وإن خالفوا في نبوة قوم (۱۸) بأعيانهم وليس ذلك من قول مُحِيل الرسالة جُمْلَةً في شيء فيقال لهم : ما الدليل على إثبات نُبُوَّةِ آدَمَ وإبراهيم عليهما السلام (۱) ؟ فإن قالوا : ظهور الأعلام على أيديهما قيل لهم : وما الدليل على صحة هذه الأعلام ونحن لم نشاهدها ولا عاصرنا أصحابها؟ فإن قالوا : لنقل (٢) مَنْ يستحيل عليه الكذب لها عورضوا بمثل ذلك في نقل أعلام موسى وعيسى ومحمد وه عليهم السلام والكلام مع هؤلاء كالكلام مع اليهود وسنذكر منه ما يُنبى (٣) عن الحق إن شاء الله تعالى
As for those who affirm from the Brahamah the prophethood of Adam and deny (11) those after him of the messengers (11), and those who affirm the prophethood of Abraham and deny (12) those after him of (13) the messengers (14), they have (15) acknowledged the permissibility of sending messengers and that it (16) has occurred (17) and been transmitted, even if they disagree concerning the prophethood of a people (18) specifically. And that is not from the saying of one who entirely rejects the message in any way. So it is said to them: What is the evidence for establishing the prophethood of Adam and Abraham, peace be upon them (1)? If they say: the appearance of signs at their hands, it is said to them: And what is the evidence for the correctness of these signs while we did not witness them nor did we live contemporaneously with their people? If they say: by the transmission (2) of those whom it is impossible to lie about them, they are refuted by the like of that in the transmission of the signs of Moses, Jesus, and Muhammad, peace be upon them. And the discussion with these is like the discussion with the Jews, and we will mention from it what indicates (3) the truth, if God the Most High (1) wills.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical refutation (rada) of the Brahamah—a group that accepts some prophets (e.g., Adam, Abraham) but denies later ones (e.g., Moses, Jesus, Muhammad). The author first notes that these opponents have not completely rejected prophethood (risala) but have only denied specific individuals. This is important because it means they already accept the principle that God can send messengers and that reports of prophets exist. The author then engages them in a dialogue: He asks them for the evidence (dalil) for the prophethood of Adam and Abraham. If they reply that it is the miracles (a'lam) that appeared at their hands, the author presses further: What is the evidence for those miracles, given that we did not witness them? If they then appeal to the transmission (naql) of these miracles by people who cannot be suspected of conspiring to lie (man yastahil 'alayhi al-kadhib)—that is, tawatur—then the author counters that the same type of transmission exists for the miracles of Moses, Jesus, and Muhammad. Therefore, the argument against the Brahamah is identical to the argument against the Jews, and the author promises to elaborate what is correct on this subject later. The logical structure is a dilemma: either the opponent admits that tawatur is valid for Adam and Abraham, in which case it must also be valid for later prophets, or they must produce a different proof, which they cannot. This shows the inconsistency of accepting some prophets while rejecting others on the basis of the same type of evidence.

Key Terms
البراهمة
الأعلام
النقل
التواتر
الرد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Brahamah completely reject prophethood.
Correction: They accept some prophets (e.g., Adam, Abraham) but reject others, which is a weaker position that Baqillani exploits.

Checkpoint
How does the author refute the Brahamah who accept Adam but reject later prophets?
A) By proving that Adam's miracles are not transmitted.
B) By showing that the same transmission used for Adam also proves later prophets.
C) By arguing that the Brahamah are liars.
D) By comparing them to Christians.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani demonstrates that accepting some prophets based on transmitted miracles logically requires accepting all prophets for whom the same transmission exists.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what areas of your life do you accept God's guidance selectively, embracing what suits you but rejecting what challenges your comfort? What would it take for you to be consistent like Baqillani demands of the Brahamah?
?
When you hear the miracles of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) through transmitted reports, do you accept them with the same certainty as if you had witnessed them? If not, what does that hesitation reveal about the strength of your faith?
?
If the same evidence that proves the prophethood of Adam and Abraham also proves the prophethood of Muhammad, what prevents you from fully submitting to his message? Is it the evidence itself, or some resistance within you that you have not yet confronted?

The Jewish Challenge: Demanding Proof for Muhammad's Prophethood
Baqillani presents the chapter heading and the hypothetical objection demanding proof for Muhammad's prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific objection raised by opponents of Muhammad's prophethood and why Baqillani sets it up as a dialectical starting point.

Core Idea
Proving Muhammad's prophethood requires specific evidence, not just general arguments.

Baqillani opens his chapter on the Jews by presenting the key objection that any honest seeker must face: 'You have shown that God can send messengers, but what proves that Muhammad is one of them?' This objection separates the general possibility of prophethood from the specific claim. Understanding this challenge is essential to following Baqillani's refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how it combines a chapter heading with a hypothetical objection.
The heading names multiple groups: Jews, Magians, Sabians, Christians.
2
Identify the objection
What exactly does the questioner ask? Distinguish between the general permissibility of prophethood and the specific proof for Muhammad.
The objection uses 'fa-in qala qa'il' to introduce a hypothetical speaker.
3
Consider the opponents
Why are Jews, Magians, Sabians, and Christians mentioned? They all accept prophecy in principle but reject Muhammad's claim.
This shows Baqillani is addressing a broad audience of opponents who share common ground.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الكلام على اليهود (۱) في إثبات نبوة () محمد صلى الله () عليه (۸) والرد على من أنكرها وطعن فيها من المجوس والصابئة (٩) والنصارى فإن قال قائل : قد (١٠) دَلَلْتُم على جواز إرسال الله الرسل عليهم السلام (۱) فما (١٠) الدليل على إثبات نبوة نبيكم مع خلاف من يخالفكم (١٢)
Chapter on the discussion concerning the Jews (1) regarding the establishment of the prophethood of () Muhammad, may God bless () him (8) and the refutation of those who deny it and attack it from the Magians, the Sabians (9), and the Christians. For if someone says: You (10) have demonstrated the permissibility of God sending messengers, peace be upon them (1), so what (10) is the evidence for establishing the prophethood of your prophet, given the disagreement of those who oppose you (12)?
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a chapter heading (bab) followed by a hypothetical objection (fa'in qala qa'il). The chapter is titled 'The Discussion concerning the Jews' and its purpose is to establish the prophethood of Muhammad and to refute those who deny or attack it from among the Magians, Sabians, and Christians. After the heading, the author presents an objection that a questioner might raise: 'You have already proven that it is permissible for God to send messengers in general, so what is the specific evidence (dalil) for the prophethood of your prophet (Muhammad), especially given that many people disagree with you?' This objection sets up the need for a proof that is specific to Muhammad, not just a general proof of prophethood. The author will presumably answer this objection in the following pages, but here he merely states it. The inclusion of multiple groups (Jews, Magians, Sabians, Christians) indicates that the refutation is intended to address a broad range of opponents who accepted the possibility of prophecy in principle but denied Muhammad's claim. The objection is dialectically important because it forces the Muslim to produce evidence beyond general arguments for the possibility of prophethood.

Proof of Earlier Prophets through Transmitted Miracles
Refutation of an objection about unseen miracles for earlier prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the argument for the prophethood of Adam and Abraham through transmitted miracles is used to prove the prophethood of Muhammad.

Core Idea
If transmitted miracles prove Adam, they also prove Muhammad.

Imam Baqillani engages in a dialectical exchange with an opponent who questions how we can prove the prophethood of earlier prophets like Adam and Abraham. The opponent proposes that miracles are proof, but then questions their authenticity since they were not witnessed. Baqillani turns the argument around, showing that the same method of transmission applies to later prophets, including Muhammad. This passage teaches a powerful rebuttal by parity of reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the dialectical structure: question, objection, reply, counter-reply.
The passage is a condensed argument; take your time to follow the back-and-forth.
2
Identify the key objections
Find where the opponent challenges the proof of earlier prophets. Note how Baqillani responds by shifting the burden of proof.
3
Understand the parity argument
See how Baqillani applies the same standard to the transmission of miracles for all prophets. What is the logical conclusion?
This is the core of the lesson.
4
Reflect on the broader implication
Consider why this argument is effective against those who deny later prophethood while accepting earlier ones.
Think about the consistency required in accepting transmitted proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لهم : ما الدليل على إثبات نُبُوَّةِ آدَمَ وإبراهيم عليهما السلام؟ فإن قالوا : ظهور الأعلام على أيديهما قيل لهم : وما الدليل على صحة هذه الأعلام ونحن لم نشاهدها ولا عاصرنا أصحابها؟ فإن قالوا : لنقل من يستحيل عليه الكذب لها عورضوا بمثل ذلك في نقل أعلام موسى وعيسى ومحمد عليهم السلام والكلام مع هؤلاء كالكلام مع اليهود وسنذكر منه ما ينبئ عن الحق إن شاء الله تعالى.
To them: What is the proof for establishing the prophethood of Adam and Abraham, peace be upon them? For if they say: The appearance of miracles at their hands, it is said to them: And what is the proof for the authenticity of these miracles while we have not witnessed them nor were we contemporaries of their people? For if they say: (They were) transmitted by one for whom lying is impossible, they are confronted by the like of that in the transmission of the miracles of Moses, Jesus, and Muhammad, peace be upon them. And the discussion with these people is like the discussion with the Jews, and we will mention from it what indicates the truth, God willing.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and response in a dialectical format. The opponent asks how we can prove the prophethood of Adam and Abraham. The opponent suggests that miracles appearing at their hands are the proof. The author then questions the authenticity of those miracles since we did not witness them. The opponent replies that these miracles were transmitted by narrators who cannot possibly lie. The author refutes this by pointing out that exactly the same claim can be made for the transmission of miracles of Moses, Jesus, and Muhammad. Thus, if the opponent accepts the method of transmission for earlier prophets, they must also accept it for later ones. The author concludes that the discussion with these opponents is similar to the discussion with the Jews, and promises to present what indicates the truth.

Key Terms
نبوة
أعلام
نقل
معجزات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The prophethood of earlier prophets like Adam and Abraham cannot be proven because we did not witness their miracles.
Correction: The same method of reliable transmission that proves their miracles also proves the miracles of later prophets, including Muhammad.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of Baqillani's response to the objection about the prophethood of Adam and Abraham?

B) That the same method of transmitted miracles proves the prophethood of all prophets, including Muhammad
C) That the Jews are correct in denying Muhammad's prophethood
D) That miracles are not needed for prophethood

Key Takeaway
The same logical standard must apply: if transmitted miracles prove earlier prophets, they equally prove the prophethood of Muhammad.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Proof of Muhammad's Prophethood Through Miracles
The author proves Muhammad's prophethood by miracles and states their purpose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the primary proof of Muhammad's prophethood is the miracles (mu'jizat) that Allah manifested through him, and that these miracles serve to confirm his truthfulness and obligate belief.

Core Idea
Miracles are Allah's stamp of truth on His prophets.

In this passage, Imam Baqillani addresses the specific question: what is the proof for Muhammad's prophethood? After establishing that God can send messengers, he now provides the decisive evidence: the miracles that broke the laws of nature. He then explains why God performs such wonders—not for show, but to confirm the prophet's truthfulness and to demand our submission.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the question
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that the opponent asks: 'You have shown that God can send messengers—so what is the proof for your prophet specifically?'
This sets up the need for a concrete proof beyond mere possibility.
2
Understand the answer: miracles as proof
The author answers that the proof is the dazzling signs and overwhelming miracles that appeared at the prophet's hands. These are described as breaking custom and departing from nature.
These are called 'mu'jizat' (miracles) and are the central evidence.
3
Reflect on the purpose of miracles
The passage explains that Allah only performs miracles to indicate the truthfulness of the prophet, unveil his status, and obligate belief and obedience. This shows that miracles are not random but purposeful divine acts.
This connects the proof to its theological function.

Source Text

The passage concludes with the opponent asking for examples of these miracles, but the text cuts off with 'It is said: Matters...' before enumerating them.

Baqillani lists several miracles and states they are impossible for creatures.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
Miracles are divine acts beyond the power of any creature.

In this passage, Imam Baqillani lists a selection of the Prophet Muhammad's miracles, from the Qur'an to the glorification of pebbles. By stating that such events are impossible for creation, he underscores that only Allah can produce these signs, thereby establishing the truth of prophethood.

He then deduces that such events are impossible for any creature and can only come from the Creator. This reinforces the argument that miracles are divine acts that prove prophethood.

Objection to the Silence Argument
An objection that silence may indicate disagreement not acceptance, cut off.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that silence does not necessarily imply consent, and why this challenges Baqillani's argument from the Companions' silence.

Core Idea
Silence can conceal disagreement; it does not prove acceptance.

Baqillani argued that the Companions' silence about reported miracles indicated their acceptance. But an objector raises a crucial doubt: what if they remained silent despite opposing the claim? This lesson presents that objection in its own words, though the response is incomplete here. Understanding the objection is key to grasping the debate about the reliability of collective silence.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the objector frames the scenario: opponents who do not speak up despite believing a doctrine is false.
2
Identify the analogy
The objector compares the Companions' situation to that of later opponents who remain silent about a manifest doctrine. Ask yourself: is this a fair comparison?
3
Understand the challenge
The objection directly attacks the inference from 'silence' to 'acceptance.' If silence can be due to fear, prudence, or other reasons, then Baqillani's proof loses force.
This objection is a standard tool in kalam: undermining the necessary connection.
4
Note the incomplete state
The passage cuts off mid-sentence. Baqillani's response would follow, but it is missing here. Reflect on what a complete answer might need to address.
The objection alone shows the debate is not settled by a simple observation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل: أليس قد يجوز عندكم إمساك المخالفين عن القول والمذهب الظاهر فيهم مع خلافهم عليه واعتقادهم لفساده؟ فإن لم يدل إمساكهم على توثيقهم له واعتقادهم إياه فما أنكرتم أيضاً من مثل ذلك في الإمساك عما يدعى على الجماعات الكثيرة حضوره ومشاهدته إذا أمسكوا عن
For if someone says: 'Is it not permissible in your view for opponents to refrain from speaking against a doctrine that is manifest among them, despite their opposition to it and their belief in its corruption? For if their silence does not indicate their trust in it and their belief in it, then why do you not also deny the like of that in the case of silence regarding what is claimed of a large group's presence and witnessing when they remain silent about...'
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage presents an objection (i'tirad) to Baqillani's argument from the Companions' silence. The objector argues by analogy: it is possible for a group of people to remain silent about a matter they actually oppose and consider false. For example, scholars who disagree with a popular doctrine in their midst often remain silent out of fear or expediency, yet their silence does not imply endorsement. Similarly, the Companions' silence about transmitted miracles might not necessarily indicate their truth; they could have remained silent for other reasons. The text cuts off here, so Baqillani's answer is not included in this window. The objection challenges the inference that silence equals acceptance, and a full response would need to address the difference between the Companions' context and ordinary cases of dissent.

Key Terms
إمساك
مخالف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Silence always implies consent.
Correction: The objector shows that silence can also result from fear, prudence, or inability to respond, and does not necessarily indicate acceptance.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the objection presented in this passage?
A) That the Companions were not reliable.
B) That silence can occur even when people disagree with a claim.
C) That the miracles were not witnessed.
D) That tawatur is impossible.

Key Takeaway
The objection establishes that silence alone cannot prove acceptance; the context and motives for silence must be examined.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Refuting the Objection of Lost Objections
Baqillani answers the objection that the Companions' objections might have been lost.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani argues that the Companions' objections to miracle claims could not have been lost in transmission.

Core Idea
Prominent objections cannot be lost—they would be transmitted just as prominently.

Baqillani continues his defense of miracle transmission by anticipating a subtle objection: what if the Companions did object but their objections were not reported to us? This lesson unpacks his refutation, which rests on the principle that major events generate widespread transmission motives. The text also uses an analogy with the prophets Jesus and Moses to reinforce the point.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
The objector suggests that Companions might have denied the miracle reports but their denials were lost. Notice the phrasing: 'ما أنكرتم أن يكون الصحابة... قد أنكروا... وإن لم ينقل ذلك إلينا'
2
Identify Baqillani's refutation
He calls it false and gives a reason: such denial would have abundant motives for transmission. Find the key phrase 'توفر الدواعي على نقله'
3
Examine the analogy
He draws an analogy to Jesus and Moses: if their signs were countered, the counter would be transmitted. Reflect on why this supports his argument.
The analogy strengthens the claim by showing consistency across prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سؤال آخر على هذا الاستدلال. فإن قال قائل: فما أنكرتم أن يكون الصحابة أو كثير منهم قد أنكروا مشاهدة ما ادعاه الناقلون عليهم وسماعه وإن لم ينقل ذلك إلينا؟ قيل لهم: هذا باطل من قبل أن إنكار هذه الأعلام مما يجب توفر الدواعي على نقله وضبطه ومعرفة عين المعترض فيه ولفظه حتى يشتهر ذلك ويظهر وينشر وينقل نقل مثله ويجري مجرى الخبر الذي هو اعتراض عليه؛ وإنكار هذا واجب في مستقر العادة ووضعها. كما أن عيسى وموسى لو عورضا في نقل أعلامهما لوجب أن تنقل المعارضة كنقل الأمر
Another question on this inference. For if a speaker says: 'Why do you not allow that the Companions or many of them denied the witnessing of what the transmitters claimed upon them and their hearing of it, even if that was not transmitted to us?' It was said to them: 'This is false, because the denial of these indications (a'lam) is something for which the motives (dawa'i) must be abundant for its transmission and recording, and for knowing the very person of the objector and his wording, so that that becomes famous, apparent, and widespread, and transmitted like its like, and follows the course of the report (khabar) which is an objection against it; and the denial of this is obligatory in the established custom (mustaqarr al-ada) and its situation. Just as if Jesus and Moses were countered in the transmission of their signs (a'lam), it would be obligatory to transmit the counter-narrative (mu'arada) like the transmission of the matter.'
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is another objection-and-answer passage. The objector raises a new challenge: 'What if the Companions (sahaba) or many of them actually objected to the claim (the miracle report) but their objection was never transmitted to us?' The author (Baqillani) refutes this as false. The reason is that the denial (inkar) of such prominent miraculous signs (a'lam) would necessarily generate widespread motives (tawafur al-dawa'i) for its transmission and preservation. People would ensure that the objection is recorded, including the identity of the objector and his exact words, so that it becomes well-known, apparent, and transmitted like any other important report. Moreover, it is an obligation in the established custom (mustaqarr al-ada) to transmit such counter-narratives. The author draws an analogy: if the miracles of Jesus and Moses (peace be upon them) had been countered by contemporaries, those counter-narratives would have been transmitted just like the original reports. (The answer appears to continue beyond the page, but the core argument is presented.)

Key Terms
سؤال
استدلال
إنكار
أعلام
دواعي
عادة
معارضة
نقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that objections could be lost in transmission because we don't have records of every Companion's opinion.
Correction: Baqillani argues that due to the importance of these events, any objection would have been widely transmitted, and its absence proves it never occurred.

Checkpoint
Why does Baqillani consider the objection that the Companions' denial might not have been transmitted to be false?
A) Because the Companions never objected.
B) Because the denial of such signs would provoke abundant motives for transmission.
C) Because the transmitters would always hide objections.
D) Because only the reports of miracles are transmitted.

Key Takeaway
The absence of any reported objection from the Companions to a miracle claim is itself evidence that no such objection occurred, because any significant denial would have been transmitted.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a clear truth about Islam (like a miracle), do you find yourself secretly objecting in your heart? What would it mean if your internal objections were recorded for all to see?
?
Are you willing to be as transparent about your doubts as the Companions would have been? Is your silence evidence of faith or fear?
?
If your denial of a truth would be transmitted to future generations, would you still deny it? What does your silence today reveal about your commitment to the truth?

Refuting the Denial of Non-Muslims as Proof Against the Miracle
Baqillani refutes the objection from Jewish/Christian denial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam al-Baqillani argues that the denial of Jews and Christians does not invalidate the miraculous nature of the Quran.

Core Idea
Denial by unreliable witnesses does not disprove a miracle.

Imam al-Baqillani addresses a common objection: if the Quran were truly miraculous, why didn't the Jews and Christians of the time acknowledge it? He explains that their denial carries no weight because they were either absent from the events or were known liars. This passage teaches us how to evaluate the credibility of witnesses in theological arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once to get a feel for the argument. Don't worry about understanding every word yet.
The passage is a single sentence in the original, so pay attention to the logical connectors.
2
Identify the objection being refuted
What is the claim that Baqillani is responding to? He mentions 'denial of those who denied' – that is the objection that non-Muslims' rejection proves the miracle is false.
This is a classic dialectical argument: the opponent says 'if it were true, they would have believed'.
3
Analyze the two reasons given
Baqillani gives two scenarios: (1) the Jews and Christians were not present at most events, or (2) only a few were present and they are prone to lying and concealment. Understand why each makes their denial invalid as evidence.
4
Consider the conclusion
Since the deniers are not credible witnesses, the objection is baseless. Reflect on how this reasoning can be applied to similar objections today.
The conclusion is stated clearly: 'this objection becomes invalid with clear invalidity'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنواحي كخيبر وغيرها لم يجب أن يكون إنكار من أنكر ذلك من اليهود والنصارى حجة في إبطاله لأنهم إما ألا يكون حضر معه في أكثرها أحد منهم أصلاً أو أن يكون حضر منهم الواحد والاثنان والخمسة أو العدد الذي عليهم الكذب وعلى مثلهم افتعاله والكتمان لما [؟] وإذا كان ذلك كذلك بطل هذا الاعتراض بطلاناً ظاهراً.
And the areas like Khaybar and others, it is not necessary that the denial of those who denied that from the Jews and Christians be a proof for its invalidation, because either not one of them was present with him in most of them at all, or that one, two, five, or a number who are prone to lying and, like them, to fabrication and concealment of what [?] were present. And if that is so, this objection becomes invalid with clear invalidity.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an implied objection. The author, Imam al-Baqillani, addresses the claim that if the Quran's miraculous nature were true, even Jews and Christians would have acknowledged it. He argues that their denial is not a valid proof against the miracle because they were not reliable witnesses. First, many of the battles and events where the Prophet's miracles occurred (like the conquest of Khaybar) were not witnessed by Jews or Christians at all. Second, even if a few were present, they are people known for lying and concealing the truth. Therefore, their denial cannot be used as evidence to invalidate the miracle. The author concludes that the objection is baseless and clearly void.

Key Terms
إنكار (denial)
حجة (proof)
بطلان (invalidity)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The denial of the Quranic miracle by contemporary Jews and Christians proves that the miracle did not happen.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the deniers either were not present at the events or are unreliable witnesses, so their denial is not a valid proof.

Checkpoint
Why does Baqillani reject the objection from Jews and Christians regarding the Quranic miracle?
A) Because they were all hostile to the Prophet.
B) Because they were not present at most events or were few and prone to lying.
C) Because the Quranic miracle is self-evident and needs no witnesses.
D) Because Jews and Christians later accepted Islam.

Key Takeaway
Denial of a miracle by unreliable or absent witnesses does not invalidate the miracle's truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In this passage, Baqillani says the Jews and Christians denied the miracle either because they were not present or because they are prone to lying and concealment. When you find yourself doubting a clear truth from Allah—like the Quran's miraculousness—is it because you haven't truly witnessed it, or because your own desires make you conceal what you know? Which of these excuses is your heart using right now?
?
Baqillani dismisses the objection as 'clearly invalid.' But is there any objection about your faith that you secretly entertain—something you haven't fully settled in your heart? What would it look like for you to treat that objection the same way: to examine its source and, if it rests on unreliable grounds, to let it go with clear invalidity?
?
If the testimony of those who deny the truth is dismissed because of their unreliability, what about the testimony of your own actions? Do your daily habits and choices testify to the truth of Islam, or do they contradict what you claim to believe? What one change can you make today so that your life becomes a reliable witness to the truth?

Two Proofs of the Quranic Miracle
Baqillani enumerates the two aspects of the Quranic miracle and elaborates on the composition proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two aspects of the Quranic miracle as presented by Imam al-Baqillani: its unique composition and its reports of the unseen, and how these prove the Prophet's truthfulness.

Core Idea
The Quran's miracle is twofold: its unmatched eloquence and its hidden knowledge.

This passage from Imam al-Baqillani's Tamhid al-Awa'il establishes the foundational evidence for the Quranic miracle. He asserts that the Quran's appearance through the Prophet is known necessarily, but then answers an objection by detailing two independent proofs: the Quran's inimitable composition and its news of the unseen. This lesson unpacks the first proof in depth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two proofs
Read the opening of the passage to find the two ways the Quran indicates the Prophet's truthfulness. Note that Baqillani states them clearly.
2
Examine the composition proof
Study the detailed argument about the challenge to the Arabs. Notice how Baqillani emphasizes their inability despite their motivation.
3
Understand the role of illiteracy
Reflect on the verse from Surah al-Ankabut (48) cited at the end. Understand how the Prophet's illiteracy strengthens the miracle.
This is part of the composition proof, showing the Quran could not be humanly authored.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما العلم بظهور القرآن على يده ومجيئه من جهته فضرورة لا إشكال فيها ولا جدال. سمع وشوهد. فإن قال قائل: فما وجه دلالة ظهور القرآن على يده مما يدل على صدقه؟ قيل له: وجه ذلك من طريقين: أحدهما نظمه وبراعته والثاني ما انطوى عليه من أخبار الغيوب وعلمها. فأما الدلالة من جهة نظمه فهو أنا نعلم أنه صلى الله عليه وسلم تحدى العرب بأن تأتي بمثله في براعته وفصاحته وحسن تأليفه ونظمه وجزالته ورصانته وإيجازه واختصاره واشتمال اللفظ اليسير منه على المعاني الكثيرة ودعاهم إلى ذلك وطالبهم به في أيام المواسم وغيرها مجتمعين ومتفرقين فقال لهم في نص التلاوة: {قل لئن اجتمعت الإنس والجن على أن يأتوا بمثل هذا القرآن لا يأتون بمثله ولو كان بعضهم لبعض ظهيرا} [الإسراء: 88] يقول: موالياً معيناً. وقال: {فأتوا بعشر سور مثله مفتريات} [هود: 13]. وقال: {فأتوا بسورة من مثله} [البقرة: 23] مبالغة في تقريعهم بالعجز عنه مع عزة أنفسهم وعظم الأنفة وشدة الحمية والحرص على تكذيبه وتشتيت جمعه وتفريق الناس من حوله والتوفر على إكذابه وما يعره وغض منه وخروجهم إلى ما خرجوا إليه معه من الحرب والمسايفة وحمل الأنفس على إراقة الدماء والخروج عن الديار ومفارقة الأوطان. فلو كانوا مع ذلك قادرين على معارضته أو معارضة سورة منه لسارعوا إلى ذلك، ولكان أهون عليهم وأخف من نصب الحرب معه والجلاء عن الأوطان وتحمل الأهوال والصبر على القتل وألم الجراح واحتمال الذل والعار؛ لأنه قد كان عليه السلام مكنهم من تكذيبه من وجهين: أحدهما قوله: {لن تأتوا بمثله}، والآخر قوله: {إن أتيتم فلجتم وكنت مبطلاً وكنتم المحقين}، هذا مع تلاوته عليهم في نص التنزيل قوله: {وما كنت تتلو من قبله من كتاب ولا تخطه بيمينك إذا لارتاب المبطلون} [العنكبوت: 48]. ولو عرفوه بذلك أو بصحبة أهل الكتب ونقلة السير ومداخلة أهل الأخبار ومجالسة أهل هذا الشأن لم يلبثوا أن يقولوا له: هذا كذب، لأنك ما زلت معروفاً بصحبة أهل الكتب ومجالستهم وقصدهم إلى مواضعهم ومواطنهم ومجاراتهم والأخذ عنهم والاستفادة منهم.
As for the knowledge of the appearance of the Quran at his hand and its coming from his direction, it is a necessity with no ambiguity in it and no dispute. It was heard and witnessed. If a sayer says: What is the aspect of the evidence of the appearance of the Quran at his hand that indicates his truthfulness? It is said to him: The aspect of that is from two ways: one is its composition and eloquence, and the second is what it contains of reports of the unseen and their knowledge. As for the evidence from the aspect of its composition, it is that we know that he, peace and blessings be upon him, challenged the Arabs to bring something like it in its eloquence, its fluency, its good arrangement, its composition, its grandeur, its solidity, its conciseness, its brevity, and the inclusion of its few words for many meanings. He called them to that and demanded it from them in the seasons and other times, gathered and scattered. He said to them in the text of recitation: {Say: If mankind and jinn gathered to produce the like of this Quran, they could not produce its like, even if they were helpers of one another} [Al-Isra: 88] – meaning allies and assistants. And He said: {Then bring ten surahs like it, fabricated} [Hud: 13]. And He said: {Then bring a surah like it} [Al-Baqarah: 23] – exaggerating in rebuking them for their inability, despite their pride of souls, greatness of arrogance, intensity of zeal, eagerness to deny him, scatter his assembly, disperse people from around him, to refute him and to dishonor and diminish him, and their embarking on war and sword-fighting with him, and exposing their souls to bloodshed, leaving homes, and parting from homelands. If they were, despite that, able to oppose it or oppose a surah from it, they would have hastened to that, and it would have been easier for them and lighter than waging war with him, exile from homelands, enduring terrors, patience in killing, the pain of wounds, bearing humiliation and shame; because he, peace be upon him, enabled them to deny him in two ways: one is his saying: {You will never bring its like}, and the other is his saying: {If you bring it, you would prevail and I would be false and you would be truthful}. This is with his recitation upon them in the text of revelation of His saying: {And you did not recite before it any book, nor did you write it with your right hand, for then the falsifiers would have doubted} [Al-Ankabut: 48]. And if they had known him by that or by companionship with the people of the scriptures, the transmitters of biographies, the frequenting of the people of reports, and sitting with the people of this matter, they would not have delayed to say to him: This is a lie, because you have always been known for companionship with the people of the scriptures, sitting with them, going to their places and homelands, conversing with them, and taking from them and benefiting from them.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive proof of the Quranic miracle (I'jaz al-Quran) as evidence of the Prophet's truthfulness. It begins by asserting that the knowledge of the Quran's appearance through the Prophet is a necessary knowledge, beyond doubt or dispute, as it was heard and witnessed. Then it presents a hypothetical objection: 'How does the Quran's appearance indicate his truthfulness?' The answer is given through two aspects: (1) the Quran's composition and eloquence (nazm), and (2) its news of the unseen (akhbar al-ghuyub). The author then elaborates on the first aspect in detail. He states that the Prophet challenged the Arabs to produce something similar in its eloquence, fluency, arrangement, grandeur, conciseness, and the inclusion of many meanings in few words. This challenge was issued during seasons and gatherings. The Quranic verses of challenge are cited: Surah Al-Isra 88, Hud 13, and Al-Baqarah 23. The author emphasizes that despite the Arabs' extreme pride, zeal, and eagerness to discredit the Prophet, and despite their willingness to go to war and endure hardships, they could not produce a single surah like it. If they had been able, they would have chosen that much easier path instead of war and exile. Moreover, the Prophet gave them two ways to prove him wrong: either produce the like, or if they succeed, they would be victorious. Additionally, the Prophet's illiteracy (ummah) is cited from Surah Al-Ankabut 48 – he never read a book nor wrote with his hand, so he could not have learned from previous scriptures. If the Arabs had known him to be associated with scholars of scriptures, they would have accused him of learning from them, but they did not, because he was known to be unlettered. This further solidifies the divine origin of the Quran.

Key Terms
تحدى (challenge)
نظم (composition)
براعة (eloquence)
أخبار الغيوب (news of the unseen)
إعجاز (miracle)
أمية (illiteracy)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Quran's miracle is only its style and eloquence.
Correction: Baqillani explicitly includes the news of the unseen as a separate and independent proof, not just style.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what two aspects constitute the Quranic miracle as proof of prophethood?
A) Its rhythm and rhyme.
B) Its composition/eloquence and its reports of the unseen.
C) Its legal rulings and its historical accuracy.
D) Its length and its memorization.

Key Takeaway
The Quran's miracle is established through both its unmatched literary excellence and its supernatural knowledge of the unseen, proving the Prophet's truthfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Quran's eloquence is a clear proof of its divine origin, why do you still find yourself neglecting its recitation? What excuse do you have for not connecting with it daily?
?
The Prophet's illiteracy proves the Quran is from God. How does this truth impact your trust in every word of the Quran, especially when it commands you to change your life?
?
The Arabs were willing to fight and die rather than admit the truth. Are there areas in your life where you resist God's guidance even though you know it's true? What will you do today to submit fully?

Prophethood

The Arabs' Inability to Match the Quran
Baqillani argues the Arabs' failure to oppose the Quran is a miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Arabs' avoidance of opposing the Quran, despite their eloquence and motivation, serves as the greatest proof of the Prophet's truthfulness.

Core Idea
The greatest proof of prophethood is the Arabs' silence against the Quran.

Baqillani begins by highlighting a striking historical fact: the Arabs, masters of eloquence, made no attempt to produce a surah like the Quran. This avoidance, given their ability and incentive, is a powerful sign of its divine origin. Let's explore his reasoning and see why this is considered a miracle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice how Baqillani emphasizes the Arabs' knowledge of the Quran's unique composition.
2
Identify the two key observations
The passage makes two points: 1) the Arabs avoided opposing the Quran, 2) the Quran's composition differs from all human speech. Identify these in the text.
These two observations together form the miracle.
3
Understand why this proves truthfulness
Reflect on why their avoidance is a proof: if they could have matched it, they would have, since they wanted to refute the Prophet. Their failure shows it is beyond human capacity.
This is the core of the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي صرفهم عن هذا أجمع وعن تكلف معارضة سورة منه أو إيراد ما قل وكثر من ذلك مع علمهم بخروج نظم القرآن عن سائر أوزان كلامهم ونظومهم أعظم دليل على صدقه صلى الله عليه وسلم. وأن ظهور القرآن وهو نشأ معهم وبين أظهرهم ولم يعرفوه بقصد أهل الكتاب ومجالسة غير من لقوه وعرفوه والاقتباس منه ولا انفرد بمداخلة فصيح منهم ومتقدم في البراعة واللسن عليهم آية عظيمة وأمر خارق للعادة لأن مثل ذلك لا يكتسب بتعلم وتدقيق ذكاء وفطنة ولطيف حس وحيلة. وأنه يبيت عليه السلام وهو غير عالم بلغة ذلك ولا فرق بين الزنج والترك وغيرهما من اللغات ثم يصبح أفصح الناس بكل لغة منها وأجرأهم فيها مع العلم بأنه لم يأخذ ذلك عن أهلها لأن خلق العلم فيه بذلك وإقداره عليه في يسير الوقت خرق للعادة وخارج عما عليه بناء الطبيعة. وكذلك تعلم هذه اللغات واكتساب معرفتها والتمكن من علمها وتحصيلها في يسير الوقت الذي لا يكتسب في مثله العلم بعظيم ما جاء به آية عظيمة وخرق للعادة. فإنزال هذا الكلام عليه واضطراره إلى إجراء لسانه أو خلق لطيفة يتمكن بها من إدراك هذا النظم ورصفه وبيانه من أظهر الآيات وأبين الدلالات لأن التمكن من تعلم ذلك بكل لطيفة في يسير الوقت مما لم تجر العادة بمثله نقض لها. والله سبحانه لا يظهر الآيات إلا لما ذكرنا من القصد إلى الدلالة على صدق الرسل عليهم السلام.
And in their avoidance of this altogether and their refraining from attempting to oppose a surah of it or to produce something like it, whether little or much, despite their knowledge that the composition of the Quran departs from all the meters of their speech and their compositions, is the greatest proof of his truthfulness, peace be upon him. And that the appearance of the Quran while he grew up among them and in their midst, and they did not know him to have sought out the People of the Book or to have sat with others he met and knew and to have borrowed from them, nor did he alone engage with any eloquent speaker among them or one advanced in eloquence and fluency, is a great sign and a matter that breaks custom, because such a thing cannot be acquired by learning or by the precisity of intelligence, acumen, subtle sense, or cunning. And that he, peace be upon him, goes to sleep while not knowing the language of that people—and there is no difference between the Zanj, the Turks, and other languages—then he wakes up as the most eloquent of people in every language among them and the most fluent, while it is known that he did not acquire that from its people, because the creation of knowledge in him of that and enabling him to do it in a short time is a break in custom and outside what nature is based upon. And similarly, learning these languages, acquiring knowledge of them, mastering their science, and obtaining them in a short time in which knowledge of the great thing he brought is not normally acquired, is a great sign and a break in custom. So the sending down of this speech upon him and his being compelled to utter it, or the creation of a subtle faculty by which he can grasp this composition, its arrangement, and its clarity, is among the clearest signs and most evident indications, because the ability to learn that by every subtle faculty in a short time—whose like custom does not entail—is a violation of it. And God, exalted be He, only shows signs for what we have mentioned of the intention to indicate the truthfulness of the messengers, peace be upon them.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage presents two interconnected arguments for the miraculous nature of the Quran and the prophethood of Muhammad (PBUH). First, Baqillani notes that the Arabs, despite being masters of eloquence and having every motive to refute the Prophet, avoided attempting to produce anything like the Quran altogether. This avoidance, coupled with their knowledge that the Quran's composition surpasses all known poetic meters, is the greatest proof of his truthfulness. Second, he argues that the Prophet himself could not have acquired such eloquence through human means: he grew up among them without studying with scholars or practicing with experts, and his sudden mastery of languages—illustrated by the hypothetical of his going to sleep ignorant of a language and waking up fluent—breaks the natural course of things. Baqillani emphasizes that such acquisition in a short time is not possible by ordinary learning, intelligence, or cunning. He concludes that the very revelation of this speech and the Prophet's ability to articulate it, whether by direct inspiration or by a divinely created faculty, is among the most evident signs. Finally, he states a general principle: God only produces such miracles to prove the truthfulness of His messengers.

Key Terms
صرفهم عن المعارضة
نظم القرآن
أعظم دليل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the greatest proof of the Prophet's truthfulness?
A) The Arabs' production of similar poetry
B) The Arabs' avoidance of opposing the Quran despite their ability and knowledge
C) The Prophet's own eloquence
D) The length of the Quran

Key Takeaway
The Arabs' failure to match the Quran, despite their eloquence, is a clear miracle proving the Prophet's truthfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Arabs, the most eloquent people, could not produce a surah like the Quran. You have heard its challenge—have you ever truly let its words confront your own resistance? What would it take for you to surrender completely to its authority today?
?
The Prophet was not trained in eloquence, yet he brought a book that silenced experts. Do you use your own lack of knowledge or background as an excuse to avoid living the Quran? What one verse will you memorize and act upon this week, despite feeling inadequate?
?
Baqillani says the Arabs' failure is the 'greatest proof.' If you already believe this, why are there still areas of your life where you live as if the Quran is merely advice rather than the decisive word? Name one habit you will change this week to treat the Quran as your ultimate authority.

The Prophet's Miraculous Eloquence and Language Acquisition
Baqillani details the Prophet's miraculous acquisition of eloquence and languages.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's sudden mastery of languages and eloquence, without human instruction, constitutes a clear miracle and proof of prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's overnight fluency in any language is a divine miracle.

Baqillani extends his argument by focusing on the Prophet himself. He presents a striking image: the Prophet goes to bed unaware of a language and wakes up as its most eloquent speaker. This complete transformation in a short time defies all natural laws of learning. Let's see how this becomes another clear sign of his prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the Prophet's language acquisition
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the hypothetical example of the Zanj and Turks to illustrate the point.
2
Analyze the two scenarios
The passage describes two intertwined miracles: 1) the Prophet's sudden fluency in any language, and 2) the revelation of the Quran itself. Identify both.
Both are presented as breaks in custom.
3
Connect to the general principle
At the end, Baqillani states that God only shows such miracles to prove the truthfulness of messengers. Understand this as the overarching purpose.
This ties the entire argument together.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي صرفهم عن هذا أجمع وعن تكلف معارضة سورة منه أو إيراد ما قل وكثر من ذلك مع علمهم بخروج نظم القرآن عن سائر أوزان كلامهم ونظومهم أعظم دليل على صدقه صلى الله عليه وسلم. وأن ظهور القرآن وهو نشأ معهم وبين أظهرهم ولم يعرفوه بقصد أهل الكتاب ومجالسة غير من لقوه وعرفوه والاقتباس منه ولا انفرد بمداخلة فصيح منهم ومتقدم في البراعة واللسن عليهم آية عظيمة وأمر خارق للعادة لأن مثل ذلك لا يكتسب بتعلم وتدقيق ذكاء وفطنة ولطيف حس وحيلة. وأنه يبيت عليه السلام وهو غير عالم بلغة ذلك ولا فرق بين الزنج والترك وغيرهما من اللغات ثم يصبح أفصح الناس بكل لغة منها وأجرأهم فيها مع العلم بأنه لم يأخذ ذلك عن أهلها لأن خلق العلم فيه بذلك وإقداره عليه في يسير الوقت خرق للعادة وخارج عما عليه بناء الطبيعة. وكذلك تعلم هذه اللغات واكتساب معرفتها والتمكن من علمها وتحصيلها في يسير الوقت الذي لا يكتسب في مثله العلم بعظيم ما جاء به آية عظيمة وخرق للعادة. فإنزال هذا الكلام عليه واضطراره إلى إجراء لسانه أو خلق لطيفة يتمكن بها من إدراك هذا النظم ورصفه وبيانه من أظهر الآيات وأبين الدلالات لأن التمكن من تعلم ذلك بكل لطيفة في يسير الوقت مما لم تجر العادة بمثله نقض لها. والله سبحانه لا يظهر الآيات إلا لما ذكرنا من القصد إلى الدلالة على صدق الرسل عليهم السلام.
And in their avoidance of this altogether and their refraining from attempting to oppose a surah of it or to produce something like it, whether little or much, despite their knowledge that the composition of the Quran departs from all the meters of their speech and their compositions, is the greatest proof of his truthfulness, peace be upon him. And that the appearance of the Quran while he grew up among them and in their midst, and they did not know him to have sought out the People of the Book or to have sat with others he met and knew and to have borrowed from them, nor did he alone engage with any eloquent speaker among them or one advanced in eloquence and fluency, is a great sign and a matter that breaks custom, because such a thing cannot be acquired by learning or by the precisity of intelligence, acumen, subtle sense, or cunning. And that he, peace be upon him, goes to sleep while not knowing the language of that people—and there is no difference between the Zanj, the Turks, and other languages—then he wakes up as the most eloquent of people in every language among them and the most fluent, while it is known that he did not acquire that from its people, because the creation of knowledge in him of that and enabling him to do it in a short time is a break in custom and outside what nature is based upon. And similarly, learning these languages, acquiring knowledge of them, mastering their science, and obtaining them in a short time in which knowledge of the great thing he brought is not normally acquired, is a great sign and a break in custom. So the sending down of this speech upon him and his being compelled to utter it, or the creation of a subtle faculty by which he can grasp this composition, its arrangement, and its clarity, is among the clearest signs and most evident indications, because the ability to learn that by every subtle faculty in a short time—whose like custom does not entail—is a violation of it. And God, exalted be He, only shows signs for what we have mentioned of the intention to indicate the truthfulness of the messengers, peace be upon them.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage presents two interconnected arguments for the miraculous nature of the Quran and the prophethood of Muhammad (PBUH). First, Baqillani notes that the Arabs, despite being masters of eloquence and having every motive to refute the Prophet, avoided attempting to produce anything like the Quran altogether. This avoidance, coupled with their knowledge that the Quran's composition surpasses all known poetic meters, is the greatest proof of his truthfulness. Second, he argues that the Prophet himself could not have acquired such eloquence through human means: he grew up among them without studying with scholars or practicing with experts, and his sudden mastery of languages—illustrated by the hypothetical of his going to sleep ignorant of a language and waking up fluent—breaks the natural course of things. Baqillani emphasizes that such acquisition in a short time is not possible by ordinary learning, intelligence, or cunning. He concludes that the very revelation of this speech and the Prophet's ability to articulate it, whether by direct inspiration or by a divinely created faculty, is among the most evident signs. Finally, he states a general principle: God only produces such miracles to prove the truthfulness of His messengers.

Key Terms
خرق العادة
خلق العلم
آية عظيمة
اضطراره إلى إجراء لسانه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the Prophet's eloquence was purely a natural gift or acquired through study.
Correction: The passage insists it was miraculously created by God in an instant, without any human learning process.

Checkpoint
What does the passage say about the Prophet waking up after sleeping?
A) He would forget the language he knew
B) He would become the most eloquent speaker in a language he previously did not know
C) He would speak in a new accent
D) He would need time to practice

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's sudden mastery of languages and the revelation of the Quran are clear miracles, proving his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If the Prophet's overnight language mastery is a sign of his truth, does your response to his message reflect that conviction? What would change if you truly believed the Quran is a miracle that demands your full obedience?
?
God only shows miracles to prove His messengers. That means you have enough evidence for faith. If you still waver, what deeper resistance in your heart is preventing you from fully submitting? Will you repent from that today?

Refuting the Objection that the Quran is Mere Human Speech
Baqillani answers the objection that the Quran could be excellent human speech and proves its miraculous nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes the objection that the Quran is merely excellent human speech by showing it exceeds the limits of human skill and belongs to a unique genre.

Core Idea
The Quran exceeds all human capacity and defies genre—proof of its divine origin.

In this passage, Baqillani addresses a common objection from non-Muslims: that the Quran is simply extraordinarily eloquent human speech. He systematically dismantles this by showing that the Quran surpasses any possible human achievement and does not fit any known Arabic literary form. This establishes the Quran as a miracle.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the structure: an objection followed by two arguments.
The objectors suggest Muhammad's high eloquence could naturally produce the Quran.
2
Analyze the first argument
Identify Baqillani's claim that human skill has a known limit that does not break custom. The Arabs' inability to produce anything like the Quran despite intense motivation shows it is beyond ordinary skill.
This argument uses the concept of 'breaking custom' (kharq al-‘adah) to identify a miracle.
3
Analyze the second argument
Notice Baqillani's second point: the Quran is composed on a meter that does not match any known Arabic poetic or rhetorical form. If it were human, its genre would be recognizable.
The unique meter demonstrates the Quran is not from any known human composition.
4
Consider the evidence from Quraysh
Reflect on how Quraysh, the most eloquent Arabs, were utterly confused—calling the Quran magic, legends, etc. Their inability to classify it confirms its miraculous nature.
Conflicting accusations indicate they were at a loss.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالت اليهود والنصارى ما أنكرتم أن يكون ما أتى به النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من جنس كلامهم، غير أنه كان أفصح وأوجز وأحسن نظماً وأن يكون ذلك إنما تأتى له بتقدمه في البلاغة عليهم وحسن فصاحته ولَسَنهِ وبَرَعَهم بذلك وزاد فيه على جميعهم؟ قيل لهم : إن قدر ما يقتضيه التقدم والحذق في الصناعة قدر معروف لا يخرق العادةَ مِثلُه ولا يعجز أهل الصناعة والمتقدمون فيها عنه مع التحدي والتقريع بالعجز والقصور لأن العادة جارية بجمع الدواعي والهمم على بلوغ منزلة الحاذق المتقدم في الصناعة وما أتى به النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم من القرآن قد خرج عن حد ما يُكتسب بالحذق وعجز القوم عن معارضته ومقابلته مع إيثارهم لذلك واجتماع هممهم له وتوفر دواعيهم عليه وعلمهم بجعله حجة له ودلالة على صدقه فخرج بذلك عن نمط ما سألتم عنه. وعلى أن الآية في القرآن أنه منزل بلسان العرب وكلامهم ومنظوم على وزن يفارق سائر أوزان كلامهم ولو كان من بعض النظوم التي يعرفونها لعلموا أنه شعر أو خطابة أو رَجَزٌ أو طويل أو مزدوج غير أن ناظمه قد برع وتقدم فيه وليس يُخرج الحذقُ في الصنعة إلى أن يؤتي بغير جنسها وما ليس منها في شيء وما لا يعرفه أهلها وإذا كان ذلك كذلك وكنا نعلم أن قريشاً أفصح العرب وأعرفها باللسان وأقدرها على سائر أوزان الكلام وأنها قد دهِشَت وطاشت عقولها فيما أتى به فقالت مرة إنه سحر، وقالت تارةً إنه معلم مجنون، وقالت أخرى أساطير الأولين
If the Jews and Christians say: 'What do you deny that what the Prophet, peace be upon him, brought is from the same genus as their speech, except that it was more eloquent, more concise, and better in composition, and that this was only achieved by his surpassing them in eloquence and the excellence of his fluency and his excelling them thereby and surpassing all of them?' Say to them: 'Indeed, the extent that is required by being advanced and skilled in a craft is a known extent; its like does not break custom, and the people of the craft and those advanced in it are not incapable of it when challenged and reproached for inability and deficiency, because custom runs that motives and efforts combine to reach the station of the skilled and advanced in the craft. But what the Prophet, peace be upon him, brought of the Quran has gone beyond the limit of what is acquired by skill, and the people were incapable of opposing it and matching it despite their preference for that, their combined efforts, their abundant motives, and their knowledge that he made it a proof for him and an indication of his truthfulness. So it thereby departed from the category of what you asked about. And also: The sign in the Quran is that it is revealed in the language of the Arabs and their speech, and composed on a meter that departs from all the meters of their speech. If it were one of the compositions they knew, they would know that it is poetry, oratory, rajz, a long meter, or a double meter, except that its composer had excelled and advanced in it. But skill in a craft does not produce something outside its genus and entirely unrelated to it and unknown to its practitioners. Since that is so, and we know that Quraysh were the most eloquent of the Arabs, the most knowledgeable of the language, and the most capable of all the meters of speech, and that they were bewildered and their minds were confounded by what he brought, saying sometimes it is magic, sometimes that he is a taught madman, and at other times legends of the ancients'.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objectors (Jews and Christians) propose that the Quran might simply be excellent human speech, with Muhammad being exceptionally eloquent and surpassing all others in rhetoric. Baqillani responds with two arguments. First, he argues that human skill in a craft has a known limit that does not break custom; normally, others can eventually catch up or at least rival it when challenged. But the Quran exceeds that limit entirely—the Arabs, despite their intense desire to refute him, their combined efforts, and their knowledge that he used the Quran as a proof, were utterly unable to produce anything comparable. This places the Quran outside the category of ordinary human achievement. Second, Baqillani points to the unique composition of the Quran: it is in Arabic but on a meter that does not match any known form of their speech (poetry, oratory, rajz, long meters, double meters). If it were within their genres, they would have identified it. Their failure to classify it, and their contradictory accusations (magic, teaching, myths), prove their confusion. Since Quraysh were the most eloquent and knowledgeable, their inability and confusion demonstrate that the Quran is a miracle, not merely excellent human speech.

التحدي
المعارضة
خرق العادة
وزن يفارق

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that extraordinary human eloquence could be mistaken for divine revelation.
Correction: The passage shows the Quran is categorically beyond human capacity and genre, as evidenced by the Arabs' failure and confusion.

Checkpoint
What is the second argument Baqillani uses to refute the objection that the Quran is merely excellent human speech?
A) The Quran is too long to be human composition
B) The Quran is composed on a meter that does not belong to any known genre of Arabic speech
C) The Arabs did not try to oppose it
D) The Prophet was illiterate

Key Takeaway
The Quran's inimitability is established by its surpassing of human capacity and its unique form, proving it is a divine miracle.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you treat the Quran as a human book, worthy of study but not of absolute submission? When you read it, do you feel the awe of its divine origin, or do you analyze it as a mere literary text? What would change in your life if you truly believed every word is from Allah?
?
The Arabs were bewildered and resorted to contradictory accusations when faced with the Quran. In your moments of doubt, have you ever made excuses—'this is too difficult, I can't understand, it's old stories'—to avoid its demands on your life? Will you now stop hiding behind such excuses and submit to its truth?
?
Baqillani argues that human skill has limits. Have you ever felt that your own intellect or effort is sufficient to understand Islam without divine guidance? The Quran is beyond human comprehension—are you humble enough to approach it with surrender, not arrogance?

Rebuttal of the Fear Argument for Mu'arada
Baqillani refutes the claim that fear prevented transmission of the challenge to the Qur'an.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the fear of the sword cannot explain the absence of transmitted challenges to the Qur'an, and how Baqillani extends this reasoning to defend all prophetic miracles.

Core Idea
Fear cannot block transmission if it does not block the claim itself.

Baqillani confronts a common objection: that the Prophet's opponents were too afraid to transmit any successful challenge to the Qur'an. He shows this argument is self-defeating and then extends it by analogy to earlier prophets. Let's read his refutation carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing deeply. Then read the literal translation to grasp the argument flow.
Notice the compact style and the structure of the argument.
2
Identify Baqillani's main argument
Baqillani points out that if fear prevented transmission, it would also prevent the claim of opposition itself. Yet opponents did claim opposition, so fear alone cannot explain the absence of transmitted challenges.
This is the core logical point.
3
Notice the analogy with Moses and Jesus
Baqillani extends the argument by analogy: if the fear argument were valid, it would apply equally to the miracles of Moses and Jesus, leading to absurd consequences.
This strengthens the refutation by parity of reasoning.
4
Consider the implications
The argument is not limited to the Qur'an but defends all prophetic miracles. Reflect on how this reinforces the inimitability of revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السيف مانعاً ذلك نقلاً ظاهراً، ويقع تفصيله والنص عليه والبيان له من كل رجل بعينه وإذا كنا لا نعلم وجود المعارضة للقرآن كعلمنا لظهوره من جهة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وجب سقوط ما قالوا وأيضاً فلو كان الخوف من نقلهم المعارضة لمنع ذلك أيضاً من دعوى المعارضة فإذا لم يمنع الخوف من قولكم : قد عورض وإن كان تصريحاً بالقدح في القرآن والتكذيب له مع عروه من حجة أو شبهة فكيف يمنعكم الخوف من إظهار ما ادعيتم . ويقال لمن سأل عن هذا من اليهود والنصارى لو كان ما قلتموه صحيحاً لجاز لمدع أن يدعي أن موسى وعيسى عليهما السلام قد عورضا في قلب العصا حية وفلق البحر وإحياء الميت وإبراء الأكمه والأبرص وأن الخوف من أسيافكم يمنع من قتل ذلك وأن الخوف من سيوف المسلمين اليوم يمنع من نقله الآن لأن مكذب موسى وعيسى عند المسلمين بمنزلة مكذب محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم فإن لم يجب هذا لم يجب ما قلتم.
The sword prevents that, as a manifest transmission; and its detail, explicit statement, and clarification occurs from every specific man. And since we do not know the existence of opposition to the Qur'an like we know its appearance from the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, their claim must fall. Also, if fear of their transmitting the opposition were to prevent that, it would also prevent the claim of opposition. So if fear does not prevent your saying: 'It has been opposed'—even though it is an explicit disparagement of the Qur'an and its denial, devoid of proof or semblance—how does fear prevent you from manifesting what you claim? And it is said to whoever asks about this from the Jews and Christians: If what you said were true, it would be permissible for a claimant to claim that Moses and Jesus, peace be upon them, were opposed in the turning of the staff into a snake, and the splitting of the sea, and reviving the dead, and healing the blind and leprous, and that fear of your swords prevents mentioning that, and that fear of the swords of Muslims today prevents its transmission now, because the one who denies Moses and Jesus among Muslims is in the position of one who denies Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace. If this is not necessary, then what you said is not necessary.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that fear of the sword prevented the opponents of the Prophet from transmitting any successful challenge (mu'arada) to the Qur'an. Baqillani first argues that the existence of the Qur'an is known through widespread transmission (tawatur) from the Prophet, and we have no known instance of a successful challenge being transmitted. If fear were a real barrier, it would also have prevented opponents from even claiming a challenge—yet they did claim it, though without evidence. Thus fear cannot be the reason for the absence of transmitted challenges. He then extends the argument: if the Jews and Christians accepted that fear prevented transmission, they would have to accept that their own prophets' miracles might have been successfully opposed, and that fear of Muslim swords today prevents transmitting those challenges. This leads to an absurdity, so their premise is false.

Key Terms

الخوف
النقلي
المعجزة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The fear argument only applies to the Qur'an.
Correction: Baqillani extends the reasoning to all prophetic miracles by parity of reasoning.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why does the fear argument fail to explain the absence of transmitted challenges to the Qur'an?
A) Because the opponents did not fear the sword at all.
B) Because fear would also prevent opponents from even claiming a challenge, yet they did claim it.
C) Because the Qur'an was never challenged.
D) Because the Prophet forbade challenges.

Key Takeaway
Fear of reprisal cannot account for the absence of transmitted challenges to the Qur'an, because it would also suppress the claim itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

This passage shows that if you feared to transmit the truth, you would also fear to claim it. Yet you may have claimed it weakly. What truth are you currently hiding? Name it and decide one concrete step to speak it this week.
?
Baqillani uses a parity argument: what applies to the Qur'an must also apply to other prophets' miracles. Do you treat all of Allah's messengers with equal respect, or do you downplay some because of the company you keep? Examine your conversations—when was the last time you defended the truth of Musa or Isa with the same conviction you have for Muhammad (peace be upon them)? Make it your aim to speak boldly about all prophets.
?
If fear were a valid excuse for not transmitting something, then even the claim itself would be suppressed. But you have made claims about your faith—perhaps in private or with close friends. What is one claim you have made but not backed up with action because of fear? Write down a specific situation where your fear overshadowed your testimony, and pray for courage to live that claim openly.
