Rebuttal of Forgetting as a Cause for Lost Mu'arada
Baqillani refutes the claim that counter-challenges were forgotten due to divine prevention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani argues that divine prevention of transmitting a successful counter-challenge would undermine all prophethood, not just the Qur'an.

Core Idea
Forgetting a miracle is itself a miracle—and it destroys all proof of prophethood.

Baqillani now tackles a subtle objection: what if a counter-challenge truly occurred, but God caused everyone to forget it? This would seem to spare the objector from having to produce actual evidence. But Baqillani shows that this very scenario would be as miraculous as any prophetic sign, and if accepted, would make it impossible to distinguish any true prophet from a false one. This argument reveals the deep link between miracles and the preservation of knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the opening lines: The opponent suggests that a successful counter-challenge occurred but was forgotten because God turned people's hearts away from transmitting it.
This is a hypothetical objection to the argument that no counter-challenge exists.
2
First answer: It would be a miracle for liars
Baqillani replies that divine prevention of transmission is like manifesting a miracle for false claimants—there is no difference between turning a staff into a snake and turning hearts away from transmitting a great event.
3
Second answer: It corrupts all proof of prophethood
If such divine prevention were possible, we could never be certain that any prophet's miracle wasn't similarly countered and forgotten; thus, all prophetic claims would become uncertain.
This shows the objection is self-defeating.
4
Conclusion: The objection is from universal skepticism
Baqillani emphasizes that this line of reasoning does not come from followers of a particular religion but from someone who attacks all prophethood. Its answer is that it would imply God is unable to provide clear proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : ما أنكرتم أن تكون المعارضة قد وقعت ونسيت وذهب ذكرها وضبطها عن كل فرقة لأن الله صرف دواعي الناس وهممهم عن حفظها والتوفر على نقلها؟ قيل لهم : هذا أيضاً غير جائز لأنه بمنزلة ابتداء إظهار المعجزات على أيدي الكذابين لأنه لا فرق بين خرق العادة بقلب العصا حية وفلق البحر وغير ذلك وبين خرقه العادة في صرف دواعي الناس عن نقل الأمر العظيم والخطب الجسيم وما قد بحفظه وانطلاق الألسن عليه وإلهاج الأنفس بذكره وغلبة إشهاره وإظهاره على طيه وكتمانه لأن ذلك أجمَعَ خَرْق للعادة ولأنه أيضاً إفساد الأدلة وسد العلم بإثبات النبوة لأنه لو جاز ذلك لم نأمن أن يكون جميع الرسل قد عورضوا في آياتهم وصرف الله سبحانه دواعي الناس نقل المعارضة وحفظها فلا يكون لنا مع ذلك سبيل إلى العلم بصدق واحد منهم وقيام حجة على أمته لأننا إذ لم نأمن كونه المعارضة وإن جهلناها لموضع ترك النقل لها، لم نأمن أن يكونوا كذبة غير صادقين وذلك يضاد اعتقاد نبوته وهذا كلام ليس لبعض أهل الملل على بعض وإنما للطاعن على سائر النبوات وجوابه ما ذكرناه من أنه إفساد للأعلام وإيجاب لعجز القديم سبحانه عن الأدلة على صدق الصادق والتفرقة بينه وبين الكاذب.
If someone says: What prevents you from saying that opposition occurred but was forgotten, and its mention and preservation disappeared from every group, because God turned people's inclinations and ambitions away from preserving it and attending to its transmission? It is said to them: This also is not permissible, because it is like the beginning of the manifestation of miracles at the hands of liars. For there is no difference between the breaking of custom by turning a staff into a snake, splitting the sea, and so on, and His breaking custom in turning people's inclinations away from transmitting the great matter and momentous event, despite its preservation, the tongues flowing with it, the souls being inflamed with its mention, and the predominance of its publicizing and manifesting over its concealment and suppression—for all of that is a breaking of custom. And also because it corrupts the proofs and blocks the way to knowledge of establishing prophethood. For if that were allowed, we would not be safe from the possibility that all the messengers were opposed in their miracles, and God turned people's inclinations away from transmitting the opposition and preserving it; then we would have no way to know the truthfulness of any one of them or the establishment of proof against his community. For if we are not safe from the possibility of opposition even while we are ignorant of it due to the abandonment of its transmission, we are not safe from the possibility that they were liars, not truthful—and that contradicts the belief in their prophethood. This speech does not belong to some followers of religions against others; rather, it belongs to the one who attacks all prophethoods. Its answer is what we have mentioned: that it corrupts the signs and necessitates the inability of the Eternal, glorified be He, to provide proofs for the truthfulness of the truthful and to distinguish between him and the liar.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage addresses another objection: perhaps a successful challenge to the Qur'an did occur, but was forgotten due to God turning people's inclinations away from transmitting it. Baqillani argues that this is impossible because it would be a miracle in support of false claimants. There is no difference between God causing a stick to become a snake as a true sign, and God causing people to forget a challenge—both break natural custom. If God could cause such forgetting, then all prophets might have been successfully opposed but people forgot, and we could never be certain of any prophet's truthfulness. This argument does not come from a follower of one religion against another; it comes from a universal skeptic who attacks all prophethood. The only answer is that such a scenario would corrupt the very signs of prophethood and imply that God is unable to provide convincing proofs—which is impossible.

Key Terms
خرق العادة
المعجزات
إفساد الأدلة
العلم
النبوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think this argument only applies to the Qur'an, not to other prophets.
Correction: Baqillani explicitly states that this objection would apply to all prophets, making it a universal argument against prophethood itself.

Checkpoint
Why does Baqillani reject the claim that a successful challenge to the Qur'an was forgotten?
A) Because the challenge would have been recorded despite divine intervention.
B) Because divine prevention of transmission would itself be a miracle, and would make all prophethood uncertain.
C) Because the Qur'an is unchangeable.
D) Because people have strong memories.

Key Takeaway
Divine prevention of transmitting a counter-challenge would be a miracle that destroys the very evidence for prophethood, making the objection self-defeating.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed a clear sign from Allah because you conveniently assumed that doubts or counterarguments might exist that you haven't heard? How does Baqillani's argument expose the danger of such rationalizations?
?
When you face questions about your faith, do you genuinely seek evidence or do you hide behind hypothetical possibilities? Baqillani shows that entertaining certain possibilities destroys all certainty. How does this challenge your own approach to conviction?
?
How often do you treat the truthfulness of the Prophet ﷺ as a settled matter that you are responsible to defend? After seeing that even a hypothetical 'what if' can unravel the entire fabric of proof, what must you change about how you guard your certainty?

Why the Arabs Could Not Have Neglected the Challenge
Baqillani rejects the negligence objection for the Qur'an's inimitability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani dismisses the claim that the Arabs failed to challenge the Qur'an due to negligence, and how he argues that the connection between inability and failure is self-evident to any rational person.

Core Idea
If the Arabs could have matched the Qur'an, they would have — their failure proves inability, not negligence.

Baqillani now addresses a final objection: perhaps the Arabs did not try to produce a rival to the Qur'an simply because they never thought about it. He rejects this outright, arguing that any rational person would immediately see the implication of matching the Qur'an. This lesson unpacks his reasoning and shows why the objection collapses.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Understand what the hypothetical objector is claiming: that the Arabs refrained from opposing the Qur'an because they turned away from reflecting on the consequences.
Notice the objector is suggesting a lack of reflection, not inability.
2
Examine Baqillani's response
Baqillani says the matter requires no reflection or consideration because it is obvious to any person of complete intellect.
He dismisses the need for deep thought; the link between matching and discrediting is immediate.
3
Reflect on the underlying principle
Why does Baqillani consider the matter so obvious? Because if someone could produce a like text, they would discredit the claimant. Any rational person would realize this, so their failure to try proves they could not.
This reinforces the miracle: the Arabs had every motive to try, yet they did not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : ما أنكرتم أن يكون القوم إنما تركوا معارضة القرآن لإعراضهم عن النظر في أن مقابلته بمثله موجب لتكذيب من أتى به؟ قيل لهم : فهذا مما لا نظر فيه ولا تأمل لأنه لا شبهة على أحد كمل عقله.
If someone says: What prevents you from saying that the people only refrained from opposing the Qur'an because they turned away from reflecting that matching it with its like would necessitate the denial of the one who brought it? It is said to them: This is something that requires no reflection or consideration, because there is no doubt for anyone of complete intellect.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage presents a final objection: the Arabs did not attempt to produce a challenge to the Qur'an because they simply did not reflect on the fact that matching it would prove the Prophet false. Baqillani dismisses this as impossible. The reason requires no deep reflection: any sane person would realize that if he could produce something similar, he would discredit the claimant. The fact that no one even attempted it shows they knew it was impossible. The answer begins by stating that the matter is so obvious that no one of sound mind could doubt it.

Key Terms
المعارضة
النظر
التكذيب
العقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Arabs were too ignorant or negligent to attempt challenging the Qur'an.
Correction: Baqillani argues that the matter is so clear that any person of sound intellect would have perceived the challenge; their failure to attempt shows they could not, not that they did not think of it.

Checkpoint
Why does Baqillani reject the claim that the Arabs failed to challenge the Qur'an due to lack of reflection?
A) Because the Arabs were highly educated.
B) Because any sane person would see that matching the Qur'an would discredit the Prophet, so if they could, they would have done it.
C) Because the Qur'an explicitly forbade them from trying.
D) Because the Prophet prevented them.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani argues that the Arabs' failure to challenge the Qur'an cannot be attributed to mere negligence because any rational person would have recognized that producing a like text would discredit the Prophet, and thus their inaction is proof of inability.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If you were in the Arabs' position and you knew you could disprove a claimant by producing a single verse, would you not do it? Then why do you sometimes avoid seeking evidence that would challenge your own comfortable beliefs? What is holding you back from the truth you already suspect?

Why Preventing a Counter-Miracle Undermines Prophethood
Baqillani argues that preventing transmission of a counter-miracle aids liars and undermines evidence for prophethood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why preventing the transmission of a counter-miracle would logically undermine the proof of prophethood.

Core Idea
If God could hide counter-miracles, no prophet could ever be proven true.

Baqillani here addresses a subtle objection: what if God, while granting a miracle to a true prophet, simultaneously prevents people from transmitting a miraculous counter-event that would expose a claimant as false? He shows that such a possibility would not only break God's custom but would destroy the very basis for distinguishing truth from falsehood in prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the English translation. Notice the logical flow: the objection, the analogy, the consequence, and the refutation.
2
Identify the analogy used
Baqillani compares preventing transmission to initiating miracles for liars. Find the exact phrase where he says there is no difference between breaking custom in a visible miracle and breaking it by turning away people's motivations.
This is the key move: both are breaches of God's customary way.
3
Trace the logical consequence
Ask yourself: if God could suppress a counter-miracle, what would that mean for our knowledge of any prophet's truth? Write down the conclusion: we could never be sure, and prophethood proof collapses.
This shows the argument is not just polemic but a universal principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جرت العادة حفظها والتوفر على نقلها؟ قيل لهم: هذا أيضاً غير جائز لأنه بمنزلة ابتداء إظهار المعجزات على أيدي الكذابين لأنه لا فرق بين خرق العادة بقلب العصا حية وفلق البحر وغير ذلك وبين خرقه العادة في صرف دواعي الناس عن نقل الأمر العظيم والخطب الجسيم وما قد بحفظه وانطلاق الألسن عليه وإلهاج الأنفس بذكره وغلبة إشهاره وإظهاره على طيه وكتمانه لأن ذلك أجمع خرق للعادة ولأنه أيضاً إفساد الأدلة وسد العلم بإثبات النبوة لأنه لو جاز ذلك لم نأمن أن يكون جميع الرسل قد عورضوا في آياتهم وصرف الله سبحانه دواعي الناس نقل المعارضة وحفظها فلا يكون لنا مع ذلك سبيل إلى العلم بصدق واحد منهم وقيام حجة على أمته لأننا إذ لم نأمن كون المعارضة وإن جهلناها لموضع ترك النقل لها، لم نأمن أن يكونوا كذبة غير صادقين وذلك يضاد اعتقاد نبوّتهم وهذا كلام ليس لبعض أهل الملل على بعض وإنما للطاعن على سائر النبوات وجوابه ما ذكرناه من أنه إفساد للأعلام وإيجاب لعجز القديم سبحانه عن هو الأدلة على صدق الصادق والتفرقة بينه وبين الكاذب.
Is the custom preserved and transmitted? It was said to them: This too is not permissible, because it is like the initial display of miracles at the hands of liars, since there is no difference between breaking the custom by turning the staff into a snake and splitting the sea and so on, and breaking the custom in turning away the people's motivations from transmitting a great matter and a grave calamity, and what is preserved and on which tongues are loosed and souls are incited by its mention, and the dominance of its publicizing and manifesting over its concealment and suppression—for all of that is a breaking of custom. And also because it vitiates the proofs and blocks the path to knowledge of establishing prophethood. For if that were permissible, we could not be safe from the possibility that all the messengers may have been opposed in their miracles, and Allah, exalted, turned away the people's motivations from transmitting the opposition and preserving it, so that we would have no way to know the truthfulness of any one of them or the establishment of a proof upon his nation. Since we are not safe from the existence of opposition—even if we are ignorant of it due to the omission of its transmission—we are not safe from their being liars, not truthful. That contradicts belief in their prophethood. This speech is not from some religious communities against others, but rather from one who attacks all prophethoods. Its answer is what we mentioned: that it vitiates the signs and necessitates the incapacity of the Eternal, exalted, regarding the proofs of the truthful one's truthfulness and the distinction between him and the liar.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage presents a refutation of an objection: if God could prevent the transmission of a counter-miracle, then the evidence for prophethood would collapse. The argument begins by stating that preventing transmission is like initiating miracles for liars, since breaking custom (kharq al-‘ādah) in turning away people's motivations is as much a miracle as changing a staff into a snake. If such prevention were possible, then we could never be certain that any messenger's miracles were not secretly opposed by an equally miraculous counter-event that was suppressed. This would make it impossible to distinguish true prophets from false ones, since a liar's false claim could be hidden by God's prevention of transmission. Therefore, the objection is not just sectarian polemic but a universal attack on all prophethood. The answer is that such a possibility would destroy the evidentiary system (i'lām) and necessitate incapacity in God—impossible for the Eternal. The conclusion is that the original proof of miracles stands firm.

Key Terms
خرق العادة (kharq al-‘ādah)
دواعي الناس (dawā‘ī al-nās)
المعارضة (al-mu‘āraḍa)
إفساد الأدلة (ifsād al-adilla)
إثبات النبوة (ithbāt al-nubuwwa)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument is a mere dialectical trick with no real force.
Correction: Baqillani shows it is a logical necessity: if hidden counter-miracles were possible, the entire system of proving prophethood breaks down.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if God could prevent the transmission of a counter-miracle?
A) Miracles would still be valid but weaker.
B) The proof of prophethood would be undermined.
C) Only false prophets would be affected.
D) The Quran would still be inimitable.

Key Takeaway
Without the guarantee that counter-miracles are not suppressed, miracle-based proof for prophethood collapses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Are there areas of your life where you doubt the evidence for prophethood because you haven't physically seen signs? What does this passage teach you about the sufficiency of God's proof?
?
This argument shows that God does not allow confusion between truth and falsehood in the matter of prophethood. How does that compel you to actively seek the truth in other areas of your faith, knowing that God never leaves you without clear evidence?

Prophecies of the Unseen as Proof of Inimitability
Lists Quranic prophecies fulfilled exactly as promised, proving divine origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran's accurate prophecies of future events demonstrate its divine origin and constitute a separate aspect of its inimitability.

Core Idea
Fulfilled prophecies prove the Quran is from Allah, not human speech.

In previous lessons, we explored the miraculous composition of the Quran. Here, Imam al-Baqillani introduces another dimension: reports of the unseen (أخبار الغيوب). The Quran contains predictions that were fulfilled exactly as stated, something no human could accomplish. This provides compelling evidence for its divine authorship.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the question
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that it starts with a question asking if there are other aspects of inimitability beyond composition. The answer is yes, and two aspects are mentioned.
2
Focus on the first aspect: prophecies
The first aspect is reports of the unseen. The author explains that these are things no human could know. Then he lists several examples from the Quran.
The second aspect is not detailed in this passage.
3
Examine each prophecy example
Go through each prophecy mentioned: entry into the Sacred Mosque, defeat of the multitude, victory of Islam, succession of the Rightly Guided Caliphs, and the Jews' inability to wish for death. Confirm that each was fulfilled historically.
You may need to refer to historical accounts for fulfillment.
4
Reflect on the miraculous nature
Ask yourself: Why are these prophecies considered miraculous? Because they could not have been known by human means at the time. Their accurate fulfillment proves the Quran is from Allah.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة في وجوه الإعجاز
فإن قال قائل: فهل في القرآن وجه من وجوه الإعجاز غير ما ذكرتموه من بديع نظمه وعجيب رصفه وتأليفه؟ قيل له: أجل، فيه وجهان آخران من وجوه الإعجاز.
أحدهما ما انطوى عليه من أخبار الغيوب التي يعلم كل عاقل عجز الخلق عن معرفتها والتوصل إلى إدراكها نحو قوله: "لتدخلن المسجد الحرام إن شاء الله آمنين محلقين رؤوسكم ومقصرين لا تخافون" فدخلوه كما وعدهم وأخبرهم. ومن ذلك قوله تعالى: "سيهزم الجمع ويولون الدبر" فكان ذلك كما أخبر. وقوله: "ليظهره على الدين كله ولو كره المشركون" أظهره الله وأعلى دعوته وأذل الملوك المحاولة لأبطاله التي كانت حول صاحب الدعوة إليه. وقوله تعالى: "وعد الله الذين آمنوا منكم وعملوا الصالحات ليستخلفنهم في الأرض كما استخلف الذين من قبلهم" وكان من ذلك ما وعدهم الله تعالى واستخلف الأئمة الأربعة الخلفاء الراشدين.
وقوله لليهود: "قل إن كانت لكم الدار الآخرة عند الله خالصة من دون الناس فتمنوا الموت إن كنتم صادقين ولن يتمنوه أبداً بما"
A question on the aspects of inimitability. For if someone says: Is there in the Quran any aspect of inimitability other than what you mentioned of its wonderful composition, amazing arrangement, and structure? It is said to him: Yes, there are two other aspects of inimitability. One of them is what it contains of reports of the unseen, which every rational person knows the inability of creation to know or attain. For example, His statement: 'You will surely enter the Sacred Mosque, if Allah wills, in safety, with your heads shaved and [hair] shortened, not fearing.' So they entered it as He promised and informed them. And of that is His statement, Exalted: 'The multitude will be defeated, and they will turn their backs.' And that happened as He informed. And His statement: 'That He may make it prevail over all religion, even if the polytheists dislike it.' Allah made it prevail and raised His call and humiliated the kings who attempted to nullify it, who were around the master of the call to it. And His statement, Exalted: 'Allah has promised those who have believed among you and done righteous deeds that He will surely grant them succession in the land, just as He granted succession to those before them.' And of that was what Allah promised them, and He gave succession to the four imams, the Rightly Guided Caliphs. And His statement to the Jews: 'Say, 'If the Final Abode with Allah is exclusively for you, excluding the [other] people, then wish for death if you are truthful.' And they will never wish for it ever because of...'
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is a question-and-answer that introduces additional aspects of the Quran's inimitability beyond its stylistic excellence. After establishing the miraculous composition, the author is asked whether there are other aspects. He answers affirmatively, mentioning two, but only the first is detailed here: reports of the unseen (أخبار الغيوب). These are events that no human could have known at the time, but the Quran predicted them accurately. The author provides several examples: the prophecy that the Muslims would enter the Sacred Mosque peacefully (fulfilled at the conquest of Mecca), the defeat of the confederates (Battle of the Trench), the victory of Islam over all religions, the succession of the Rightly Guided Caliphs, and the challenge to the Jews to wish for death (which they never did, despite their claim of exclusive salvation). These fulfilled prophecies demonstrate that the Quran is from Allah, as human beings cannot know the future with such certainty.

Misconception: Some think that prophecies in the Quran are merely predictions that could be coincidental or based on human guesswork.
Correction: The accuracy and specificity of multiple prophecies, all fulfilled exactly as stated, cannot be attributed to chance. They demonstrate divine knowledge and confirm the Quran's divine origin.

The Challenge to the Jews to Wish for Death
Baqillani presents the challenge to the Jews as proof of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Jews' refusal to wish for death served as a proof of the Prophet's truthfulness.

Core Idea
The Jews' failure to accept the challenge proved the Prophet's prophethood.

Baqillani begins by citing the Qur'anic challenge to the Jews: if they truly believed they were the chosen people, they should wish for death. Their refusal demonstrated their awareness that the Prophet's claim was true.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how the challenge is presented as a conditional: if they wish for death, they die.
2
Identify the proof structure
The passage states that the Prophet informed them they would not wish for death, and they indeed did not wish for it. This confirms his truthfulness.
The proof relies on their knowledge that his claim was true, so they refrained.
3
Reflect on why this is miraculous
Think about why this event could not be coincidental. The accuracy of the prediction and the certainty of the outcome point to divine knowledge.
This shows the Prophet knew something hidden from others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قدمت أيديهم فأخبر أنهم إن تمنوا الموت ماتوا وأنهم لن يتمنوه فلم يتمنوه على ما أخبر به علماً منهم بصدقه وأنهم لو تمنوا الموت لماتوا لا محالة. وكذلك امتنع النصارى عن مباهلته عند دعائه لهم إليها ومطالبته بها في قوله تعالى: فقل تعالوا ندع أبناءنا وأبناءكم ونساءنا ونساءكم وأنفسنا وأنفسكم ثم نبتهل فنجعل لعنة الله على الكاذبين فامتنعوا عن المباهلة خوفاً من النكال وأليم العقاب وأن ما ينزل بهم توعدهم به؛ وليس ذلك إلا لعلمهم بصدقه وثبوت نبوته. ومن أخبار الغيوب قوله تعالى: الم غلبت الروم في أدنى الأرض وهم من بعد غلبهم سيغلبون؛ فغلبت الروم فارس في بضع سنين كما أخبر تعالى. نظائر هذا مما يكثر تتبعه واتفاق الصواب في هذا أجمع على سبيل التخمين والظن ممتنع متعذر فدل ذلك على أنه من أخبار علام الغيوب سبحانه. والوجه الآخر ما عليه القرآن من قصص الأولين وسير الماضين وأحاديث المتقدمين وذكر ما شجر بينهم وكان في أعصارهم مما لا يجوز حصول علمه إلا لمن كثر لقاؤه لأهل السير ودرسه لها وعنايته بها ومجالسته لأهلها وكان ممن يتلو الكتب ويستخرجها مع العلم بأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لم يكن يتلو كتاباً ولا يخطه بيمينه وأنه لم يكن ممن يعرف بدراسة الكتب ومجالسة أهل السير والأخذ عنهم ولا لقي إلا من لقوه ولا عرف إلا من عرفوه، وأنهم يعرفون دأبه وديدنه ومنشأه وتصرفه في حال إقامته بينهم وظعنه عنهم؛ فدل ذلك على أن المخبر له عن هذه الأمور هو الله سبحانه علام الغيوب. فهذا وجه الإعجاز في القرآن.
"Their hands have been sent forth" — so He informed that if they wished for death they would die, and that they will not wish for it, and they did not wish for it, according to what He informed, as knowledge from them of his truthfulness, and that if they wished for death they would die inevitably. Likewise, the Christians refrained from imprecation (mubāhala) with him when he called them to it and demanded it from them in His statement, the Exalted: "Say: Come, let us call our sons and your sons, our women and your women, and ourselves and yourselves, then we pray earnestly and invoke the curse of Allah upon the liars." So they refrained from the imprecation out of fear of calamity and painful punishment, and that what would befall them was what He threatened them with; and that was only because of their knowledge of his truthfulness and the establishment of his prophethood. And among the reports of the unseen (akhbār al-ghuyūb) is His statement, the Exalted: "Alif Lam Mim. The Romans have been defeated in the nearest land, and they, after their defeat, will be victorious" — so the Romans defeated Persia in a few years, as the Exalted informed. Similar examples to this, which are many to follow, and the agreement of correctness in all of this by way of conjecture and guesswork is impossible and unattainable; so that indicates that it is from the reports of the Knower of the Unseen, the Exalted. Another aspect is what is found in the Qur'an of stories of earlier peoples, biographies of the past, accounts of the ancients, and mention of what occurred between them and what happened in their eras — matters whose knowledge cannot be obtained except by one who has frequently met with people of biographies (ahl al-siyar), studied them, paid attention to them, and sat with their experts; and he would be among those who recite books and extract them, while knowing that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not recite any book nor write it with his right hand, and that he was not among those known for studying books, or sitting with people of biographies and taking from them, and he did not meet except those whom they met, nor did he know except what they knew; and they (the people of biographies) know his habit, his custom, his upbringing, and his conduct during his stay among them and his departure from them. So that indicates that the one who informed him about these matters is Allah, the Exalted, the Knower of the Unseen. This is one aspect of the inimitability (iʿjāz) of the Qur'an.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage presents a continuous argument proving the Prophet Muhammad's prophethood through miracles and reports of the unseen. It begins by citing the Qur'anic challenge to the Jews to wish for death (Quran 2:94-95), noting that they did not dare to do so because they knew the Prophet was truthful and would die if they did. Second, it references the Christians' refusal to engage in imprecation (mubāhala) when challenged in Quran 3:61, again due to their knowledge of his truthfulness. Third, it invokes the prophecy of the Romans' victory over the Persians (Quran 30:1-3), which occurred as foretold. The author argues that such consistent and accurate predictions cannot be the result of coincidence or guesswork, proving they come from God, the Knower of the Unseen. The second part of the argument examines the Prophet's knowledge of past events and stories of earlier nations, which he could not have learned through normal means since he was unlettered and had no access to scholarly circles. This again demonstrates divine revelation. The passage concludes that these are aspects of the Qur'an's inimitability (iʿjāz).

Key Terms
تمنى الموت
صدقه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Jews refused out of cowardice or disbelief, not because they knew the Prophet was truthful.
Correction: The passage states they refrained because they had knowledge of his truthfulness (علمهم بصدقه), not out of mere fear of death.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did the Jews not wish for death?
A) They did not believe in the Prophet
B) They knew he was truthful and would die
C) They were afraid of death
D) They forgot the challenge

Key Takeaway
The Jews' refusal to wish for death, despite the challenge, proves they recognized the Prophet's truthfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Jews claimed to long for the afterlife but refused to wish for death when challenged. Is there a belief you profess that your actions contradict? What would it take for you to act consistently with that belief today?
?
Imagine you were in the audience when the Prophet issued the challenge. Would you have been among those who remained silent? What does your silence reveal about your own certainty in the truth?
?
If you knew with certainty that wishing for death would prove the truth of a message, would you dare to wish for it? What holds you back from that level of commitment in your faith?

The Christians' Refusal of Imprecation
Baqillani presents the Christians' refusal of mubāhala as proof of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Christians' refusal to engage in imprecation (mubāhala) proves the Prophet's prophethood.

Core Idea
The Christians' fear of divine curse confirmed the Prophet's truthfulness.

Baqillani next discusses the incident of mubāhala: the Prophet challenged the Christians to pray for Allah's curse on the liar. Their refusal, despite their claims, showed they knew he was the truthful prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the Qur'anic verse cited and the Christians' reaction.
2
Understand the logic
The Prophet challenged them to imprecation, but they declined because they were certain that if they did, the curse would fall on them, proving the Prophet's truth.
Their fear was based on knowledge, not doubt.
3
Connect to earlier proof
Compare this to the Jewish example: again, the opponents' own avoidance proves the Prophet's claim.
Both proofs rely on the opponents' inner recognition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قدمت أيديهم فأخبر أنهم إن تمنوا الموت ماتوا وأنهم لن يتمنوه فلم يتمنوه على ما أخبر به علماً منهم بصدقه وأنهم لو تمنوا الموت لماتوا لا محالة. وكذلك امتنع النصارى عن مباهلته عند دعائه لهم إليها ومطالبته بها في قوله تعالى: فقل تعالوا ندع أبناءنا وأبناءكم ونساءنا ونساءكم وأنفسنا وأنفسكم ثم نبتهل فنجعل لعنة الله على الكاذبين فامتنعوا عن المباهلة خوفاً من النكال وأليم العقاب وأن ما ينزل بهم توعدهم به؛ وليس ذلك إلا لعلمهم بصدقه وثبوت نبوته. ومن أخبار الغيوب قوله تعالى: الم غلبت الروم في أدنى الأرض وهم من بعد غلبهم سيغلبون؛ فغلبت الروم فارس في بضع سنين كما أخبر تعالى. نظائر هذا مما يكثر تتبعه واتفاق الصواب في هذا أجمع على سبيل التخمين والظن ممتنع متعذر فدل ذلك على أنه من أخبار علام الغيوب سبحانه. والوجه الآخر ما عليه القرآن من قصص الأولين وسير الماضين وأحاديث المتقدمين وذكر ما شجر بينهم وكان في أعصارهم مما لا يجوز حصول علمه إلا لمن كثر لقاؤه لأهل السير ودرسه لها وعنايته بها ومجالسته لأهلها وكان ممن يتلو الكتب ويستخرجها مع العلم بأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لم يكن يتلو كتاباً ولا يخطه بيمينه وأنه لم يكن ممن يعرف بدراسة الكتب ومجالسة أهل السير والأخذ عنهم ولا لقي إلا من لقوه ولا عرف إلا من عرفوه، وأنهم يعرفون دأبه وديدنه ومنشأه وتصرفه في حال إقامته بينهم وظعنه عنهم؛ فدل ذلك على أن المخبر له عن هذه الأمور هو الله سبحانه علام الغيوب. فهذا وجه الإعجاز في القرآن.
"Their hands have been sent forth" — so He informed that if they wished for death they would die, and that they will not wish for it, and they did not wish for it, according to what He informed, as knowledge from them of his truthfulness, and that if they wished for death they would die inevitably. Likewise, the Christians refrained from imprecation (mubāhala) with him when he called them to it and demanded it from them in His statement, the Exalted: "Say: Come, let us call our sons and your sons, our women and your women, and ourselves and yourselves, then we pray earnestly and invoke the curse of Allah upon the liars." So they refrained from the imprecation out of fear of calamity and painful punishment, and that what would befall them was what He threatened them with; and that was only because of their knowledge of his truthfulness and the establishment of his prophethood. And among the reports of the unseen (akhbār al-ghuyūb) is His statement, the Exalted: "Alif Lam Mim. So that indicates that the one who informed him about these matters is Allah, the Exalted, the Knower of the Unseen. This is one aspect of the inimitability (iʿjāz) of the Qur'an.

?

?

?
The Christians feared the curse because they knew the Prophet was truthful. What do you fear more: the consequences of rejecting God's truth, or the discomfort of living it? What one step will you take this week to act on what you know?

The Prophecy of the Romans' Victory
Baqillani presents the prophecy of the Romans' victory as a proof from reports of the unseen.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the prophecy about the Romans' victory serves as a proof of divine revelation.

Core Idea
The accurate prediction of future events cannot be guesswork; it comes from the Knower of the Unseen.

Baqillani cites the prophecy of the Romans' victory over the Persians within a few years, which occurred exactly as foretold. He argues that such consistent accuracy cannot be attributed to coincidence or human guessing.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Identify the prophecy: the Romans would be victorious after their defeat.
The verses are from Surah Ar-Rum (30:1-3).
2
Understand the argument
The passage emphasizes that such accurate predictions across many events cannot be explained by guesswork; they must come from Allah.
The phrase 'agreement of correctness in all of this by way of conjecture is impossible' is key.
3
Reflect on the implication
If the Prophet could not have known this by natural means, it proves that his knowledge was from Allah, confirming his prophethood.
This is a direct proof of divine revelation.

The Prophet's Knowledge of Past Stories
Baqillani presents the Prophet's knowledge of past stories as proof of divine revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's accurate knowledge of past nations, despite being unlettered, proves divine revelation.

Core Idea
An unlettered man could not have known detailed histories without divine teaching.

Baqillani presents another aspect of i'jāz: the Qur'an contains stories of earlier peoples and ancient events. The Prophet Muhammad was unlettered and had no access to books or scholars, yet he narrated these with perfect accuracy. This could only come from Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the description of the Prophet's background: he did not read or write, nor did he sit with historians.
2
Understand the argument from inability
The passage argues that such knowledge cannot be obtained without extensive study, which the Prophet did not have. Therefore, it must be from Allah.
This is a proof from the Prophet's unlettered status.
3

This is identified as 'one aspect of the inimitability of the Qur'an', showing that the Qur'an is miraculous.
The conclusion ties this proof to the concept of i'jāz.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet could have learned these stories from oral tradition or occasional sources.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that such detailed knowledge requires extensive study and access to written records, which the Prophet lacked entirely.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what proves that the Prophet's knowledge of past stories is from Allah?
A) He memorized them from books
B) He was unlettered and had no access to scholars or books
C) He traveled to learn history
D) He was inspired by poets

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's accurate knowledge of past events, despite his unlettered state, proves that the Qur'an is from Allah and is therefore miraculous.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quran's accounts of past nations, do you recognize the impossibility of the Prophet knowing them except by divine revelation? How does this realization impact your trust in the Quran as the word of Allah, not just a human composition?
?
The Prophet, despite being unlettered, conveyed the most accurate history. Are you willing to submit your intellect to the Quran’s narratives over historical theories or your own assumptions? What change in your daily life would this submission require?
?
If the Prophet's unlettered state is a clear sign of the Quran's divine origin, why do you often treat the Quran as one among many books? Name one practical step you can take today to honor the Quran as the direct word of your Creator.

Prophethood
beginner

The Jewish Claim and Baqillani's Initial Objection
Baqillani challenges Jewish proof and elicits tawatur criteria.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani challenges the Jewish proof for Moses' prophethood and the Jewish criteria for establishing tawatur.

Core Idea
Jewish tawatur is not immune to objection from skeptics.

Baqillani begins a dialectical argument against the Jews. He asks them to prove Moses' prophethood, and they respond citing the miraculous signs transmitted by their community. But Baqillani immediately points out that other groups deny those reports, so how can they claim certainty? The Jews then articulate the conditions that make a transmission certain despite opposition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial challenge
Baqillani asks the Jews for the proof of Moses' prophethood. Notice how he frames the question as a direct challenge.
This sets up the dialectical structure.
2
Examine the Jewish response
The Jews refer to the miracles transmitted by their community, such as the splitting of the sea. Understand their reliance on transmitted reports.
3
Notice Baqillani's objection
Baqillani immediately points out that many groups (Brahmins, Magians, etc.) deny those reports. Ask yourself: how can the Jews claim certainty if there is strong opposition?
This is a key move in the argument.
4
Understand the Jewish tawatur criteria
The Jews define tawatur: a report with consistent transmission from beginning to end, by a large and diverse group, makes lying impossible. This becomes the standard.
Note the conditions: large number, diverse motives, spread across lands, and impossibility of collusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيقال لهم جميعاً : ما الدليل على إثبات نبــوة موسى عليه السلام ؟ فإن قالوا ما ظهر على يده من الأعلام المعجزة كفلق البحر وإخراج اليد البيضاء وغير ذلك من أعلامه قيل لهم : وما الدليل على صحة هذه الأعلام وثبوتها مع علمكم بخلاف من يخالف فيها من البراهمة والمجوس والملحدين وأهل التنجيم وغيرهم من الجاحدين ؟ فإن قالوا : الدليل على ذلك نقل اليهود خلفاً سلفاً عن قوم بهم تقوم الحجة لما هم عليه من كثرة العدد وتفرق الدواعي والهمم وتباين الأوطان وتباعد الديار واختلاف المذاهب والكذب ممتنع على مثلهم أن موسى عليه السلام أتى بهذه الأعلام التي ذكرناها فوجب العلم بصحتها. يقال لهم : أليس قد أنكر جميع من قدمنا ذكرهم من المجوس والبراهمة وغيرهم صحة ما نقله أسلافكم وأخلافكم فكيف يكون النقل موجباً للعلم مع إنكار من أنكره وطعن من طعن فيه. فإن قالوا : إذا استوى أول الخبر وطرفاه من آخره ووسطه ثبتت صحته ووجب العلم بصدق نقلته وإن خالف في ذلك مخالفون. يقال لهم : ما أنكرتم أن يكون محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم نبياً وأن يكون ما أثبته المسلمون من أعلامه صحيحاً بنقل من نقل ذلك من المسلمين؟ وذلك أن المسلمين في وقتنا هذا قوم ببعضهم يثبت التواتر وتقوم الحجة ; وقد نقلوا خلفاً عن سلف مع كثرة عددهم وتنافر طباعهم وتباين أغراضهم ودواعيهم واختلاف آرائهم ومذاهبهم وتفرق أوطانهم وامتناع جواز الكذب على مثلهم أن محمداً صلى الله عليه وسلم أتى بالأعلام الباهرة والبراهين اللائحة فمنها ما قد أطبقوا جميعاً وسائر أهل الملل على نقله والعلم به كالقرآن ومنها ما أخبرت الحجة من المسلمين أنها أخذته عن حجة والحجة عن مثلها حتى ينتهي ذلك إلى قوم نقلوه بحضرة جماعة الصحابة.
So it is said to them all: What is the proof for establishing the prophethood of Moses, peace be upon him? If they say: What appeared at his hand of miraculous signs, like the splitting of the sea, the bringing forth of the white hand, and other signs of his, it is said to them: And what is the proof for the correctness and establishment of these signs, given your knowledge of the opposition of those who differ regarding them, from the Brahmins, Magians, atheists, astrologers, and other deniers? If they say: The proof of that is the transmission of the Jews, successors from predecessors, from a people through whom the proof is established, because of their large number, divergence of motives and ambitions, diversity of homelands, distance of abodes, difference of sects, and the impossibility of lying upon the likes of them, that Moses, peace be upon him, came with these signs which we mentioned, so knowledge of their correctness becomes necessary. It is said to them: Did not all those we mentioned earlier from the Magians, Brahmins, and others deny the correctness of what your ancestors and descendants transmitted? So how can transmission be a cause of knowledge when there is denial by those who deny and criticism by those who criticize? If they say: When the beginning of the report and its two ends from its end and its middle are equal [consistent], its correctness is established and knowledge of the truthfulness of its transmitters becomes necessary, even if opposers oppose it. It is said to them: What prevents you from acknowledging that Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, is a prophet, and that what the Muslims have established of his signs is correct, through the transmission of those who transmitted that from the Muslims? And that is because the Muslims at our present time are a people through some of whom tawātur (massive transmission) is established and the proof is established; and they have transmitted, successors from predecessors, with the multiplicity of their number, divergence of their natures, diversity of their goals and motives, difference of their opinions and sects, dispersal of their lands, and the impossibility of lying upon the likes of them, that Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, came with dazzling signs and clear proofs. Among them are those which all of them and all the people of [religious] communities have unanimously transmitted and have knowledge of, like the Qur'an. And among them are what the authority (al-ḥujja) from the Muslims reported that he took from another authority, and the authority from the like of it, until that reaches people who transmitted it in the presence of the group of the Companions.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical refutation. Baqillani first challenges the Jews: what is your proof for Moses' prophethood? They answer: the miracles transmitted by the Jews. Baqillani objects: but many groups deny those reports, so how can you claim certainty? The Jews respond by describing the conditions for tawātur: a report transmitted by a large, diverse group that cannot plausibly collude on a lie. They claim that the Jewish transmission meets those conditions, establishing certainty despite deniers. Baqillani then turns their own argument against them: the Muslims also transmit Muhammad's miracles—such as the Qur'an and other signs—through a chain of reliable transmitters back to the Companions. The Muslim transmission is even stronger because of the large number, diverse motives, and impossibility of collusion. Therefore, if the Jews accept their own transmission as proof, they must logically accept the Muslim transmission as proof for Muhammad's prophethood.

Key Terms
نقل
تواتر
حجة
أعلام معجزة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Tawatur requires universal agreement without any opposition.
Correction: Baqillani shows that tawatur can still yield certain knowledge even when there are opposers, as long as the internal transmission conditions (e.g., consistency, impossibility of collusion) are met.

Checkpoint
According to the Jews in Baqillani's argument, what condition must a report fulfill to establish certain knowledge?
A) It must be transmitted by a single trustworthy narrator.
B) It must be written in a sacred book.
C) Its beginning, ends, and middle must be consistent (equally transmitted).
D) It must be confirmed by miracles.

Key Takeaway
The Jews define tawatur as a transmission that is consistent from beginning to end and surrounded by conditions that prevent lying, which they claim justifies certainty despite opposition.

Turning the Tables: Applying Tawatur to Muhammad
Baqillani applies Jewish tawatur criteria to Muhammad's prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the Jewish criteria for tawatur to prove the prophethood of Muhammad.

Core Idea
If the Jews accept their own tawatur, they must accept the Muslims' tawatur for Muhammad.

Having gotten the Jews to spell out their conditions for tawatur, Baqillani now turns their own argument against them. He points out that the Muslim community also meets—and even exceeds—those same conditions in transmitting the miracles of Muhammad. Therefore, consistency demands that the Jews accept Muhammad's prophethood just as they accept Moses'.

Guided Path
1
See the logical pivot
Baqillani asks: 'What prevents you from acknowledging Muhammad's prophethood?' This is the moment he turns their criterion against them.
2
List the Muslim transmission conditions
Notice how Baqillani enumerates the same conditions for the Muslim transmission: large number, diversity of natures and motives, distant lands, impossibility of lying.
He mirrors the Jewish formulation.
3
Identify the two categories of signs
Baqillani distinguishes between signs transmitted universally (like the Qur'an) and those transmitted by a chain of authorities (ḥujja to ḥujja) back to the Companions.
This shows the strength of Muslim transmission.
4
Reflect on the argument's strength
If the Jews accept their own transmission as proof, they must logically accept the Muslim transmission. Consistency is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

According to Baqillani, what evidence do Muslims transmit that is universally agreed upon by all communities?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you treat the transmission of Islam as objectively as you treat other historical facts? If not, why? What would it take for you to accept the truth of Muhammad's prophethood based on tawatur alone?
?
If the Jews denied Muhammad's prophethood despite the evidence, what does that teach you about your own potential to deny Allah's signs? Where in your life have you rejected clear proofs because they conflicted with your desires?
?
Baqillani lists conditions for reliable transmission: diversity of goals, motives, sects, lands. Do you apply similar critical thinking to the sources of your own beliefs, or do you accept them uncritically? What belief are you holding onto without evidence?

Prophethood

Proof of Muhammad's Prophethood by Tawatur Analogy
Baqillani proves Muhammad's prophethood by analogy to Jewish tawatur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the principle of tawatur (mass transmission) to argue for Muhammad's prophethood by drawing an analogy to the Jewish acceptance of Moses' miracles.

Core Idea
Mass transmission (tawatur) makes knowledge necessary, even if some deny it.

Baqillani tackles a key objection to Muhammad's prophethood: that only Muslims accept his miracles. He shows that the same standard used by Jews to prove Moses' signs—unbroken mass transmission—can and should be applied to Muhammad's signs. This lesson walks through his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of tawatur
Read the passage to grasp the conditions for tawatur: large number, differing motives, distant lands, diverse sects. The key claim is that lying is impossible for such a group, so their report yields necessary knowledge.
Notice how Baqillani uses 'خلف عن سلف' (successive generations) to emphasize the chain's continuity.
2
See the Jewish case
The Jews transmit Moses' signs (the 'a'lam) through a tawatur that meets all conditions. Baqillani asserts that this makes knowledge of those signs obligatory.
3
Anticipate an objection
The objection is that other groups (Magians, Brahmins) deny these signs. How can transmission produce knowledge if there are deniers? Baqillani presents the reply: tawatur remains valid as long as the report is consistent from beginning to end, regardless of dissenters.
This is a key move: tawatur does not require universal acceptance.
4
Apply the analogy to Muhammad
Now Baqillani turns the tables: Muslims also transmit Muhammad's signs with the same tawatur conditions. Some signs (like the Quran) are universally agreed; others are traced back to Companions who witnessed them. Therefore, Muhammad's prophethood is established by the same logic.
Reflect on why this analogy is powerful: it uses the opponent's own standard against them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدليل على ذلك نقل اليهود خلفاً سلفاً عن قوم بهم تقوم الحجة لما هم عليه من كثرة العدد وتفرق الدواعي والهمم وتباين الأوطان وتباعد الديار واختلاف المذاهب والكذب ممتنع على مثلهم أن موسى عليه السلام أتى بهذه الأعلام التي ذكرناها فوجب العلم بصحتها. يقال لهم: أليس قد أنكر جميع من قدمنا ذكره من المجوس والبراهمة وغيرهم صحة ما نقله أسلافكم وأخلافكم فكيف يكون النقل موجباً للعلم مع إنكار من أنكره وطعن من طعن فيه. فإن قالوا: إذا استوى أول الخبر وطرفاه من آخره ووسطه ثبتت صحته ووجب العلم بصدق نقلته وإن خالف في ذلك مخالفون. يقال لهم: ما أنكرتم أن يكون محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم نبياً وأن يكون ما أثبته المسلمون من أعلامه صحيحاً بنقل من نقل ذلك من المسلمين؟ وذلك أن المسلمين في وقتنا هذا قوم ببعضهم يثبت التواتر وتقوم الحجة؛ وقد نقلوا خلفاً عن سلف مع كثرة عددهم وتنافر طباعهم وتباين أغراضهم ودواعيهم واختلاف آرائهم ومذاهبهم وتفرق أوطانهم وامتناع جواز الكذب على مثلهم أن محمداً صلى الله عليه وسلم أتى بالأعلام الباهرة والبراهين اللائحة، فمنها ما قد أطبقوا جميعاً وسائر أهل الملل على نقله والعلم به كالقرآن، ومنها ما أخبرت الحجة من المسلمين أنها أخذته عن حجة والحجة عن مثلها حتى ينتهي ذلك إلى قوم نقلوه بحضرة جماعة الصحابة وأضافوه إلى مشاهدتهم وعلموا تصديقهم لما ادعي عليهم وإقرارهم بصحته كالذي نُقل من أعلام موسى وادعي فيه مشاهدة سلف عاصره، فوجب القضاء بنبوة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم.
The proof of that is the transmission of the Jews, generation after generation, from a people by whom the proof is established because of their great number, divergence of motives and ambitions, difference of homelands, distance of lands, and variety of sects; lying is impossible for the likes of them that Moses, peace be upon him, brought these signs which we mentioned, so knowledge of their soundness is necessary. It is said to them: Did not all those we mentioned before from the Magians, Brahmins, and others deny the soundness of what your predecessors and successors transmitted? So how can transmission be productive of knowledge despite the denial of deniers and the criticism of critics? If they say: When the beginning of the report and its two ends—its end and its middle—are equal, its soundness is established and knowledge of the truthfulness of its transmitters is necessary, even if dissenters dissent. It is said to them: What prevents you from acknowledging that Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, is a prophet and that what the Muslims have established of his signs is sound through the transmission of those who transmitted that from the Muslims? And that is because the Muslims in our present time are a people by whom tawatur is established and proof is made; and they have transmitted, generation after generation, with their great number, disagreement of their natures, difference of their aims and motives, variance of their opinions and sects, and dispersion of their lands, and the impossibility of lying for the likes of them, that Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, brought brilliant signs and clear proofs. Among them is what they have all unanimously transmitted and what all the people of religions have transmitted and known, such as the Qur'an. And among them is what a reliable authority from the Muslims has told that he received it from a reliable authority, and the reliable authority from the like of it, until that reaches a people who transmitted it in the presence of the group of Companions and attributed it to their witnessing, and they knew their confirmation of what was claimed to them and their acknowledgment of its soundness, like what was transmitted of the signs of Moses and claimed therein the witnessing of the earlier generation that coexisted with him. So judgment is made of the prophethood of Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is a proof (dalīl) for the prophethood of Muhammad (s) based on the principle of tawatur (mass transmission). The author begins by noting that the Jews' transmission of the signs of Musa (a) meets the criteria of tawatur—large numbers, differing motives, distant lands, diverse sects—so lying is impossible; thus, the signs are known to be true. He then anticipates an objection: if some people (Magians, Brahmins) deny these signs, how can transmission be knowledge? The opponent replies that when a report is consistent from beginning to end, its truth is necessary even if some deny it. The author then makes the key analogy: why do you not accept the same for Muhammad? The Muslim community today also meets all conditions of tawatur—great number, divergent natures, aims, opinions, and lands, making lying impossible. They transmit that Muhammad (s) brought brilliant signs, some universally agreed upon like the Qur'an, and others traced through a chain of reliable authorities back to the Companions who witnessed them firsthand and affirmed them. Just as the Jews' transmission of Musa's signs is accepted despite deniers, so too should Muslim transmission of Muhammad's signs be accepted, thereby establishing his prophethood.

Key Terms
تواتر
الحجة
الأعلام
النقل
خلف عن سلف
ضرورة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that tawatur requires universal acceptance and that denial by any group negates it.
Correction: Baqillani shows that tawatur only requires consistency within the chain and that denial by outsiders does not invalidate it, as seen in the Jewish case.

Checkpoint
What is the main argument used by Baqillani to prove Muhammad's prophethood?
A) Direct miraculous proof witnessed by all
B) Analogy to the Jewish transmission of Musa's signs
C) Consensus of all religious communities
D) Logical necessity without transmission

Key Takeaway
The tawatur of Muslim transmission of Muhammad's miracles is logically parallel to the Jewish tawatur of Moses' miracles, thus establishing his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear someone dismiss the miracles of the Prophet as myths, do you feel your own certainty shaken? What evidence from this lesson can you hold onto to steady your heart, and what specific step will you take this week to strengthen your conviction in the tawatur of the Qur'an?
?
The Jews deny Muhammad despite their own tawatur for Musa. Are there areas in your life where you reject truth because it is uncomfortable or inconvenient? Pause and identify one truth you have been avoiding, and commit to acting on it within 24 hours.
?
If the proof of prophethood is as clear as the tawatur described, why do you sometimes hesitate to share Islam with others? Is it from lack of knowledge or from fear? Resolve to learn one argument from this lesson by heart and share it with someone before this week ends.

Refutation of the Few Transmitters Objection
Baqillani refutes an objection about few early Muslim transmitters using parity with Jewish transmission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses parity of reasoning to refute the objection that the early Muslim transmitters were too few to establish tawatur.

Core Idea
Consistency demands accepting Muslim transmission if you accept Jewish transmission.

Imam Baqillani faces a common objection: early Muslim transmitters were few and could have lied, so their reports don't give certain knowledge. He responds with a powerful counter-argument, showing that the same objection would apply to the Jewish transmission of Moses' miracles. In this passage, you'll see his precise reasoning and how he turns the opponent's claim against them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the back-and-forth structure: objection, reply, rejoinder, final answer.
2
Identify the opponent's objection
Find the sentence where the opponent states their claim about the early Muslims being few and why that prevents knowledge.
3
Identify Baqillani's counter-argument
Look for how Baqillani turns the objection back on the opponent, using the example of Jewish transmission of Moses' signs.
The phrase 'fama an kartum' indicates the counter-argument.
4
Analyze the rejoinder and final answer
See how the opponent tries to distinguish the Jewish case, and how Baqillani responds by showing the Muslim case is parallel.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قالوا: سلف المسلمين الذين أخذ النقل عنهم كانوا قلة ونفراً يجوز على مثلهم الكذب وإن كان خلفهم اليوم بخلاف هذه الصفة فلذلك لم يجب العلم بصدقهم. قيل لهم: فما أنكرتم أن يكون السلف الذين نقلوا في الأصل أعلام موسى عليه السلام قلة ونفراً يجوز على مثلهم الكذب فلذلك لم يجب ثبوتها وعلم البراهمة والمجوس بصحتها؟ فإن قالوا: قد أخبرت اليهود وهم اليوم حجة أنهم أخذوا هذا النقل عن قوم هم حجة كهم وعمن نقل بحضرة الحجة وادعى حضورهم لإخراج اليد بيضاء ومشاهدتهم لذلك فأمسكوا عن إنكاره. قيل لهم: فكذلك المسلمون وهم اليوم حجة بل بعضهم يخبرون أنهم أخذوا نقلهم عن حجة كهم وممن نقل بحضرة الحجة فلم ينكر ما نقله مع ادعائه حضورهم.
And if they say: The predecessors of the Muslims from whom the transmission was taken were few in number and a small group for whom lying is possible, even though their successors today are not of this description, therefore knowledge of their truthfulness is not necessary. It is said to them: What prevents you from acknowledging that the predecessors who originally transmitted the signs of Moses, peace be upon him, were few in number and a small group for whom lying is possible, therefore their establishment and the knowledge of the Brahmins and Magians of their soundness is not necessary? If they say: The Jews have reported, and they today are a proof, that they took this transmission from a people who are a proof like them, and from one who transmitted in the presence of the proof and claimed their presence for the extraction of the white hand and their witnessing of that, so they refrained from denying it. It is said to them: Similarly the Muslims, while they today are a proof, indeed some of them report that they took their transmission from a proof like them and from one who transmitted in the presence of the proof, so he did not deny what he transmitted with his claim of their presence.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and answer. The opponent argues that the early Muslims who transmitted Muhammad's signs were few and could have lied, so their transmission cannot yield knowledge. The author's reply is a counter-argument by parity: the early Jews who transmitted Musa's signs were also few and could have lied, so by the same reasoning their transmission should also be invalid—yet the opponent accepts it. The opponent then says that the Jews today report that their transmission goes back to a reliable chain, including witnesses who saw the miracle of the white hand, and thus they refrained from denying it. The author answers that the Muslims similarly have today a reliable chain; some Muslims report that they took their transmission from a reliable source and from one who transmitted in the presence of a reliable witness, and no one denied what he transmitted along with his claim of their presence. Thus, if the opponent accepts the Jewish claim, he must also accept the Muslim claim on the same basis.

Key Terms
سلف
خلف
قلة
حجة
ادعاء
مشاهدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that a small number of early transmitters invalidates Muslim tawatur but does not affect Jewish transmission because Jews have a continuous chain.
Correction: Baqillani shows that both traditions have similar chains, so consistency requires accepting both or rejecting both. The objection fails because it is applied selectively.

Checkpoint
How does Baqillani respond to the objection that early Muslim transmitters were too few?
A) He denies that they were few.
B) He argues that later numbers compensate.
C) He points out that the same objection applies to Jewish transmission of Musa's signs.
D) He says that a few witnesses are sufficient for tawatur.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani shows that the same reasoning applies to Jewish transmission of Moses' signs, so the objection fails due to inconsistency.

Baqillani's Response to the Claim of Necessary Knowledge from Tawatur
Baqillani counters the claim that tawatur must yield necessary knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's method of refuting the objection that Muslim transmission must produce necessary knowledge, and how he turns the opponent's accusation back against them.

Core Idea
If you allow lying in one part of a chain, you allow it in all.

In this passage, Baqillani confronts a critical objection from skeptics who argue that since Muslim transmission does not produce necessary knowledge for everyone, it cannot be reliable. He responds by exposing a fatal inconsistency in the opponent's position: if they permit the possibility of lying when Muslims claim to have received the transmission from a proof, then they must permit that possibility in every part of the transmission. This effectively dismantles the opponent's own argument and restores the integrity of the transmission.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the Arabic passage once through, then read the translation. Notice the structure: first the opponent's claim, then Baqillani's reply.
The passage ends mid-sentence, but the argument is complete in its logic.
2
Identify the opponent's claim
The opponent asserts that if the transmission were true as claimed, it would produce necessary knowledge (darura). Underline the phrase 'لعلمنا صدقهم ضرورة'.
3
Analyze Baqillani's counter-argument
Baqillani points out that the opponent already allows lying against today's Muslims when they say 'we received this from a proof.' This is the key: once lying is allowed in that claim, it is allowed in all claims and transmissions.
Notice the term 'تجويز الكذب' (allowing lying) — this is the pivot of the argument.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this response defeats the objection. If the opponent concedes that lying is possible in the link to the proof, then the entire chain becomes suspect, and the demand for necessary knowledge becomes impossible to meet — even for the opponent's own position.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: لو كان ذلك كما يدعون لعلمنا صدقهم فيما نقلوه ضرورة. قيل لهم: أول ما في هذا تجويزكم الكذب على عدد المسلمين اليوم في قولهم إنهم أخذوا ذلك عن حجة وإن جاز الكذب عليهم في هذه الدعوى جاز عليهم في جميع ما يدعونه وينقلونه وجاز أيضاً على
If they say: If that were as they claim, we would know their truthfulness in what they transmitted necessarily. It is said to them: The first thing in this is your allowing of lying against the number of Muslims today in their saying that they received that from a proof. And if lying is allowed against them in this claim, then it is allowed against them in everything they claim and transmit, and it is also allowed against...
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage presents a third objection and its partial answer. The opponent argues that if the Muslim transmission were truly as claimed (i.e., meeting tawatur conditions), it would produce necessary knowledge (darura) for everyone, but since it does not, it must be false. The author counters by pointing out the inconsistency in the opponent's position: the opponent allows the possibility of lying against today's Muslims when they say they received their transmission from a reliable source. If lying is possible in that claim, then it is also possible in all other claims and transmissions they make. The argument is that if you doubt one link, the whole chain becomes suspect. The text cuts off mid-sentence at the bottom of the page, but the intended conclusion is clear: the opponent's position leads to an infinite regress or total skepticism.

Key Terms
ضرورة
تجويز الكذب
حجة
دعوى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Tawatur must produce necessary knowledge for everyone, or else it is unreliable.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the opponent's own allowance of lying in one claim makes it impossible to claim necessity, thus the argument against tawatur is self-defeating.

Checkpoint
What is the author's initial response to the claim that Muslim transmission should produce necessary knowledge?
A) He agrees that it does produce necessary knowledge.
B) He argues that necessary knowledge is not required for tawatur.
C) He points out that the opponent allows lying against Muslims in one claim, so it is allowed in all.
D) He says the transmission is not actually tawatur.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani defeats the objection by showing that if lying is possible in one claim, it is possible in all, making the opponent's demand for necessary knowledge self-defeating.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

The Parity Argument for Prophethood
Baqillani argues from transmitted signs of Moses to Muhammad's prophethood and refutes an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the transmission of Moses' signs to argue for Muhammad's prophethood and how he refutes the objection about few transmitters by parity of reasoning.

Core Idea
If Jewish transmission is valid, Muslim transmission is equally valid.

Baqillani presents a powerful analogical argument: the very method used to establish the miracles of Moses—continuous transmission from witnesses—also establishes the prophethood of Muhammad. He then anticipates and refutes an objection about the number of transmitters, showing that the objection would undermine Jewish transmission as well.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: a positive argument followed by an objection-and-response.
2
Identify the core analogy
Find where Baqillani compares the transmission of Moses' signs to the transmission of Muhammad's signs. What is the logical link?
He argues that both rely on the same method of tawatur (continuous transmission).
3
Analyze the objection and response
The opponent claims early Muslim transmitters were few and could lie. Baqillani responds by turning the argument back: the same applies to Jewish transmitters of Moses' signs. Understand why this refutes the objection symmetrically.
This is a classic strategy of 'qiyas' (analogical parity).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأضافوه إلى مشاهدتهم وعلموا تصديقهم لما ادعي عليهم وإقرارهم بصحته كالذي نُقل من أعلام موسى وادعي فيه مشاهدة سلف عاصره فوجب القضاء بنبوة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم . وإن قالوا : سلفُ المسلمين الذين أخذ النقل عنهم كانوا قلة ونفراً يجوز على مثلهم الكذب وإن كان خلفهم اليوم بخلاف هذه الصفة فلذلك لم يجب العلم بصدقهم قيل لهم : فما أنكرتم أن يكون السلف الذين نقلوا في الأصل أعلام موسى عليه السلام قلة ونفراً يجوز على مثلهم الكذب فلذلك لم يجب ثبوتها وعلم البراهمة والمجوس بصحتها؟ فإن قالوا : قد أخبرت اليهود وهم اليوم حجة أنهم أخذوا هذا النقل عن قوم هم حجة كهم وعمن نقل بحضرة الحجة وادعى حضورهم لإخراج اليد بيضاء ومشاهدتهم لذلك فأمسكوا عن إنكاره قيل لهم : فكذلك المسلمون وهم اليوم حجة بل بعضهم يخبرون أنهم أخذوا نقلهم عن حجة كهم وممن نقل بحضرة الحجة فلم ينكر ما نقله مع ادعائه حضورهم .
And they added it to their witnessing and knew their confirmation of what was claimed upon them and their acknowledgment of its correctness, like what was transmitted of the signs of Moses and it was claimed therein the witnessing of the predecessors of his era, so it became necessary to judge the prophethood of Muhammad, peace be upon him. And if they say: The predecessors of the Muslims from whom the transmission was taken were few and a small group; lying is possible upon the like of them, even though their successors today are not of this description, therefore necessary knowledge of their truthfulness does not obtain. Say to them: What prevents you from considering that the predecessors who transmitted originally the signs of Moses, peace be upon him, were few and a small group, so that lying is possible upon the like of them, and therefore their establishment and the knowledge of the Brahmins and Magians of its correctness does not obtain? If they say: The Jews, who are today an authoritative group (hujja), have informed that they took this transmission from a people who are an authoritative group like them, and from one who transmitted in the presence of the authoritative group and claimed their presence for the extraction of the white hand and their witnessing of that, so they refrained from denying it. Say to them: Likewise the Muslims, who are today an authoritative group, and some of them inform that they took their transmission from an authoritative group like them, and from one who transmitted in the presence of the authoritative group, and he did not deny what he transmitted with his claim of their presence.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is both a positive argument and a refutation of an objection. Baqillani first states that the same method used to establish the miracles of Moses—namely, the continuous transmission (tawatur) of reports that the predecessors witnessed his signs—also necessitates the prophethood of Muhammad, because the transmission of Muhammad's signs is analogous. Then he anticipates an objection: the opponents might say that the early Muslim transmitters were few and could have conspired to lie, so their testimony cannot yield certain knowledge. Baqillani turns the argument back on them: if that is true, then the same applies to the transmission of Moses' signs—the Jewish predecessors were also few and could have lied, so the Brahmins and Magians are not obliged to accept them. The opponent then tries to rescue Jewish transmission by noting that the Jews today are an authoritative group (hujja) who claim to have received the transmission from an authoritative chain and that the original witnesses did not deny it when claimed in their presence. Baqillani responds that the same is true of the Muslims: they are today an authoritative group, and some of them claim that they received their transmission from an authoritative chain, and that the original witnesses did not deny it. So the objection fails because parity of reasoning.

Key Terms
سلف (predecessors)
نقل (transmission)
حجة (authoritative group)
ضرورة (necessity)
إقرار (acknowledgment)
مشاهدة (witnessing)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection that early Muslim transmitters were few is a valid criticism of Islamic transmission.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the same criticism applies to Jewish transmission of Moses' signs, so it is self-defeating; if accepted, it would undermine Judaism, which the opponent does not accept.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of Baqillani's response to the objection that early Muslim transmitters were few?
A) He admits the weakness of Muslim transmission.
B) He argues that Jewish transmission is equally vulnerable.
C) He claims that Muslims today are more reliable than Jews.
D) He denies the objection outright.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's parity argument shows that if Jewish transmission of Moses' signs is accepted, then Muslim transmission of Muhammad's signs must also be accepted.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you accept the miracles of Moses based on Jewish transmission, on what grounds could you reject the same type of transmission for Muhammad? Examine your own heart: is there a bias that makes you demand more evidence from Muslims than from others?
?
Baqillani uses the parity argument to force consistency. Where in your life do you apply different standards to evidence from different sources? How would your beliefs change if you applied the same standard everywhere? What would you have to let go of?
?
The opponent tried to exempt Jewish transmission by appealing to the status of later Jews. Have you ever given your own tradition a pass while demanding proof from others? Would you be willing to apply Baqillani's test to your most deeply held assumptions? If not, why not?
