The Necessity of an Uncarried Carrier in Transmission
Baqillani refutes objections about the carriers of Moses' signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the logical necessity of an uncarried transmitter to defend the transmission of Muhammad's signs.

Core Idea
Every transmission chain needs an uncarried carrier; the same logic proves Muhammad's signs.

Imam Baqillani addresses a skeptical objection that challenges the reliability of prophetic transmission. By analyzing who 'carried' the transmission of Moses' signs, he shows that any chain must have a group that transmitted freely without external compulsion. This logical principle then defends the transmission of Muhammad's signs.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the passage and identify the opponent's possible positions regarding who carried the transmission of Moses' signs.
The opponent presents three alternatives; each is refuted.
2
Follow Baqillani's rebuttal
Trace how Baqillani refutes each claim, leading to the conclusion that an uncarried group must exist.
Notice the logical necessity: freedom of choice in transmission.
3
Apply the principle to Muhammad
See how Baqillani turns the argument: if the uncarried group exists for Moses, it can exist for Muhammad, nullifying the objection.
This is the decisive move that defends prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحاملون لأنفسهم أم غيرهم ممن باين ملتهم وكذب نبيهم حملهم على نقل أعلامه بالسيف؟ فإن قالوا غيرهم حملهم مع تكذيبهم لنبيهم تجاهلوا وتركوا قولهم وما توجبه قضية العقل والعادة، وإن قالوا: هم الحاملون لأنفسهم على نقل أعلام نبيهم قيل لهم: فكيف يحمل الحامل نفسه على الشيء إلا من حيث لو آثروا ترك النقل لصاروا إليه ووقع؟ فهذا يعود إلى أنهم نقلوا ذلك مختارين للنقل. وإن قالوا: إنما صاروا محمولين على النقل بأن حمل بعضهم بعضاً، يقال لهم: فلا بد أن تكون فيهم فرقة غير محمولة هي لغيرها؛ فإذا قالوا: هو كذلك، قيل لهم: فما أنكرتم أن تكون أعلام محمد صلّى الله عليه وسلم صحيحة ثابتة بنقل تلك الطبقة التي هي غير محمولة أصلاً؟ وهذا يبطل تعلقهم بالحمل.
Were they the carriers of themselves or others who differed from their religion and denied their prophet carried them to transmit his signs by the sword? If they say 'others carried them while denying their prophet,' they are being ignorant and abandoning their statement and what the judgment of reason and custom necessitates. And if they say 'they were the carriers of themselves to transmit their prophet's signs,' it is said to them: How could a carrier carry himself to something except from the standpoint that if they preferred to abandon the transmission they would have resorted to it and it occurred? So this returns to the fact that they transmitted that freely choosing the transmission. And if they say: 'They only became carried upon transmission because some of them carried others,' it is said to them: Then there must be among them an uncarried group that is [carrier] for others; so when they say: 'It is so,' it is said to them: What prevents you from accepting that the signs of Muhammad, peace be upon him, are sound and established by the transmission of that class which is essentially uncarried? And this nullifies their clinging to the notion of being carried.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer structure within the broader argument about the reliability of prophetic transmission. The author, Imam Baqillani, addresses a hypothetical opponent (likely Jews or skeptics) who deny the transmission of Muhammad's miracles by analogy with Moses. The opponent first questions who carried the transmission of Moses' signs: were the carriers themselves (the Jews) or others who differed in religion and denied Moses? If they claim others carried it while denying Moses, that is self-contradictory and defies reason and custom. If they claim the Jews themselves carried it, then they must have done so willingly, not under compulsion. If they claim some Jews carried others, then there must be an initial uncarried group that transmitted freely. Baqillani then turns the argument against the opponent: if there is an uncarried group in the transmission of Moses' signs, why cannot the same be said for the transmission of Muhammad's signs? This undermines the opponent's objection.

Key Terms
الحاملون
النقل
أعلام
الطبقة غير المحمولة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument is about historical accuracy of transmission.
Correction: It is about logical necessity: any chain requires an uncarried transmitter.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what logical consequence follows if the Jews were 'carried' by some of them?
A) The transmission is unreliable.
B) There must be an uncarried group that transmitted freely.
C) The signs of Muhammad are also carried.
D) The Jews were forced to transmit.

Key Takeaway
The transmission of prophetic signs must have an uncarried carrier; this applies equally to Moses and Muhammad.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own life, when you pass on what you believe about Islam, are you an 'uncarried carrier' — freely convinced from within — or are you being carried by family, culture, or fear of standing out? What would it take for you to become an uncarried carrier of the truth?
?
The argument shows that the transmission chain must have a first link not forced by others. Who was that for you? Was it a parent, a teacher, or did you come to conviction on your own? If you had to stand alone as an uncarried carrier, would your faith hold?
?
Baqillani says the same logic proves Muhammad's signs. But do you personally treat the transmission of Muhammad's message as that certain? If you were asked why you believe the Quran is from God, could you point to this logic, or do you rely on something else? What is that something else, and is it as solid as an uncarried chain?

Objection of Jewish Tawatur and Reply
Objection that Jewish transmission is tawatur; reply about Brahmins and Magians.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the objection of Jewish tawatur by pointing to the denial of other groups and turning the argument back on the opponent using parity of reasoning.

Core Idea
Tawatur does not force belief if the opponent is biased.

In this objection, the opponent argues that the Jewish community's continuous transmission of Moses' miracles makes their report undeniable. The author counters by asking why other groups like Brahmins and Magians deny it, and then turns the same reasoning against the opponent using Muslim transmission of Muhammad's miracles. This lesson walks through the logic of the reply.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection from the opponent
The opponent claims that the Jews today are mutawatir in reporting that their ancestors transmitted the miracles of Moses, so their report must be true.
What is the basis of their claim?
2
Analyze the author's first response
The author asks: why do Brahmins, Magians, and others not know this and deny it? This challenges the universality of the Jewish claim.
This shows that tawatur does not compel acceptance from everyone.
3
See how the argument is turned back
If the opponent says those groups are stubborn, then the same applies to the opponent regarding Muslim tawatur. The author points out that Muslims today are also mutawatir in reporting Muhammad's miracles, yet the opponent denies them stubbornly.
The objection is refuted by parity of reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: قد أخبرت اليهود اليوم، وهم أهل تواتر أن سلفهم كخلفهم فوجب صدقهم في ذلك، قيل لهم: فما بال البراهمة والمجوس وأهل الإلحاد والتنجيم والفلاسفة لا يعلمون ذلك ويجحدونه وينكرونه؟ فإن قالوا: هم يعلمون ذلك ولكنهم يكابرون، قيل لهم: فكذلك المسلمون قد أخبروا اليوم وهم أهل تواتر، أنهم أخذوا النقل عن سلف كخلفهم ومن آحاد نقلوا بحضرة من هو كخلفهم وادعوا حضورهم وسلّموا نقلهم فوجب صدقهم وأنتم وكل واحد تعلمون ذلك ولكنكم تجحدون وتعاندون ولا جواب عن ذلك.
Then if they say: 'The Jews today have reported, and they are people of tawatur (mass transmission), that their predecessors are like their successors, so their truthfulness in that is necessary,' it is said to them: 'What is the matter with the Brahmins, Magians, people of atheism, astrology, and philosophers – they do not know that, deny it, and reject it?' If they say: 'They know that but they are stubborn,' it is said to them: 'Likewise, the Muslims today have reported, and they are people of tawatur, that they took the transmission from predecessors like their successors and from individuals who transmitted in the presence of those who are like their successors, and they claimed their presence, and they accepted their transmission, so their truthfulness is necessary, and you and everyone know that but you deny and oppose, and there is no answer to that.'
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This is another objection-answer pair. The opponent argues that the Jewish community today is mutawatir (massively transmitted) in reporting that their ancestors transmitted the miracles of Moses, so their report is necessarily true. The author counters by asking: why then do Brahmins, Magians, atheists, astrologers, and philosophers not know this and deny it? If the opponent responds that these groups know it but are stubborn, then the author turns the argument back: likewise, the Muslims today are mutawatir in reporting Muhammad's miracles, yet the opponent (Jews) also deny stubbornly. Thus the opponent's objection is invalid because the same logic would apply to them.

Key Terms
تواتر
يكابرون
يجحدون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Jewish tawatur proves their religion true beyond doubt.
Correction: The author shows that tawatur can be denied by stubborn opponents, so it does not force acceptance; moreover, the same argument applies to Muslim tawatur.

Checkpoint
What is the author's first response to the claim that the Jews are mutawatir?
A) The Jews are not mutawatir.
B) Brahmins and Magians do not know or deny the Jewish report.
C) The Muslims are also mutawatir.
D) The Jews are lying.

Key Takeaway
The objection of Jewish tawatur fails because the same logic applies to Muslim tawatur and the opponent's stubbornness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself rejecting a clear truth simply because it came from a person or group you dislike? What would it take for you to admit that you are stubborn like the opponents in this passage? Commit to one concrete step to overcome that bias today.
?
When someone presents a counter-argument that is logically parallel to your own, do you honestly engage with it or do you dismiss it? Think of a time you did the latter. What would change if you applied the same standard to yourself?
?
Is there a religious or intellectual claim you hold to be 'mutawatir' in your own mind that others reject? This passage warns that your certainty may be a result of stubbornness rather than evidence. Ask yourself: Am I willing to be wrong? If not, why not?

Objection: Miracles as Tricks; Reply with Parallel
Objection that Moses' miracles were tricks; reply with parallel for Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Baqillani refutes the claim that Moses' miracles were merely tricks and draws a parallel to the miracles of Muhammad (ﷺ).

Core Idea
Claiming miracles are tricks is inconsistent; opponents of Moses deny them outright, just as you deny Muhammad's miracles.

Imam al-Baqillani continues his defense of prophethood by addressing a recurring objection: that the miracles of Moses were not denied, but were dismissed as tricks. He shows this claim is false by examining the actual stance of Brahmins, Magians, and others. Then, he turns the argument on the opponent, drawing a parallel to their own denial of the Prophet Muhammad's miracles. This lesson reveals the dialectical power of consistency in theological argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Understand the opponent's claim that miracles are tricks, not denials. The opponent says Brahmins, Magians, etc. do not deny Moses' miracles but consider them tricks.
2
Follow the refutation
See how al-Baqillani refutes this by stating that these groups actually deny the miracles entirely (splitting the sea, white hand, water). Any admission is only dialectical.
3
Observe the parallel
Notice how the author turns the argument: the opponent (Jews) themselves do not privately deny Muhammad's miracles but call them tricks, exposing inconsistency.
The author uses the same logic to show the opponent's stance is untenable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: ليس تنكر البراهمة والمجوس والفلاسفة والملحدة ظهور هذه الأمور على يد موسى وإنما يدعون أنها حيل ومخاريق، قيل لهم: ليس كذلك كما تقولون لأنهم جميعاً ينكرون فلق البحر وخروج اليد بيضاء من الصخرة ونبع الماء جملةً وإنما يستضعفون بعض من يُسلمون له ذلك جدلاً طمعاً في انتهاز فرصته وإظهار كل وجه. وقيل لهم: وكذلك أنتم لا تنكرون إذا خلوتم بأنفسكم أن يكون محمد صلّى الله عليه وسلم أتى بهذه المعجزات الخارقة للعادة وإنما تظنون أنها حيل ومخاريق فإن قالوا: لسنا نقول ذلك قيل لهم: وكذلك البراهمة والمجوس وأهل الإلحاد لا يُقِرُّون بوجود شيء مما تدَّعُونه لموسى عليه السلام ولا جواب عن ذلك.
Then if they say: 'The Brahmins, Magians, philosophers, and atheists do not deny the appearance of these things at the hands of Moses; they only claim that they are tricks and deceptions,' it is said to them: 'It is not as you say, because they all deny the splitting of the sea, the emerging of the white hand from the rock, and the gushing of water entirely; they only feebly [admit] some of it to those who concede it to them dialectically, hoping to seize an opportunity and show every aspect.' And it is said to them: 'Likewise, you yourselves, when you are alone, do not deny that Muhammad, peace be upon him, brought these miracles that break custom; rather, you think they are tricks and deceptions.' If they say: 'We do not say that,' it is said to them: 'Likewise, the Brahmins, Magians, and atheists do not acknowledge the existence of anything you claim for Moses, peace be upon him, and there is no answer to that.'
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage continues the objection-answer sequence. The opponent claims that Brahmins etc. do not deny the occurrence of Moses' miracles, but consider them tricks. The author refutes this by stating that these groups actually deny the miracles outright (splitting the sea, white hand, water from rock); any partial admission is merely dialectical. Then the author turns the argument: similarly, the opponent (Jews) in private do not deny that Muhammad performed miracles, but they call them tricks. If they protest, the author points out that the Brahmins likewise deny Moses' miracles, so consistency fails. This is a symmetrical rebuttal.

Misconception: Some think that opponents of Moses admit his miracles but dismiss them as tricks.
Correction: In reality, these groups deny the miracles entirely; any apparent admission is merely for dialectical purposes.

Checkpoint
Do the Brahmins and Magians actually admit Moses' miracles according to the author?
A) Yes, they admit them fully.
B) They admit them but call them tricks.
C) They deny them outright.
D) They have no opinion.

Key Takeaway
Claiming miracles are tricks is inconsistent because opponents of Moses actually deny them outright, and the same logic applies to those who deny Muhammad's miracles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This passage forces you to confront the inconsistency of rejecting a truth while accepting its equivalent. Where in your own heart do you hold a double standard—accepting something for yourself or your group that you deny to others? How can you repent from this and embrace full submission to the truth?

Objection: Non-Muslims Deny Miracles – Response
Baqillani defends Muslim miracles against the charge that non-Muslims deny them knowingly.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the tu quoque argument to defend Muslim miracles against the charge that non-Muslims knowingly deny them.

Core Idea
Non-Muslims deny miracles not from ignorance but from obstinacy, just as the objector denies.

Baqillani anticipates a common objection: if miracles are so clear, why don't non-Muslims accept them? His response is sharp and symmetrical. In this passage, he turns the objection back on the questioner, showing that the very same charge applies to them. Let's dive into the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the direct question-and-answer style.
2
Identify the objection and response
The objector lists groups that deny miracles. Baqillani first presents a possible reply, then turns it against the objector. Identify each part.
3
Reflect on the tu quoque logic
Consider how the same accusation is mirrored back. Why is this an effective counterargument?
This connects to the broader theme of tawātur and obstinacy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قيل لهم : فما بال البراهمة والمجوس وأهل الإلحاد والتنجيم والفلاسفة لا يعلمون ذلك ويجحدونه وينكرونه؟ فإن قالوا : هم يعلمون ذلك ولكنهم يكابرون ، قيل لهم : فكذلك المسلمون قد أخبروا اليوم وهم أهل تواتر، أنهم أخذوا النقل عن سَلَفٍ كَخَلَفِهم ومِنْ آحاد نقلوا بحضرة من هو كخَلَفِهم وادعوا حضورهم وسلّموا نقلهم فوجب صِدْقُهم وأنتم وكل واحد تعلمون ذلك ولكنكم تجحدون وتعاندون ولا جواب عن ذلك.
It was said to them: What is the matter with the Brahmins, the Magians, the people of atheism, astrology, and the philosophers that they do not know that, and they deny it and reject it? If they say: They know that but they stubbornly resist, it was said to them: Likewise, the Muslims have reported today, and they are people of tawātur, that they took the transmission from predecessors like their own successors, and from individuals who transmitted in the presence of one like their successors, and they claimed their presence and accepted their transmission, so their truthfulness must be affirmed, and you and every one know that, but you deny and oppose, and there is no answer to that.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-answer pair in a kalam argument about the evidentiary force of tawātur for miracles. The objector asks: why do non-Muslim groups—Brahmins, Magians, atheists, astrologers, philosophers—not acknowledge the miracles of Moses or Muhammad, and instead deny and reject them? The author anticipates the response that these people secretly know the truth but are obstinate. The author then turns this against the objector: just as those non-Muslims know but stubbornly resist, so too the objectors (Jews or others) are in the same position regarding Muslim reports of miracles. The Muslim community is a tawātur-transmitting community (ahl tawātur) that received the reports from generation to generation, and their truthfulness is binding. The objector himself knows this but denies out of obstinacy. The argument is a tu quoque: the same accusation the objector levels at Muslims applies to him. The passage ends by asserting that there is no valid counterargument (la jawab).

Key Terms
البراهمة
المجوس
الإلحاد
التنجيم
الفلاسفة
تواتر
يكابرون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think non-Muslims are simply ignorant of miracles.
Correction: Baqillani argues that they know but stubbornly deny (يكابرون), turning the accusation back on the objector.

Checkpoint
What does the author argue about non-Muslims who deny miracles?
A) They are ignorant of the miracles.
B) They know the truth but stubbornly deny it.
C) They accept miracles as tricks.
D) They have no knowledge of the reports.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani turns the objection of non-Muslim denial back on the objector, showing that both parties know the truth but some deny obstinately.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The author says 'you and every one know that, but you deny and oppose.' What specific teaching from the Prophet (peace be upon him) do you know to be true but hesitate to fully implement? What is one practical change you will make this week to stop denying and start obeying?

Refuting the 'Miracles as Tricks' Objection
Baqillani refutes the claim that non-Muslims accept miracles as mere tricks.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes the objection that non-Muslims accept miracles as mere tricks by showing their actual denial and using a tu quoque argument.

Core Idea
Non-Muslims deny miracles outright, not just dismiss them as tricks.

In this passage, Baqillani addresses a common objection: that non-Muslims acknowledge the extraordinary events but call them tricks. He refutes this by clarifying their actual denial and then turning the argument back on the objector, showing inconsistency.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the structure: objection, then two-part refutation.
The objection is in the first sentence.
2
Identify the first refutation
Baqillani says non-Muslims deny the miracles entirely (جملة). Find the evidence: they do not accept the splitting of the sea or the white hand.
This is a factual correction.
3
Recognize the tu quoque argument
Baqillani turns the argument: the objector himself, when alone, admits Muhammad's miracles but calls them tricks. This mirrors the non-Muslims' stance.
This shows the objector's inconsistency.
4
Understand the final conclusion
If the objector denies this parallel, Baqillani points out that non-Muslims also deny Moses' miracles. Either way, the objector's position is indefensible.
The refutation is complete and forceful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : ليس تنكر البراهمة والمجوس والفلاسفة والملحدة ظهور هذه الأمور على يد موسى وإنما يدعون أنها حِيَل ومخاريق، قيل لهم : ليس كذلك كما تقولون لأنهم جميعاً ينكرون فلق البحر وخروج اليد بيضاء من الصخرة جُملةً وإنما يَسْتَضْعِفون بعض من يُسلمون له ذلك جدلاً طمعاً في انتهاز فرصته وإظهار عجزه من كل وجه . وقيل لهم : وكذلك أنتم لا تنكرون إذا خلوتم بأنفسكم أن يكون محمد صلّى الله عليه وسلم أتى بهذه المعجزات الخارقة للعادة وإنما تظنون أنها حِيَل ومخاريق فإن قالوا : لسنا نقول ذلك قيل لهم : وكذلك البراهمة والمجوس وأهل الإلحاد لا يُقِرُّون بوجود شيء مما تدَّعُونه لموسى عليه السلام ولا جواب عن ذلك.
If they say: The Brahmins, Magians, philosophers, and atheists do not deny the occurrence of these matters at the hand of Moses, but rather they claim that they are tricks and deceptions, it was said to them: It is not as you say, because they all deny the splitting of the sea and the emergence of the white hand from the rock entirely, and they only belittle some of those who concede that to them argumentatively, hoping to seize an opportunity and show his incapacity from every aspect. And it was said to them: Likewise, you do not deny, when you are alone with yourselves, that Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, performed these extraordinary miracles, but you think that they are tricks and deceptions. If they say: We do not say that, it was said to them: Likewise, the Brahmins, Magians, and people of atheism do not affirm the existence of anything that you claim for Moses, peace be upon him, and there is no answer to that.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is a second objection-answer pair. The objector concedes that non-Muslims acknowledge the extraordinary events (like the splitting of the sea and the white hand) but claim they are tricks (hiyal) and deceptions (makhariq). The author refutes this by asserting that non-Muslims actually deny the events outright (jumpatan), and only a few might reluctantly accept them for the sake of debate to find a loophole to show the prophet's incapacity. The author then turns the argument around: the objector himself, when honest, does not deny that Muhammad performed miracles, but merely dismisses them as tricks. When the objector denies this, the author points out that similarly the non-Muslims do not accept any of the claimed miracles of Moses. Either way, the objector's position is inconsistent, and there is no valid answer to this refutation.

Key Terms
حِيَل
مخاريق
فلق البحر
يد بيضاء
خارقة للعادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think non-Muslims accept the occurrence of miracles but explain them as tricks.
Correction: The author clarifies that non-Muslims deny the miracles entirely, not just reinterpret them.

Checkpoint
How does the author characterize the non-Muslims' stance on Moses' miracles?
A) They accept them as tricks.
B) They deny them entirely.
C) They are uncertain.
D) They claim Moses was a magician.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani shows that the objector's claim is based on a misrepresentation and that the same logic applies to the objector, rendering his argument inconsistent.

Baqillani points out that the objector privately does not deny Muhammad's miracles but dismisses them as tricks. What truth about Islam do you know in your heart but hesitate to fully embrace? What would change if you admitted it openly?
?
The objection collapses because it is inconsistent. Where in your own life are you inconsistent in submitting to the truth? What one step will you take today to align your actions with what you already know to be true?

Jewish Conditions for Tawātur and Refutation of Lineage Diversity
Baqillani presents Jewish conditions for tawātur and refutes the requirement of diverse lineages.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Jewish conditions for tawātur and why Baqillani rejects the condition of diverse lineages.

Core Idea
Tawātur does not require diversity of lineage; mass transmission suffices.

In this passage, Baqillani presents the objections raised by some Jews regarding the conditions for a report to yield conclusive knowledge. They claim that only their transmission meets these conditions, thereby invalidating the prophethood of Muhammad and others. Baqillani refutes their argument, focusing particularly on the unnecessary condition of diverse lineages.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the list of conditions the Jews postulate.
2
Identify the Jewish conditions
The Jews list several conditions for tawātur. Identify each condition from the text and understand what they claim is required.
There are about eight conditions mentioned.
3
Understand their claim of exclusivity
The Jews argue that only their transmission meets all conditions, citing examples of Muslims, Christians, and Magians failing them.
They use this to argue for Moses' miracles alone.
4
Examine Baqillani's refutation of lineage diversity
Baqillani singles out the condition of diverse lineages and declares it meaningless. He argues that even a single lineage, town, or religion can produce tawātur.
5
Reflect on the principle of tawātur
Consider how Baqillani's refutation upholds the reliability of mass transmission regardless of the transmitters' background.
This strengthens the proof of prophethood for Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد زعم كثير من اليهود أن من شرط الخبر الموجب للعلم القاطع للعُذْرِ أن تكون الناقلة لا يَحْصُرُهم عَدَد ولا يَحْوِيهم بَلَد ولا يجوز على مثلهم التكاتُبُ والتراسل وأن تتغايـر آباؤهم وتختلف وتَتَفَرَّقَ دواعيهم وهممُهم وأغراضهم وأن تختلف مللُهم ودياناتهم وألا يحملوا نقلهم بالسيف ولا يَضُمُّوا إلى خبرهم ما تُحِيلُه العقول وأن يكونوا على في دار ذلة وممن تؤخذ منهم الجزية قالوا : وكل هذه الشرائط موجودة في نقل اليهود دون المسلمين والنصارى والمجوس لأن المسلمين محمولون على نقلهم بالسيف والمجوس يقولون بقدم اثنين وعبادة النور وهو شخص محدود والنصارى يقولون بالتثليث وكل هذا تُحيله العقل وتدفعه فالواجب القضاء بصحة أعلام موسى عليه السلام دون أعلام محمد وعيسى وزرادشت وقد تكلمنا عليهم في الحمل على نقل الأعلام بما يغني عن رَدّه؛ وكذلك قد قدمنا القول في اشتراطهم كون النقلة في دار ذلة وممن تؤخذ منهم الجزية وفي ضم ما تُحِيلُه العقل إلى النقل توثيق الخبر بإطباق أهل الملل المختلفة عليه وبينا أنه لا تعلق لهم في شيء مما ذكروه . فأما تغاير الآباء واختلاف الأنساب وتباعد الأوطان والديار فإنه لا معنى له ولا لاشتراطه لأنه لو نقل إلينا خَبَراً عن مشاهدة أهل بلدة واحدة وبَنُو أب واحد وأهل نسب واحد وأهلُ دين واحد وهم أهل تواتر لوجب العِلْمُ بصدقهم وصحة نقلهم وكذلك لو كانت حرفتهم واحدة.
And many Jews have claimed that among the conditions of a report that necessitates conclusive knowledge and cuts off excuse is that the transmitters cannot be counted, cannot be contained in one country, and correspondence and communication among their like is not possible; and that their fathers differ, and their lineages differ, and their motives, ambitions, and purposes are diverse; and that their religions and faiths differ; and that they are not compelled to transmit by the sword; and that they do not add to their report what the intellect deems impossible; and that they be in a state of humiliation and from whom the jizya is taken. They said: All these conditions are found in the transmission of the Jews, not in the Muslims, Christians, or Magians, because the Muslims are compelled to transmit by the sword, the Magians affirm duality and worship light which is a limited entity, and the Christians affirm the Trinity – all of which the intellect deems impossible and rejects. Therefore, judgment must be given to the validity of the signs of Moses, peace be upon him, over the signs of Muhammad, Jesus, and Zoroaster. And we have spoken against them regarding the compulsion to transmit the signs in a way that suffices as a refutation; and likewise, we have already presented the argument regarding their condition that the transmitters be in a state of humiliation and from whom the jizya is taken, and regarding adding what the intellect deems impossible to the report, and regarding strengthening the report by the agreement of different religious communities upon it, and we have shown that they have no basis in anything they mentioned. As for the difference of fathers, diversity of lineages, and remoteness of homelands and dwellings, it has no meaning and no need for stipulating it, because if a report of an observation were transmitted to us from people of one town, children of one father, people of one lineage, people of one religion, and they are people of tawātur, then knowledge of their truthfulness and the soundness of their transmission would be necessary, and likewise if their profession were one.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is a classification and refutation of Jewish objections regarding tawātur. First, the author lists the conditions some Jews impose for a report to yield conclusive knowledge: 1. transmitters cannot be counted or contained in one country; 2. no collusion among them; 3. diverse paternal lineages; 4. diverse motives and ambitions; 5. diverse religions; 6. transmission not coerced by sword; 7. no inclusion of rationally impossible content; 8. transmitters must be subject to humiliation and jizya. The Jews claim these conditions are only met in their own tradition, not in Muslim, Christian, or Magian traditions, citing examples (Muslims coerced by sword, Magian dualism, Christian Trinity as rationally impossible). Therefore, they argue, Moses' miracles are valid but those of Muhammad, Jesus, or Zoroaster are not. The author states that he has already refuted most of these conditions elsewhere, and then he specifically addresses the condition about diverse lineages. He argues that this condition is meaningless: a tawātur report from a single town, single father, single lineage, single religion, or even single profession would still necessitate knowledge and truthfulness. The key point is that tawātur does not require diversity of lineage; the mass of transmitters itself suffices regardless of their background.

تباعد الأوطان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Tawātur requires diversity in lineage, religion, and geography.
Correction: Baqillani argues that tawātur does not require such diversity; even a single lineage, religion, or town can produce conclusive knowledge.

Checkpoint
What is the Jewish condition about the transmitters' lineages that the author rejects?
A) They must be from one lineage.
B) They must have diverse fathers and lineages.
C) They must be from different countries.
D) They must be unrelated.

Key Takeaway
The condition of diverse lineages is unnecessary for tawātur; mass transmission itself suffices for conclusive knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you listen to Islamic teachings passed down through the community, do you sometimes require extraordinary proof before accepting them? What unspoken conditions do you impose, and how might they reflect your own resistance rather than the strength of the transmission? Will you today commit to trusting the mass transmission that millions before you have accepted?
?
The Jews demanded that transmitters be from diverse backgrounds before they would accept news. Think of a time you dismissed a truth because it came from people too similar to you or too different from you. How did that bias prevent you from seeing the truth? Are you willing now to let the weight of testimony alone, as Baqillani argues, guide your certainty?
?
Baqillani refutes the condition of lineage diversity by saying that even a single town, single father group can yield knowledge if their report is tawātur. Your faith rests on reports transmitted by numerous chains. Have you ever treated the unanimity of scholars or the consensus of the community as insufficient because you wanted a more dramatic proof? What will you change today to submit to the simple, mass-transmitted truth of Islam?

Baqillani's Refutation of the 'No Rational Impossibility' Condition (Fragment)
Baqillani declares the condition of no rationally impossible content false.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Imam al-Baqillani rejects the Jewish condition that a tawātur report must not contain rationally impossible content, and recognize that his full argument is found elsewhere.

Core Idea
Even rationally impossible content can be known via tawātur—the intellect is not the final judge.

In this brief passage, Imam al-Baqillani begins his refutation of a Jewish objection: that a widely transmitted report cannot be accepted if it contains something the mind deems impossible. He declares this condition false and begins to explain why, though the text cuts off. This lesson examines the opening of his argument and its significance for the epistemology of miracles.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation. Notice the author's decisive rejection of the condition.
The passage ends mid-sentence; the full argument is not present here.
2
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: If rationally impossible content were disqualifying, what would happen to reports of miracles? This passage hints at Baqillani's defense of miraculous knowledge through tawātur.
The condition was likely proposed by Jewish opponents to reject miracles.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما اشتراطهم ألا يضموا إلى خبرهم ما تُحِيلُه العقول فإنه باطل لأن

Commentary

The author declares that this condition is false (bāṭil) and begins to provide a reason (li-anna), but the text breaks off at the page end. The argument is incomplete in this window. Based on the context, the author likely intends to argue that some rationally impossible content (like miracles) can be known through tawātur, or that the condition is self-defeating. However, the complete reasoning is not present here, so this lesson only documents the fragment.

Correction: Baqillani explicitly states this condition is false, implying that rationally impossible content (e.g., miracles) does not disqualify a report from being tawātur.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The author declares the condition false. In your own life, are there conditions you set on Allah's ability to act? Do you sometimes think, 'That couldn't happen'? Reflect on the implications of limiting Allah's power by your own reasoning. What does this passage demand from you?
?
Imagine you are faced with a report from the Prophet that your intellect finds hard to accept. Will you side with your reason or with the certainty of tawātur? Make a concrete intention to study the evidences of miracles so that your heart submits.

The Signs of Zoroaster: Two Possible Answers
Baqillani presents two possible answers to the objection about Zoroaster's signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's two possible responses to the objection regarding the authenticity of Zoroaster's miracles and how they relate to broader polemics against Magians and Christians.

Core Idea
Zoroaster's signs may be authentic, but their transmission is weak or his message was distorted.

In this passage, Baqillani responds to those who demand proof for the signs attributed to Zoroaster. He presents two alternative explanations: either the reports of these signs are not reliably transmitted, or Zoroaster was truly a prophet but his teachings were later corrupted by the Magians. This mirrors the Christian distortion of Jesus' message.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic text once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Notice how Baqillani uses 'إما... أو...' to structure the two alternatives.
Pay attention to the analogy with Christians at the end.
2
Identify the two alternatives
Locate the two possible answers Baqillani gives. The first concerns the transmission of Zoroaster's signs; the second concerns Zoroaster's prophethood and subsequent distortion.
Each alternative begins with 'إما أن نقول' and 'أو نقول'.
3
Understand the analogy with Christianity
Baqillani compares the Magians' distortion of Zoroaster's teachings to the Christians' distortion of Jesus' message. Reflect on how this analogy supports his argument.
The Christian distortions mentioned are trinity, incarnation, and mixture.
4
Reflect on the implications for prophetic signs
Consider how Baqillani's approach preserves the possibility of Zoroaster being a true prophet while rejecting later additions. What does this say about the reliability of religious traditions?
This ties into broader discussions of tawātur and distortion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك الجواب عن المطالبة بصحة أعلام زرادشت إما أن نقول إنها في الأصل مأخوذة عن آحاد لأن العلم بصدقهم غير واقع لنا أو نقول إنه نبي صادق ظهرت على يده الأعلام ودعا إلى نبوة نوح وإبراهيم وإنما كذبت المجوس عليه في إضافة ما أضافته إليه من القول بالتثنية وقدم النور والظلام وحدوث الشيطان من فكرة وشكة شكها بعض أشخاص النور وهو بمنزلة كذب النصارى على المسيح عليه السلام من دعائه إلى اعتقاد التثليث والاتحاد والاختلاط وأن مريم ولدت مسيحاً بلاهوته دون ناسوته وغير ذلك.
And likewise the answer concerning the demand for the authenticity of the signs of Zoroaster: either we say that they were originally taken from individuals (āḥād), because knowledge of their truthfulness is not actual for us, or we say that he was a truthful prophet upon whose hand signs appeared, and he called to the prophethood of Noah and Abraham, but the Magians lied against him in attributing to him the statement of dualism, the pre-eternity of light and darkness, and the origination of Satan from a thought and doubt that some persons of light entertained. And that is like the lying of the Christians against the Messiah, peace be upon him, regarding his calling to the belief in trinity, union, and mixture, and that Mary gave birth to a messiah by his divinity without his humanity, and other such things.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage concludes Baqillani's refutation of objections against prophetic signs (aʿlām). Opponents demanded the validity of Zoroaster's signs. Baqillani offers two possible answers. The first: the transmission of Zoroaster's signs is from āḥād (individual reports), not mutawātir, so we do not have certain knowledge of their truthfulness. The second: Zoroaster was a true prophet, supporting the prophethood of Noah and Abraham, but the Magians (majūs) distorted his message, attributing to him dualism (tathniya), pre-eternity of light and darkness, and the origin of Satan from a thought/doubt by some persons of light. This distortion parallels the Christians' falsification of Jesus' message, attributing trinity, incarnation (ittiḥād), and mixture (ikhtilāṭ), and the birth of a messiah from divinity without humanity. Thus, the original signs are not invalidated by later corruptions.

زرادشت

Misconception: One might think Baqillani definitively labels Zoroaster as a false prophet.
Correction: Baqillani leaves open the possibility that Zoroaster was a true prophet whose original teachings were corrupted by the Magians, similar to the Christian case.

D) The signs are in the Avesta, and they are authentic.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani offers two defenses of Zoroaster's signs: either their transmission is weak, or Zoroaster's original message was corrupted by the Magians, similar to Christian distortions of Jesus.

Why the Crucifixion Report Fails Tawatur
Baqillani rebuts the Christian claim of crucifixion by challenging its tawatur and presenting substitution theory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani argues that the Christian report of the crucifixion does not meet the criteria for certain knowledge (tawatur) and how doubt undermines its reliability.

Core Idea
Four reporters, one crucifixion, zero certainty.

Baqillani takes on an objection from Christians who claim the crucifixion is known through widespread transmission. He shows that the transmission does not meet the strict conditions of tawatur, and even if true, it could be a case of mistaken identity. This lesson examines his rebuttal and the epistemological standard for certain reports.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: first the Christian claim, then Baqillani's two-part answer.
The passage is an objection-and-answer format.
2
Identify the two refutation prongs
Baqillani gives two arguments: (1) the transmitters are only four individuals who could lie, so it's not tawatur; (2) even if a person was killed, it might not be Jesus due to a change in appearance.
3
Understand the epistemological condition
Baqillani states a general rule: a report yields certain knowledge only when the transmitters are compelled (i.e., eyewitnesses with no collusion) and all doubt is removed. Since these conditions are absent, the claim fails.
This connects to the broader kalam theory of testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : فقد نقلنا ونقلت النصارى أن المسيح قُتِلَ وصلب فيجب القطع بصحة خبرنا قيل لهم : قد قال بعض الأمة وأكثر الناس إن النقل مأخوذ عن أربعة من الحواريين لوقى ومتى ويوحنا ومرقس والأربعة يجوز عليهم الكذب ؛ وقال بعضهم : إنكم صدقتم وصدق أسلافكم في أن شخصاً قتل وصلب ولكنكم توهمتم أنه المسيح لأن المقتول تحول عن صفته هذا وتقع الشبهة في أمره والخبر لا يكون موجباً للعلم حتى تكون الناقلة قد اضطرت إلى ما أخبرت عنه وزالت الشبهة فيه وإذا كان ذلك كذلك بطل ما سألتم عنه .
For if they say: 'We and the Christians have transmitted that the Messiah was killed and crucified, so it is necessary to be certain of the truth of our report,' it is said to them: 'Some of the community and most people have said that the transmission is taken from four of the disciples: Luke, Matthew, John, and Mark, and it is possible for the four to lie; and some of them said: "You have spoken truthfully, and your predecessors spoke truthfully in that a person was killed and crucified, but you mistakenly thought that he was the Messiah, because the killed person had changed into his appearance, and doubt occurs concerning his affair, and a report does not necessitate knowledge until the transmitters are compelled to what they reported, and doubt is removed from it; and if that is the case, then what you asked about is invalid."'
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objectors (presumably Christians or those claiming the crucifixion as historically certain) argue that the crucifixion of Jesus is known through widespread transmission, so it must be certain. Imam Baqillani responds by first noting that the transmission comes from only four individuals (the evangelists), who are not immune to lying, so it is not mutawatir. Secondly, he presents an alternative explanation: the transmitters correctly report that a person was killed and crucified, but they mistakenly identified him as the Messiah, as the victim's appearance was altered (similar to the substitution theory). The author emphasizes that for a report to yield certain knowledge, the transmitters must be compelled by the situation (i.e., eyewitnesses under circumstances preventing collusion) and all doubt must be removed. Since these conditions are not met, the claim of certainty fails. Thus the objection is refuted.

Key Terms
تواتر
خبر
علم
حواريون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think tawatur can be established by a small group (like four individuals) if they are reliable.
Correction: Baqillani shows that tawatur requires a large number of transmitters such that collusion is impossible; four individuals are not sufficient because they could lie.

Checkpoint
What is the first argument Baqillani gives against the certainty of the crucifixion report?
A) The transmitters were not eyewitnesses.
B) The transmitters are only four individuals who could lie.
C) The crucifixion never happened.
D) The report contradicts the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The Christian claim of crucifixion fails because its transmitters are few and fallible, and because doubt persists; thus it does not produce certain knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How many of your deeply held beliefs about the Prophet ﷺ rest on a chain of transmission as weak as four fallible individuals? Will you examine them today, even if it unsettles you?
?
When you hear a story that confirms your emotional attachment, do you rush to accept it without demanding tawatur? What would it cost you to be honest about that?
?
You have likely believed the crucifixion narrative uncritically in the past—from movies, books, or hearsay. Now that you know the kalam critique, will you actively correct that ignorance, or let it slide?

Baqillani's Two-Pronged Refutation of Zoroaster's Claims
Baqillani answers the challenge regarding Zoroaster's miracles and his alleged dualism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani defends against the challenge of Zoroaster's miracles and teachings by offering two distinct rebuttals: questioning the certainty of transmission or accepting the prophet but rejecting the attributed doctrines.

Core Idea
Claims about Zoroaster's miracles and dualism can be refuted either by doubting their transmission or by accepting his prophethood but rejecting Magian additions.

Baqillani continues his defense of Islam against rival religions. Here he addresses the challenge of Zoroaster's claimed signs (a'lam). He presents a two-pronged response: either the reports are not reliably transmitted (ahad), or Zoroaster was a true prophet whose teachings were corrupted by the Magians. This mirrors his earlier argument against Christian claims about Jesus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that Baqillani presents two options separated by 'either...or'.
2
Identify the two responses
Find where Baqillani says 'إما أن نقول' and 'أو نقول'. These are the two answers.
3
Understand the parallel with Christianity
Notice how Baqillani compares the Magians' corruption to the Christians' corruption of Jesus' message. This is a key rhetorical move.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Baqillani ends by asserting that there is no valid question against Muslims in these matters. Why does he say this?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك الجواب عن المطالبة بصحة أعلام زردشت إما أن نقول إنها في الأصل مأخوذة عن آحاد لأن العلم بصدقهم غير واقع لنا أو نقول إنه نبي صادق ظهرت على يده الأعلام ودعا إلى نبوة نوح وإبراهيم وإنما كذبت المجوس عليه في إضافة ما أضافته إليه من القول بالتثنية وقدم النور والظلام وحدوث الشيطان من فكرة وشكة شكها بعض أشخاص النور وهو بمنزلة كذب النصارى على المسيح عليه السلام من دعائه إلى اعتقاد التثليث والاتحاد والاختلاط وأن مريم ولدت مسيحاً بلاهوته دون ناسوته وغير ذلك من جهالاتهم ولا سؤال لهم علينا في شيء من ذلك .
And similarly the answer to the demand for the authenticity of the signs of Zoroaster: either we say that they originally are taken from individuals (ahad), because knowledge of their truthfulness is not realized for us; or we say that he was a truthful prophet upon whose hand signs appeared, and he called to the prophethood of Noah and Abraham, but the Magians lied about him in adding to him what they added of the statement of dualism, the eternity of light and darkness, and the occurrence of the devil from a thought and doubt which some persons of light doubted; and it is analogous to the lying of the Christians against the Messiah (peace be upon him) from his calling to belief in the Trinity, union, mixture, and that Mary gave birth to a Messiah by his divinity without his humanity, and other such ignorances. And there is no question for them against us in any of that.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is another objection-and-answer, now concerning the claimed miracles (a'lam) and teachings of Zoroaster. Baqillani presents two possible responses. First, the transmission of these signs may come from individual reports (ahad) which do not yield certain knowledge, so we are not obliged to accept their truthfulness. Second, even if we accept that Zoroaster was a true prophet (nabi sadiq) who performed miracles and called to the monotheism of earlier prophets (Noah and Abraham), the Magians (majus) have falsely attributed dualistic teachings to him, such as belief in two eternal principles (light and darkness), and that the devil arose from a thought or doubt within the light. Baqillani parallels this to how Christians falsely attributed Trinity and incarnation to Jesus. He concludes that there is no valid objection against Muslims in such matters.

Key Terms
آحاد (ahad)
نبي صادق (nabi sadiq)
مجوس (majus)
تثنية (tathniya)
جهالات (jahalat)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If a religion has widespread teachings, they must be original and authentic.
Correction: Baqillani demonstrates that widespread teachings can be later fabrications added by followers, as seen with the Magians' corruption of Zoroaster's message and Christians' corruption of Jesus' message.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes the challenge of Zoroaster's miracles and dualism by either doubting their transmission or by accepting his prophethood while rejecting later Magian additions, showing that apparent religious teachings can be later fabrications.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Commit to investigating the original source and later history before forming a judgment.
?
The Magians added to Zoroaster's teaching; Christians added to Jesus's message. But what about you? This lesson forces you to confront the possibility that you might be following fabrications. ?

Does this challenge your assumptions about the exclusivity of truth? Use this lesson to reflect on your attitude toward people of other faiths: Are you able to acknowledge truth where it exists while still firmly rejecting falsehood? Ask Allah to guide you to humility and clarity in your da'wah and daily interactions.

Refutation of the Denier of Abrogation from Transmitted Evidence
Baqillani presents and refutes an opponent's argument that a mutawatir report prohibits abrogation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqillani refutes the claim that a mutawatir report from Moses prohibits abrogation by demonstrating that transmitted evidence must be interpreted in light of rational principles.

Core Idea
Transmitted reports are interpreted through rational necessities, not taken absolutely.

Imam Baqillani engages with an opponent who argues that a mutawatir report from Moses declares his law eternal and unchangeable. How can this be reconciled with the possibility of prophethood after Moses? Baqillani demonstrates that even the strongest transmitted evidence must be understood within the framework of rational principles, particularly the necessity to believe a prophet who appears with miracles. This lesson unpacks his dialectical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Identify the opponent's claim and Baqillani's response.
The passage uses dialectical structure: objection and answer.
2
Analyze Baqillani's first argument
Notice how Baqillani questions the interpretation of the report. He argues that the report must be conditional on the absence of a prophet with miracles.
He uses analogy with death and incapacity to show rational conditionality.
3
Understand the opponent's counter and Baqillani's conclusion
The opponent insists the report is absolute due to tawatur. Baqillani counters that the necessity of tawatur itself is subject to rational principles.
The passage cuts off but the argument is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الكلام على منكر نسخ شريعة موسى عليه السلام من جهة السمع دون العقل. يقال لمن زعم ذلك منهم: ما الخبر الموجب لمنع نسخ شريعة موسى عليه السلام؟ فإن قالوا: هو عمن شاهد موسى عليه السلام منهم أنه قال: هذه الشريعة مؤبدة عليكم لازمة لكم ما بلغت السماوات لا نسخ لها ولا تبديل هذا من اللفظ وأنه أمر بتكذيب كل من دعا إلى نسخ شريعته وتبديلها فوجب منع النسخ بما ذكرناه من الخبر؛ فيقال لهم: ما أنكرتم أن يكون هذا القول الذي نقلتموه عن موسى عليه السلام صحيحاً؟ ولكن لم زعمتم أن مراده به نفي النسخ على كل حال ولزوم العمل بشريعته وإن ظهرت الأعلام على يد من يدعو إلى نسخها وتبديلها؟ وما أنكرتم أن يكون إنما أراد بقوله إن شريعته لازمة لكم ما دامت السماوات والأرض ما لم تظهر المعجزات على يد داع يدعو إلى خلافها وتبديلها؟ لأنه قد قيد في العقل وجوب تصديق من ظهرت الأعلام على يده والمصير إلى حكم قوله وسقوط العمل بما أخبر بنسخه وإزالته؛ كما أنه قد قيد في عقولنا وجوب سقوط فرض العمل بالشريعة مع الموت والعدم والعجز عندكم؛ فوجب أن يكون معنى قوله: «الشريعة لازمة لكم ما دامت السماوات والأرض» وما كنتم أحياء موجودين وما لم تموتوا أو تعدموا أو تعجزوا وإن لم يكن ذلك في سياق اللفظ لأجل أنه مقيد في العقل؟ وكذلك ما أنكرتم أن يكون المراد بقوله: «إنها مؤبدة لازمة لكم» ما لم يبعث الله نبياً تظهر الأعلام على يده يدعو إلى نسخها وتبديلها؟ فإن قالوا: لولا أن اليهود قد نقلت وهي اليوم أهل تواتر عن مثلهم عمن شاهد عليه السلام أنه أكد هذا النفي للنسخ وقرنه بما يدل على أنه أراد عموم الأزمان على جميع الأحوال إلى أن يرث الله الأرض ومن عليها وأزال بما كان من توقيفه على ذلك وتأكيده وظهور الأسباب التي اضطروا عندها إلى أنه أراد أن الله تعالى لا يبعث أبداً نبياً بنسخها لأجزنا من التأويل ما قلتموه وسألتم عنه. ولكن الضرورة التي نقلتها إلينا أهل الحجة أمنت مما
Chapter: Discourse on the one who denies the abrogation of the law of Moses, peace be upon him, from the perspective of transmitted evidence, not reason. It is said to the one who claims that from them: What is the report that necessitates the prohibition of abrogation of the law of Moses, peace be upon him? If they say: It is from those who witnessed Moses, peace be upon him, from among them that he said: This law is perpetual upon you, binding upon you as long as the heavens endure, no abrogation for it and no alteration. This is from the wording, and that he commanded the denial of everyone who called to the abrogation of his law and its alteration, so the prohibition of abrogation is necessitated by the report we mentioned. Then it is said to them: What prevents you from acknowledging that this statement which you transmitted from Moses, peace be upon him, is authentic? But why did you claim that his intention by it is the negation of abrogation in every case and the obligation of acting by his law even if signs appear at the hand of one who calls to its abrogation and alteration? And what prevents you from acknowledging that he only meant by his statement that his law is binding upon you as long as the heavens and earth endure, as long as miracles do not appear at the hand of a caller who calls to its opposition and alteration? Because the intellect has conditioned the obligation of believing the one at whose hand signs appear and resorting to the judgment of his statement and the fall of acting by what he reports as abrogated and removed; just as it has conditioned in our intellects the obligation of the fall of the duty of acting by the law with death, non-existence, and incapacity according to you. So it is necessary that the meaning of his statement: 'The law is binding upon you as long as the heavens and earth endure' [implies] as long as you are alive and existing and as long as you do not die or become non-existent or become incapable, even if that is not in the wording of the statement, because it is conditioned in the intellect. Likewise, what prevents you from acknowledging that the meaning of his statement: 'It is perpetual and binding upon you' [is] as long as God does not send a prophet at whose hand signs appear calling to its abrogation and alteration? If they say: Were it not that the Jews have transmitted – and they are today a people of tawatur (mutawatir transmission) from the likes of them from those who witnessed him, peace be upon him – that he emphasized this negation of abrogation and coupled it with what indicates that he intended the generality of times in all circumstances until God inherits the earth and whoever is on it, and removed, by what was from his affirmation and emphasis and the appearance of the reasons by which they were compelled, that he intended that God, exalted, will never send a prophet for its abrogation, we would have permitted from interpretation what you said and asked about. But the necessity that the people of evidence transmitted to us made us safe from what...
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer argument concerning the denial of abrogation of the law of Moses based on transmitted evidence (sam') rather than reason. The structure is dialectical: the opponent's claim is presented, then refuted by the author, Imam Baqillani. The opponent argues that a mutawatir report from Moses states that his law is perpetual and cannot be abrogated. Baqillani responds by pointing out that this report must be interpreted in light of rational principles. He asks: What prevents you from acknowledging that the report is authentic but that Moses only meant his law is binding as long as no prophet comes with clear miracles to abrogate it? Reason dictates that when a prophet appears with signs, he must be believed and his command followed, even if it abrogates previous law. Just as the obligation of the law falls away with death, incapacity, etc., even if not stated explicitly, so too it falls away with the advent of a new prophet with miracles. Therefore, the reported statement is conditional upon the absence of such a prophet. The opponent then counters that the Jewish transmission emphasizes the negation of abrogation unconditionally and forever, and that this is so strongly attested that no alternative interpretation is permissible. Baqillani concludes that the necessity (al-darurah) of the transmitted evidence protects us from the interpretation they propose. The passage demonstrates the interplay between transmitted reports and rational principles in deriving rulings.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh)
شريعة (shari'a)
خبر (khabar)
تواتر (tawatur)
أعلام (a'lam)
عقل ('aql)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Mutawatir reports must be taken absolutely and cannot be qualified by rational conditions.
Correction: Baqillani shows that even mutawatir reports are interpreted in light of rational principles, such as the obligation to follow a prophet with miracles.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why must the reported statement of Moses be interpreted as conditional?
A) Because the report is not authentic.
B) Because reason obligates belief in a prophet with miracles, which implies abrogation is possible.
C) Because the Jews themselves admit the law is eternal.
D) Because the law was only for the Israelites.

Key Takeaway
Even the strongest transmitted evidence must be interpreted in light of rational principles, such as the necessity to believe a prophet who comes with clear miracles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever treated a religious text or teaching as beyond interpretation, even when clear evidence suggested it might be conditional? What would it take for you to reconsider a deeply held belief in light of new divine signs?
?
If the intellect can condition even the strongest transmitted report, how do you guard against the arrogance of assuming your understanding is absolute? Are you willing to submit to a truth that challenges your current framework, even if it feels like a threat?
?
Baqillani argues that we must follow a prophet with miracles, even if it overturns what we thought was permanent. In your own life, have you ignored 'signs'—whether intellectual, spiritual, or experiential—because they didn't fit your established beliefs? What is one step you can take today to become more open to the truth, wherever it leads?

The Perpetuity of the Torah is Conditional
Baqillani refutes the Jewish claim of Torah's eternal unchangeability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani argues that the Torah's perpetuity is conditional upon the absence of a miracle-working prophet, using rational principles and refuting the Jewish appeal to tawātur.

Core Idea
Eternal laws remain valid only until a miracle-working prophet abrogates them.

In this passage, Imam Baqillani challenges the Jewish claim that the Torah is eternally binding without exception. He argues that reason itself demands that when a prophet appears with clear miracles, the previous law is superseded. He then addresses the Jewish reliance on tawātur to claim that Moses forever negated abrogation, and demonstrates why that claim does not hold.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it. Then read the translation. Pay attention to the rhetorical questions and the structure of the argument.
Notice how Baqillani starts with a hypothetical question to the Jews.
2
Identify the rational principle
Find where Baqillani states that reason obligates accepting the abrogation of a law when a miracle-working prophet appears. Understand the analogy with death and incapacity.
This principle is central to his argument.
3
Examine the Jewish counter-claim
The Jews claim that their tawātur transmission proves Moses negated abrogation forever. Note how Baqillani refutes this by denying that Muslims have such necessary knowledge.
4
Reflect on the refutation of tawātur
Baqillani argues that if the Jewish claim were true, Muslims would also be compelled to accept it, but they are not. This lack of universal compulsion shows the claim is false.
Consider the implication for the reliability of tawātur.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما أنكرتم أن يكون إنما أراد بقوله إن شريعته لازمة لكم ما دامت السماوات والأرض ما لم تظهر المعجزات على يد داع يدعو إلى خلافها وتبديلها؟ لأنه قد قيّد في العقل وجوب تصديق من ظهرت الأعلام على يده والمصير إلى حكم قوله وسُقُوطُ العمل بما أخبر بنسخه وإزالته؛ كما أنه قد قيد في عقولنا وجوب سقوط فرض العمل بالشريعة مع الموت والعدم والعجز عندكم؛ فوجب أن يكون معنى قوله: «الشريعة لازمة لكم ما دامت السماوات والأرض» وما كنتم أحياء موجودين وما لم تموتوا أو تُعْدَمُوا أو تَعْجِزُوا وإن لم يكن ذلك في سياق اللفظ لأجل أنه مُقَيَّد في العقل؟. وكذلك ما أنكرتم أن يكون المراد بقوله : «إنها مؤبدة لازمة لكم» ما لم يبعث الله نبياً تظهر الأعلام على يده يدعو إلى نسخها وتبديلها؟ فإن قالوا : لولا أن اليهود قد نقلت وهي اليوم أهل تواتر عن مثلهم عمن شاهد عليه السلام أنه أكد هذا النَّفْي للنسخ وقرنه بما يدل على أنه أراد عموم الأزمان على جميع الأحوال إلى أن يَرِثُ اللَّهُ الأرْضَ ومن عليها وأزال بما كان مِنْ تَوْقِيفه على ذلك وتأكيده وظهور الأسباب التي اضطروا عندها إلى أنه أراد أن الله تعالى لا يبعث أبداً نبياً بنسخها لأجزنا من التأويل ما قلتموه وسألتم عنه • ولكن الضرورة التي نقلتها إلينا أهل الحجة أمنت مما ذكرتموه، فوجب حَمْلُ الخبر على العموم يقال لهم : هذه الدعوى كذب لأنه لو كان الذي أخبركم عن هذه الضرورة الواقعة بقصد الموسى عن سَلَفِكم أهل تواتر وكذلك من قبلهم إلى القوم الذين شاهدوا موسى وهم أهل تواتر قد اضْطُرُّوا إلى ما أَخْبَرُوا عنه لوجبت لنا الضرورة بأن صلى الله عليه وسلم قد وقف على ذلك وأراده وثَبَتَ أنه من دينه لأننا قد سمعنا الخبر كما سمعتم وعرفناه كما عرفتم فلو كان التوقيف والتأكيد ما وصفتم وقد نقله أهل الحجة لعلمنا ذلك ضَرُورَةً كما علمنا وجود موسى عليه السلام ضرورةً لما نقل وُجُودَه ومشاهدته قوم هم حُجَّة إلى مِثْلِهم إلى من سمعناه وكذلك سبيل وجوب العلم بكل أمر تواتر الخبر عنه واستوى فيه طَرَفا الخبر ووَسَطُه وفي رجوعنا إلى أنفسنا ووجودنـا إياها غير عالمة بذلك في جملة ولا في تفصيل فضلا عن أن تكون مضطرة دليل على كذبهم في هذه الدعوى. فإن قالوا : لو لم تكن هذه الضَّرُورَةُ صَحِيحة ثابتة لكانت اليهود اليوم كاذبةً في قولهم إنهم مضطرون إلى العلم بصحة هذه الضرورة التي أخبرهم بحصولها سَلَفُهم وكذلك أيضاً سلفهم قد كذبوا وسَلَفُ سَلَفِهم في دعواهم العلم بهذه الضرورة وكذبوا في نقلها وفي الإخبار عنها ولو جاز ذلك عليهم لجاز أن يكون كل ما نقلوه كذباً ولجاز مثل ذلك على سائر الأمم وعلى نَقَلَةِ البُلْدان والأمصار وهذا يُبْطِلُ التواتر رأساً.
And what prevents you from [acknowledging] that He only meant by His statement that His law is binding upon you as long as the heavens and the earth endure, unless miracles appear at the hand of a caller who calls to its abrogation and alteration? Because reason has established the obligation to believe one at whose hand signs appear, and to submit to his judgment, and the falling away of acting upon what he reports as abrogated and removed; just as reason has established for us the necessity of abandoning the obligation to act upon the law upon death, non-existence, and incapacity according to you. So it must be that the meaning of His statement: "The law is binding upon you as long as the heavens and the earth endure" is while you are alive and existing, and unless you die or cease to exist or become incapacitated, even if that is not in the wording, because it is restricted in reason. Similarly, what prevents you from [acknowledging] that what is meant by His statement: "It is eternal and binding upon you" is as long as God does not send a prophet at whose hand signs appear who calls to its abrogation and alteration? For if they say: Were it not that the Jews have transmitted, and they today are a people of tawātur (contiguous transmission) from the like of them from those who witnessed him (peace be upon him) that he emphasized this negation of abrogation and coupled it with what indicates that he intended universality of times in all states until God inherits the earth and whoever is upon it, and removed [any possibility] by his specification of that and his emphasis and the appearance of the reasons due to which they were compelled to [know] that he intended that God, exalted, will never send a prophet to abrogate it, we would have permitted from interpretation what you said and asked about. But the necessary knowledge (al-ḍarūra) which the reliable transmitters (ahl al-ḥujja) have transmitted to us safeguards against what you have mentioned. So the report must be interpreted generally. It is said to them: This claim is false. Because if the one who informed you about this necessary knowledge that occurred regarding the intent of Moses from your predecessors were a people of tawātur, and likewise those before them up to the people who witnessed Moses, and they are a people of tawātur, and they were compelled to what they reported, then the necessary knowledge would be obligatory for us that [Muhammad] (peace be upon him) was aware of that and intended it, and it would be established that it is part of his religion. For we have heard the report as you have heard it and we have known it as you have known it. So if the specification and emphasis were as you described and the reliable transmitters had transmitted it, we would have known that necessarily (ḍarūratan) just as we know the existence of Moses (peace be upon him) necessarily by what his existence and his witnessing was transmitted by a people who are a proof (ḥujja) to the like of them, to those who heard it. And likewise is the way of necessary knowledge of every matter about which the report has been transmitted by tawātur, and its two ends and its middle are equal. And our returning to ourselves and finding ourselves not knowing that in general nor in detail, let alone being compelled [to know it], is evidence of their falsehood in this claim. For if they say: If this necessary knowledge were not true and established, then the Jews today would be lying in their saying that they are compelled to the knowledge of the correctness of this necessary knowledge which their predecessors informed them of its occurrence. And likewise their predecessors would have lied, and the predecessors of their predecessors, in their claim of knowledge of this necessary knowledge, and they would have lied in its transmission and in reporting it. And if that were permissible for them, then it would be permissible that everything they transmitted is a lie, and the like of that would be permissible for other nations and for the transmitters of cities and regions, and this abolishes tawātur completely.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a refutation-and-answer argument in response to the Jewish claim that the Torah is eternally unchangeable. Baqillani first presents a hypothetical objection: why can't the verse about the Torah's perpetuity be understood as conditional upon no miracle-working prophet appearing to abrogate it? He argues that reason dictates that when a miracle-working prophet appears, the previous law is abrogated, just as reason dictates that the obligation to follow a law ends with death. Therefore, the perpetuity clause is implicitly conditioned on life and the absence of a counter-miracle. He then addresses the Jewish counter-argument that their transmitted tradition (tawātur) confirms that Moses explicitly negated abrogation forever. Baqillani responds by denying the validity of this claimed necessary knowledge (ḍarūra). If the Jewish chain of transmission were truly compelling, Muslims would also be compelled to accept it, but they are not. He points out that Muslims too have heard the reports and find themselves not compelled. This lack of compelling proof is evidence that the Jewish claim of necessary knowledge is false. Furthermore, he refutes the idea that if the Jews were lying about this necessary knowledge, the entire system of tawātur would collapse; instead, he argues that the impossibility of such a universal lie is precisely what preserves tawātur, but in this case the alleged necessary knowledge is not universally compelling, so their claim is baseless.

Key Terms
تواتر (tawātur)
ضرورة (ḍarūra)
نسخ (naskh)
معجزة (mu'jiza)
أعلام (a'lām)
أهل الحجة (ahl al-ḥujja)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Torah is eternally binding without any condition or possibility of abrogation.
Correction: Reason dictates that when a miracle-working prophet appears, the previous law is abrogated; thus, the Torah's perpetuity is conditional on the absence of such a prophet.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what condition does reason impose on the perpetuity of a religious law like the Torah?
A) The law is eternal regardless of circumstances.
B) The law remains valid only until the death of its followers.
C) The law is valid as long as no miracle-working prophet appears to abrogate it.
D) The law is abrogated only when God explicitly states its repeal.

Key Takeaway
The perpetuity of a law is always conditional; reason dictates that miracle-working prophets can abrogate previous laws.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If a miracle-working prophet appeared today and commanded you to abandon a practice you hold dear because it is from an earlier revelation, would your heart submit or cling to the old? What does that reveal about your attachment to God's command versus your own comfort?
?
The Jews claimed certainty from their tradition, but Muslims did not find it compelling. Think of a belief you hold that you think all rational people should accept. Have you ever considered that someone else might not be compelled by it—not out of stubbornness, but because the proof is not as airtight as you assume? How would you test whether your certainty is from God or just from your upbringing?
?
When you read Baqillani's argument that the Torah's perpetuity is conditioned on the absence of a miracle-working prophet, you see that reason itself demands willingness to change. Ask yourself: Are you prepared to have your most entrenched religious views upended by a clear sign from God? If not, what is holding you back—love of custom or love of truth?
